Bava Batra 127 – Questions About Firstborn
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhGTRxlm_tEDtP-XRWv8qNdGlBATMq0Olh045Hq06XR-ItUIAoyctKjxv8ygJWTf-S0ixxVEuoC6WuNw8VhLATNypdWd-XE_ZPSad1DTmdi2NA4cICArxTy8TiYd29YaTVTZmiQR0K3dfY/s1600-h/L%C3%A9on+Augustin+Lhermitte+Woman+with+Child+and+Two+Children.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhGTRxlm_tEDtP-XRWv8qNdGlBATMq0Olh045Hq06XR-ItUIAoyctKjxv8ygJWTf-S0ixxVEuoC6WuNw8VhLATNypdWd-XE_ZPSad1DTmdi2NA4cICArxTy8TiYd29YaTVTZmiQR0K3dfY/s320/L%C3%A9on+Augustin+Lhermitte+Woman+with+Child+and+Two+Children.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A man is believed to say about his son that he is a firstborn, even if it was presumed to be otherwise. The phrase "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/21-17.htm">he must recognize the firstborn</a>" is superfluous, and it is interpreted to mean that the father can identify the firstborn to others, that is, help them recognize the firstborn.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"> <br />If two sons were born in hiding, and it is not clear who the firstborn is, they can appoint each other as agents against other brothers and together win the portion of the firstborn – so was Rava's advice. They told Rava that even though it sounded logical, the Torah insisted on definite knowledge about a firstborn. Rabbi Yannai explained this to be valid only when the firstborn was known and then mixed up. The next day, Rava publicly announced: "The statement that I made previously was an error on my part."<br />
<br />
Art: Léon Augustin Lhermitte Woman with Child and Two Children<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/128.txt
<a id="src-00140"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/128.txt`

Bava Batra 128 – Decisions of Rabbi Abba
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh7_U4TfqgzcsuMjEHo5uez3gdC8RoMSlGgzkQg10rNyZeSydpl1VBzbQxJXPpla7mTE2_2JHwMsyylfOxBTBZUUS_YKk0ml-1t9nfGm5-9Ebyik7lyxv1EjNircU2uro-6Sjm00sgpU7g/s1600-h/Gabriel+METSU+-+The+Hunter%27s+Gift.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh7_U4TfqgzcsuMjEHo5uez3gdC8RoMSlGgzkQg10rNyZeSydpl1VBzbQxJXPpla7mTE2_2JHwMsyylfOxBTBZUUS_YKk0ml-1t9nfGm5-9Ebyik7lyxv1EjNircU2uro-6Sjm00sgpU7g/s320/Gabriel+METSU+-+The+Hunter%27s+Gift.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Abba sent several rulings to Rav Yosef. The last of them deals with inheritance.<br />
<br />
* If a defendant made an extralegal offer, like "Swear that this is your slave and take him," - he cannot retract.<br />
* A third-generation cousin can testify regarding a second-generation cousin.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">* One who knew a testimony about a land boundary but became blind cannot testify about it anymore.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"> * If one says, "My wife shall take a share in my estate like one of my sons," - it is as he says. The husband certainly can give her a gift. However, she only takes a share in his current properties, not in any subsequent acquisitions.<br />
<br />
Art: Gabriel METSU - The Hunter's Gift<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/129.txt
<a id="src-00141"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/129.txt`

Bava Batra 129 – Being Precise with “Give” vs “Bequeath”
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhh0UlbmL_lx0Vls3RjrlDu6DD3J8M5Suz-n36wTYLXx7l3UxVClh-__ZFJofDLaEWdSKWY6ntm0P9GFsMVKrpAsWYUPWnR8mHaEQ5UM7STGCSF2NL8HhTPbX5Xm9LNegs6IcdL6pvwdZ8/s1600-h/Sir+Lawrence+Alma-Tadema+-+A+Family+Group.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhh0UlbmL_lx0Vls3RjrlDu6DD3J8M5Suz-n36wTYLXx7l3UxVClh-__ZFJofDLaEWdSKWY6ntm0P9GFsMVKrpAsWYUPWnR8mHaEQ5UM7STGCSF2NL8HhTPbX5Xm9LNegs6IcdL6pvwdZ8/s320/Sir+Lawrence+Alma-Tadema+-+A+Family+Group.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: 12pt;">If a person awards his property to several people in turn by saying, "My properties shall be given to you upon my death, and after you die, so-and-so shall inherit it, and after he dies, so-and-so shall inherit it," the law is as follows:<br />
<br />
When the first beneficiary dies, the second beneficiary acquires the property. When the second beneficiary dies, the third beneficiary acquires the property. If the second beneficiary dies during the lifetime of the first one, the property reverts to the heirs of the first beneficiary upon his death.<br />
<br />
Even though the award was referred to as "inheritance,"  it was only valid because he "gave" to the first one. Thus, when the second beneficiary died, he could not "give" anything to the third one, and the regular order of inheritance was restored.<br />
<br />
Art: Sir Lawrence Alma-Tadema - A Family Group<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/13.txt
<a id="src-00142"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/13.txt`

Bava Batra 13 – Problems in Property Division (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjnyEJYJF1rtNdsfrMsedSY5DO5pR5rpmMWpzlly_7sAj72EOMN7fIAS9eWlTdCHpZ_JoPr1tv2pXDEt9YjCWmc3eXLccX-7QTPgHVbY8ghlvt8b099nX2WsSZVzywDrS6KWjY5zUIAeeF3/s1600-h/Jean-Pierre-Francois+Lamoriniere+-+By+The+Canal.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5377259479269395250" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjnyEJYJF1rtNdsfrMsedSY5DO5pR5rpmMWpzlly_7sAj72EOMN7fIAS9eWlTdCHpZ_JoPr1tv2pXDEt9YjCWmc3eXLccX-7QTPgHVbY8ghlvt8b099nX2WsSZVzywDrS6KWjY5zUIAeeF3/s320/Jean-Pierre-Francois+Lamoriniere+-+By+The+Canal.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 223px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">When brothers inherit fields of differing quality, they receive a portion in each </span><span style="font-size: 130%;">field for an equitable division. If they </span><span style="font-size: 130%;">later want to exchange the portion, they are treated as buyers from each other.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: 130%;"><br />How does one divide a field bordered by a river on one </span><span style="font-size: 130%;">side and a canal on the other? It is divided into eight sections; each brother takes every other section.<br /><br />All the properties that are not large enough to be divided, what can one partner do if he still wants to separate? One sets the price, and the other is given the option of buying his partner's share or selling his share at this price.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: By The Canal by Jean-Pierre-Francois Lamoriniere</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/130.txt
<a id="src-00143"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/130.txt`

Bava Batra 130 – Power to Change Allocations in the Inheritance
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLgAn3OxQKLra-Wi-Av2rPxuk-BsohNRTAeN6UORARY3xSn-0xW80CCRwkwiiQz3-m8f3MyNWxjAe0N7gT9M7p3u6evC6Qid0oQV7TvBF8a3-Gssl_iLD5wF5tV6UIXB_hqNgRVqRL_iE/s1600-h/Carl+Larsson+-+Mother+And+Daughter.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLgAn3OxQKLra-Wi-Av2rPxuk-BsohNRTAeN6UORARY3xSn-0xW80CCRwkwiiQz3-m8f3MyNWxjAe0N7gT9M7p3u6evC6Qid0oQV7TvBF8a3-Gssl_iLD5wF5tV6UIXB_hqNgRVqRL_iE/s320/Carl+Larsson+-+Mother+And+Daughter.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one says, "Let so-and-so inherit me," where there is a daughter who will survive him, or if he says, "Let my daughter inherit me," where there is a son who will survive him – he has said nothing, that is, his words are not effective, since he made a stipulation contrary to what is written in the Torah.<br />
<br />
However, if he increased the portion of one son among the other sons, or one daughter among the other daughters, or completely eliminated the portion of one son, leaving everything for the other sons, his words stand. Thus, one can change the portion of those in the same inheritance order. This ruling contradicts <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/12/bava-batra-126-changing-portions-in.html">the one cited earlier</a>; indeed, it is the opinion of Rabbi Yochanan ben Berokah and is the one accepted in practice.<br />
<br />
Art: Carl Larsson - Mother And Daughter<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/131.txt
<a id="src-00144"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/131.txt`

Bava Batra 131 – Is Theory or Practice More Important?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiOiIvKFjlQzI0qOR0TraUC4p8p98x8f8MU1AR7E-V0qNagPz_Xy7AYmbQiOx-jsGn_2BwWui88xOpTevrJ-NvUkgQnIvmWuQhlX_FYMVMzBh5o9mRveIeCHkAT89jy7a6QHNY9hcDTehg/s1600-h/Baron+Mikhail+Petrovich+Klodt+von+Jurgensburg+-+Beside+a+Sick+Woman.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiOiIvKFjlQzI0qOR0TraUC4p8p98x8f8MU1AR7E-V0qNagPz_Xy7AYmbQiOx-jsGn_2BwWui88xOpTevrJ-NvUkgQnIvmWuQhlX_FYMVMzBh5o9mRveIeCHkAT89jy7a6QHNY9hcDTehg/s320/Baron+Mikhail+Petrovich+Klodt+von+Jurgensburg+-+Beside+a+Sick+Woman.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Which is to be followed, a ruling issued by a Sage during learning or his practical ruling in court?<br />
<br />
Neither. While learning, the Sage may not have considered all aspects of the matter. On the other hand, a practical ruling may be misunderstood by the observer as to the reason behind it. Rather, the Sage has to declare that the law agrees with a particular view and that it is to be followed in practice.<br />
<br />
Is the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/12/bava-batra-130-power-to-change.html">ruling about changes in inheritance</a> true for someone on his deathbed, because of "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/21-16.htm">on the day when he makes his sons inherit</a>," or even for one who is young and healthy? Rebbi said (and some say ruled in an actual case) that it also works for a healthy person. The two reports disagree on whether "is theory or practice more important."<br />
<br />
Art: Baron Mikhail Petrovich Klodt von Jurgensburg - Beside a Sick Woman<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/132.txt
<a id="src-00145"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/132.txt`

Bava Batra 132 – Giving All Property to Administrator
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhn8LYCHfrVRs5X99GY8HSdlww9rw_vrr0NBhW_9VsVKT0_X_HEQssJoNqSDthdZIiPJ7CFRWNZekNseISsK__8WUZUxMiO3zrp51EZ7xmrrHw5DbiO27II-_on2QELE1oZBHtAvdCmFcw/s1600-h/Ary+Scheffer+-+Marie+Joseph+Marquise+de+La+Fayette,+on+his+Deathbed.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhn8LYCHfrVRs5X99GY8HSdlww9rw_vrr0NBhW_9VsVKT0_X_HEQssJoNqSDthdZIiPJ7CFRWNZekNseISsK__8WUZUxMiO3zrp51EZ7xmrrHw5DbiO27II-_on2QELE1oZBHtAvdCmFcw/s320/Ary+Scheffer+-+Marie+Joseph+Marquise+de+La+Fayette,+on+his+Deathbed.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one writes in his will that he is giving all his possessions to his wife, he has only made her an administrator over his estate; she does not actually acquire it.<br />
<br />
The Sages determined that a man would not strip his sons of their entire inheritance; therefore, it is assumed that he is merely appointing her as an administrator because he wants them to treat her more respectfully. The administration lasts only while the children are minors. The ruling applies only if he left over all his property to his wife, but if he left anything to his sons, the gift to his wife was genuine.<br />
<br />
Art: Ary Scheffer - Marie Joseph Marquise de La Fayette, on his Deathbed<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/133.txt
<a id="src-00146"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/133.txt`

Bava Batra 133 – Is It Appropriate to Disinherit One's Children?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhV4bShz0tTOW9m3s-d6JOPBKXcTyp5dxbj-Q5JdETe4vw6HTyS6Dm_iMvukcPKNZbM0vrPmQ9Mi65067rN3hzUoivSKOCyKa4Drf8sIZgW1y9aVuEdsuPrxOa5Vmp9YxkroPhWln6STM0/s1600-h/Francis+Wheatley+-+A+Family+Group.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhV4bShz0tTOW9m3s-d6JOPBKXcTyp5dxbj-Q5JdETe4vw6HTyS6Dm_iMvukcPKNZbM0vrPmQ9Mi65067rN3hzUoivSKOCyKa4Drf8sIZgW1y9aVuEdsuPrxOa5Vmp9YxkroPhWln6STM0/s320/Francis+Wheatley+-+A+Family+Group.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one writes over his estate to others and leaves his children without a legacy, what he has done is done; that is, his gift is valid, but the spirit of the Sages is not pleased with him. By disinheriting his children, he usurps the order of succession ordained by the Torah.<br />
<br />
Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel says: "If his children were not conducting themselves properly, he is remembered for good." Does Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel explain the ruling or argue against it? <br />
<br />
The sons of one man did not conduct themselves properly, and he left all his possessions to Yonathan ben Uziel, who, in turn, sold a third, donated another third to the Temple, and returned the rest to the sons of the donor. Shammai came after him with his stick, but Yonathan proved to Shammai that he had done right.<br />
<br />
Art: Francis Wheatley - A Family Group<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/134.txt
<a id="src-00147"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/134.txt`

Bava Batra 134 – Identifying Someone as Son or Brother
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTYiD_eEdl3U-cKjHMHFiENfevLFyE3pRglcrcdh3azxeqhOriOaX_WhQUS-geM3bIaGaQErJrXWhy8CwFSzQF9N-sLkQudHRoN2xMMJ88CYL3EIQj_rM1LHaKCDVjfbm0zzUqKERB9AY/s1600-h/Harold+Copping+-+Sam+Weller+and+his+Father,+1924.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTYiD_eEdl3U-cKjHMHFiENfevLFyE3pRglcrcdh3azxeqhOriOaX_WhQUS-geM3bIaGaQErJrXWhy8CwFSzQF9N-sLkQudHRoN2xMMJ88CYL3EIQj_rM1LHaKCDVjfbm0zzUqKERB9AY/s320/Harold+Copping+-+Sam+Weller+and+his+Father,+1924.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one says, "This is my son," he is believed. What is the practical consequence of this ruling? If it is to make him inherit, then this is obvious since the father could have given him a present. Rather, it is to make the man's wife free from the obligation of levirate marriage to his brothers.<br />
<br />
If one says, "This is my brother," - the other brothers don't have to believe him and share their inheritance with the newcomer. The one who recognized the brother, however, is obligated to share in the inheritance. If the newly known brother dies, his properties revert to the one who identified him but are not shared with other brothers. However, if the new brother inherits or acquires new properties, the other brothers inherit them. How could it be? Because they said, "We don't know."<br />
<br />
Art: Sam Weller and his Father by Harold Copping<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/135.txt
<a id="src-00148"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/135.txt`

Bava Batra 135 – A Will Written by a Seriously Ill Person is Invalid
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiy5iW_hsh7ErLzdnOqHZOcC5tmMX5qcOtW2bDJee8vpdk9WSWCtJoOHj0qsO0a8O8q8N_Oc2mp9LGDs7TlhwWvX5Pvxpu05Dp4iFIHD4fk_vlskif4Jc2ZeKdxkixrkxyupTjbucnIS6w/s1600-h/Edvard+Munch+-+The+Sick+Child.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiy5iW_hsh7ErLzdnOqHZOcC5tmMX5qcOtW2bDJee8vpdk9WSWCtJoOHj0qsO0a8O8q8N_Oc2mp9LGDs7TlhwWvX5Pvxpu05Dp4iFIHD4fk_vlskif4Jc2ZeKdxkixrkxyupTjbucnIS6w/s320/Edvard+Munch+-+The+Sick+Child.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a person dies and a sickbed will is found tied to his thigh so that there is no suspicion of forgery, the will still has no legal validity. <br />
<br />
Unless a formal acquisition act was made before the person's death, his property automatically passes to the rightful heirs defined by the Torah. The Sages, however, decreed that a seriously ill person can transfer his property to others by verbal declaration alone. They did it out of concern that a seriously ill person, fearing that his end was near, might deteriorate further if he were unable to arrange his affairs. Thus, his words take effect, and the gift takes effect upon his death.<br />
<br />
This person, who prepared a will, did not use the verbal declaration method above, and after his death, neither he nor his documents can effect acquisitions.<br />
<br />
Art: The Sick Child by Edvard Munch
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/136.txt
<a id="src-00149"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/136.txt`

Bava Batra 136 – A Will of a Healthy Person
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEipbY6DxBvlk1u5k9QAJYQkQjzwnbvvG9ewjGnoosLlrHqHoLvO0UwwdLwKx7FBK_IdZN0BgxHClC47Xn1vivcknXLtkvEKwcbWR7GHLyAl0htmSifZhlQkroTc4St5QA4s1PPjzv9ON08/s1600-h/Emile+Friant+-+Sorrow.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEipbY6DxBvlk1u5k9QAJYQkQjzwnbvvG9ewjGnoosLlrHqHoLvO0UwwdLwKx7FBK_IdZN0BgxHClC47Xn1vivcknXLtkvEKwcbWR7GHLyAl0htmSifZhlQkroTc4St5QA4s1PPjzv9ON08/s320/Emile+Friant+-+Sorrow.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">While a seriously ill person can transmit his last-will instructions orally, though not in writing, a healthy person lacks both of these options. However, one way to accomplish property transfer is to give over the title to the possessions now but the right to use them only after death.<br />
<br />
When one writes his properties over to his sons for use after death, he must indicate this by including the clause "from today and after death," - says Rabbi Yehudah. But Rabbi Yossi says that it is enough to write "after death," and the date on the document indicates that he means "from today."<br />
<br />
In such a case, the father cannot sell the properties completely because they are written over to his son, and the son cannot sell them because they are in the father's possession.<br />
<br />
Art: Sorrow by Emile Friant<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/137.txt
<a id="src-00150"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/137.txt`

Bava Batra 137 – Sale of Inheritance
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiRdDqIAUWZSRemqFQv1GGILNp1lo_YTd2QUe5BIQVWlQE21ax3O4qeIOJhgN-sRZxsLO3Vb6SLuPcfXUgl787TIRSs0guu-229OwxA7UHM1XGMRFg6s6AKv2EeGbu06PFL-Xi8o1c-L9s/s1600-h/Jacques-Louis+David+-+Death+of+Socrates.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiRdDqIAUWZSRemqFQv1GGILNp1lo_YTd2QUe5BIQVWlQE21ax3O4qeIOJhgN-sRZxsLO3Vb6SLuPcfXUgl787TIRSs0guu-229OwxA7UHM1XGMRFg6s6AKv2EeGbu06PFL-Xi8o1c-L9s/s320/Jacques-Louis+David+-+Death+of+Socrates.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a father writes his properties over to his son "from today and after I die," and the son sells them during his father's lifetime and then dies, then Rabbi Yochanan says that the buyer does not acquire those properties. Resh Lakish says that the buyer does acquire them. Rabbi Yochanan considers the ownership of the rights to the produce tantamount to ownership of the property itself. Therefore, the father, who uses the property and is the primary owner, prevents the sale. Resh Lakish disagrees with this premise.<br />
<br />
If one says, "My property shall go to you, and after you to so-and-so," then the first can sell it, and the second has no recourse. However, initially, the first one should not sell it. One who gives him advice to sell, since after the fact the second one has no recourse, is called a "smart bad person."</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
Art: Death of Socrates by Jacques-Louis David
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/138.txt
<a id="src-00151"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/138.txt`

Bava Batra 138 – Refusing a Gift
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhtaJGCBuA77X7AbKhVhxIl1tt3qPucYp-czKgxGI3DKbz7iNxliZa04F4G6qMXiIQmcPvJJMWU5E_FobE1P5F-l6nIcu5__hP-H5fLsC6VEFK3cc9g_bdot0jR6APFgQv2y6nsD8oOGBo/s1600-h/Giovanni+Battista+Tiepolo-+Neptune+Offering+Gifts+to+Venice+%28detail%29.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhtaJGCBuA77X7AbKhVhxIl1tt3qPucYp-czKgxGI3DKbz7iNxliZa04F4G6qMXiIQmcPvJJMWU5E_FobE1P5F-l6nIcu5__hP-H5fLsC6VEFK3cc9g_bdot0jR6APFgQv2y6nsD8oOGBo/s320/Giovanni+Battista+Tiepolo-+Neptune+Offering+Gifts+to+Venice+%28detail%29.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If someone writes over his properties to another, and the recipient protests that he does not want the gift, the protest is valid, and the gift reverts back to the donor. The recipient claim is not spurious and is based on "<a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/15-27.htm">one who hates gifts will live</a>." <br />
<br />
If the recipient was at first silent and later protested, his protest is invalid, and he remains in the possession of the gift.<br />
<br />
If the donor asked a third party to acquire the gift on behalf of the recipient, the acquisition act is valid since it is assumed that most people want gifts. If the recipient was at first silent and then protested, then some say that he acquired the gift, but some say that perhaps he saw no need to protest until the gift actually reached his hands, and thus, the situation is in doubt.<br />
<br />
Art: Neptune Offering Gifts to Venice (detail) by Giovanni Battista Tiepolo
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/139.txt
<a id="src-00152"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/139.txt`

Bava Batra 139 – The Daughters are Supported
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivuPurvo66U6DNMjgs25L23d7gYGLJyFk6z82rx7UHS00rO_z6jssWkhiOSoAf17pxyOFDXAhuH_jGTVVPZpGoH-FUPsmRcYJ0xJvHUdxU-UxFaJqa9dQ3me54LigewQkegweH79Ssrl0/s1600-h/John+Greenwood+-+John+Richard+Comyns+of+Hylands+Essex+with+his+daughters.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivuPurvo66U6DNMjgs25L23d7gYGLJyFk6z82rx7UHS00rO_z6jssWkhiOSoAf17pxyOFDXAhuH_jGTVVPZpGoH-FUPsmRcYJ0xJvHUdxU-UxFaJqa9dQ3me54LigewQkegweH79Ssrl0/s320/John+Greenwood+-+John+Richard+Comyns+of+Hylands+Essex+with+his+daughters.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one dies and leaves behind sons and unmarried daughters, when the estate's property is abundant, the sons inherit, and the daughters are supported (food, clothing, and wedding expenses). When the estate's property is meager, the daughters are supported, and the sons go begging at the door.<br />
<br />
According to Biblical law, a person survived by his sons and daughters is inherited only by his sons. The Sages, however, instituted that a man stipulate to his wife in her marriage contract (ketubah) that their daughters who survive him be entitled to support from his estate until they marry or reach full maturity.<br />
<br />
Admon says, "Because I am male, do I lose?" Rabban Gamliel prefers his opinion, but the final law follows the first authority—the daughters take priority.<br />
<br />
Art: John Richard Comyns of Hylands Essex With His Daughters by John Greenwood
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/14.txt
<a id="src-00153"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/14.txt`

Bava Batra 14 – Ideal Dimensions for a Torah Scroll (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg89AuCRqqwEiueAItFjCht3ctzzUgIrQRjLXgU-DnrYrL-oL1pLQje-eeZamNWmqMeFjgqHMGcXetUZyCkowyksEA0L58XprUpW5NsHa5pYuZbsn6Hw95ljtWcBFWK2lbaCWqpPIKbrHYP/s1600-h/Joos+van+Gent+-+Moses+with+The+Ten+Commandments.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5377633532835137234" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg89AuCRqqwEiueAItFjCht3ctzzUgIrQRjLXgU-DnrYrL-oL1pLQje-eeZamNWmqMeFjgqHMGcXetUZyCkowyksEA0L58XprUpW5NsHa5pYuZbsn6Hw95ljtWcBFWK2lbaCWqpPIKbrHYP/s320/Joos+van+Gent+-+Moses+with+The+Ten+Commandments.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 240px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">The Torah scroll should preferably be written on thick parchment, and its ideal proportions are such that its height and circumference are the same, and the height is six hand-breadths because that was the size of the Tablets on which the Ten Commandments were engraved.<br /><br />Rav Huna wrote seventy Torah scrolls in his lifetime, and only one turned out to be one whose height and circumference were the same.  Rav Acha wrote one Torah scroll on calfskin (which is thicker, and thus it is harder to make it ideal size), and it turned out to be a scroll whose height and circumference were the same. The Rabbis cast their eyes on him in disbelief, and he died.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Moses with The Ten Commandments by Joos van Gent</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/140.txt
<a id="src-00154"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/140.txt`

Bava Batra 140 – Doubtful Gender Takes the Lesser Portion in the Inheritance
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhj79CvZwceiNHh40JxUvvrc1VZ78uzS6rWM4ELfngKEd04DWZhN2lBNKrSdhRE9WTxUbJqeKkZ2eJB5g-q5DxbzJSpMl_z9sEuE0rFIJnOctUxfqds87WZXxG0aY-CFXh9DJSImOM_D_c/s1600-h/Michelangelo+Merisi+da+Caravaggio+-+Narcissus.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhj79CvZwceiNHh40JxUvvrc1VZ78uzS6rWM4ELfngKEd04DWZhN2lBNKrSdhRE9WTxUbJqeKkZ2eJB5g-q5DxbzJSpMl_z9sEuE0rFIJnOctUxfqds87WZXxG0aY-CFXh9DJSImOM_D_c/s320/Michelangelo+Merisi+da+Caravaggio+-+Narcissus.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the deceased left behind sons and daughters and a tumtum (a person of indeterminate gender, with genitals recessed and covered by flesh) – when the property is abundant, the males push the tumtum away to the females. Since it is unknown whether the tumtum is male or female,&nbsp; he cannot claim more than the lesser of the two portions. He thus receives support until maturity, like the daughters. When the property is meager, the females push him away to the males, and he receives nothing, like the other sons.</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Michelangelo Merisi da Caravaggio - Narcissus <br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/141.txt
<a id="src-00155"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/141.txt`

Bava Batra 141 – Gifts to Unborn Children
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhCoTO7NVfMkOvnNlvghMxh-VKuwUU8iQj4Oor7SAcFOgrU6WflVL25ntQ3ePghyphenhyphen-5x9SCkw3NH8SmjO77qK5K-CzBBIFbYqMuS3CD5wBrhH2RJpGXQ-nOespswA_deBjNjzDG5SOgySoI/s1600-h/Henri-Fran%C3%A7ois+Riesener+-+Mother+and+Her+Daughter.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhCoTO7NVfMkOvnNlvghMxh-VKuwUU8iQj4Oor7SAcFOgrU6WflVL25ntQ3ePghyphenhyphen-5x9SCkw3NH8SmjO77qK5K-CzBBIFbYqMuS3CD5wBrhH2RJpGXQ-nOespswA_deBjNjzDG5SOgySoI/s320/Henri-Fran%C3%A7ois+Riesener+-+Mother+and+Her+Daughter.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one whose wife is pregnant says, "If my wife gives birth to a boy, he takes a hundred zuz ($5,000), and if to a girl, she takes two hundred zuz – the infants acquire the money. If she gives birth to a tumtum (a person of indeterminate gender), he does not get anything, but if he is the only child – he inherits all.<br />
<br />
So the man prefers a daughter? But we learned that <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/12/bava-batra-116-man-who-leaves-not-son.html">one should leave a son</a>! Either he realizes that a daughter needs more, or he follows Rabbi Yehudah's opinion that a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/09/bava-batra-17-god-blessed-abraham-with.html">daughter is a blessing</a>.<br />
<br />
But how can an unborn child acquire a gift? This follows Rabbi Yossi's opinion that a fetus inherits<span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">&nbsp;and</span><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/12/bava-batra-130-power-to-change.html">&nbsp;Rabbi Yochanan ben Berokah's opinion that a will made to the one who inherits is valid</a>.</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Henri-François Riesener - Mother and Her Daughter <br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/142.txt
<a id="src-00156"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/142.txt`

Bava Batra 142 – Only Your Own Unborn Children Can Acquire
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZvX6VHQ4uINdi0jVcm4oShyphenhyphenwkDlfwvPztiwsG7MMXydAJbmDMK0n37yc0QWFbvxrqZb-m1FuAg5HRVIzdGJSgrstXWfqs5kY_cYrjHPAgCTZXy5hP6oPTSfbJ02ZpUmKKEJV88hMVoRw/s1600-h/+Henri+Rousseau+-+To+Celebrate+the+Baby.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZvX6VHQ4uINdi0jVcm4oShyphenhyphenwkDlfwvPztiwsG7MMXydAJbmDMK0n37yc0QWFbvxrqZb-m1FuAg5HRVIzdGJSgrstXWfqs5kY_cYrjHPAgCTZXy5hP6oPTSfbJ02ZpUmKKEJV88hMVoRw/s320/+Henri+Rousseau+-+To+Celebrate+the+Baby.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Said Rabbi Itzhak, in the name of Rabbi Yochanan, "If one grants possession to a fetus, the fetus does not acquire." And if you question this from <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra141.html">the Mishna which validated such an acquisition</a>, that Mishna was talking about one's own children. Since one feels especially close to them, his resolve to give is strong enough, but this is not so for someone else's children.<br />
<br />
But what about a contradicting rule that "A one-year-old baby inherits and bequeaths," from which we understand that a fetus does not inherit? That rule is talking about a different situation – an inheritance that passes to the baby from his mother and from him - to his paternal brothers. This type of inheritance cannot pass through an unborn child.<br />
<br />
Art: To Celebrate the Baby by Henri Rousseau</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/143.txt
<a id="src-00157"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/143.txt`

Bava Batra 143 – You and the Donkey
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhqn_zg_TO2T3Iar7e1XUZhfYRtYijVVN5cJe8eDtjY6tRts-r1jY7SRu4GorgiWFvx1Ar9eNXaQ2_XAM2XfdRMVaGU0MjhzqXn17vjwT_E-NZH6BBxS7Uv3NT1IttT47oNOXkOErh99sc/s1600-h/Luis+Mel%C3%A9ndez,+Still-Life+with+Figs.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhqn_zg_TO2T3Iar7e1XUZhfYRtYijVVN5cJe8eDtjY6tRts-r1jY7SRu4GorgiWFvx1Ar9eNXaQ2_XAM2XfdRMVaGU0MjhzqXn17vjwT_E-NZH6BBxS7Uv3NT1IttT47oNOXkOErh99sc/s320/Luis+Mel%C3%A9ndez,+Still-Life+with+Figs.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one says to the intended recipient, "Let you and the donkey acquire this gift," the recipient gets half (Rav Nachman), nothing (Rav Hamnuna), or all (Rav Sheshet).<br />
<br />
Rav Sheshet's proof: if one separates the tithe from a vegetable with a bitter interior, he must add to his tithe from a sweet section. The sweet part is "you," and the bitter part is "the donkey," and since the tithe took effect, we see that the recipient gets all.<br />
<br />
Talmud argues for Rav Sheshet: <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/11/kiddushin-50-betrothal-by-liar.html">A man betrothed five women jointly with one basket of figs</a>, and the Sages said that two sisters were not betrothed. This is the case of "you" - the three eligible women and "the donkey" - two sisters who are not eligible – and he got all he could get.<br />
<br />
But the law here follows Rav Nachman.<br />
<br />
Art: Still-Life with Figs by Luis Melendez</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/144.txt

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/144.txt`

Bava Batra 144 – Estate Division Must be Formalized
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh5nFjogLmX2_LyjSiFMWxwvr2arSI4vifA5x7yA0AXu_kuQaXghwn8jRO5mSt_owdly8Mn_mrQ2-Rjjh89Kaw0pd58Tz9anbGneWgQ4en9g4I2tIsg8loV7J6KKtrA42c31vC0T1iSrI0/s1600-h/Samuel+de+Wilde+-+Mr+Bannister+Junior+and+Mr+Parsons+as+Scout+and+Sheepface+in+The+Village+Lawyer.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh5nFjogLmX2_LyjSiFMWxwvr2arSI4vifA5x7yA0AXu_kuQaXghwn8jRO5mSt_owdly8Mn_mrQ2-Rjjh89Kaw0pd58Tz9anbGneWgQ4en9g4I2tIsg8loV7J6KKtrA42c31vC0T1iSrI0/s320/Samuel+de+Wilde+-+Mr+Bannister+Junior+and+Mr+Parsons+as+Scout+and+Sheepface+in+The+Village+Lawyer.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a man died and left adult and minor sons, and the adults improved the estate, their improvements go to the joint estate, since the estate was as yet undivided. However, if the adult sons said in court or some other public forum, "See what our father has left us," - that is, assess the total value and let us divide it, and "hereafter whatever improvements we make using the estate resources will be counted as done using our portion," the improvement accrues to them.<br />
<br />
Rav Safra's father died, leaving money to Rav Safra and his minor brothers. Rav Safra did business with this money and realized profit. The brothers summoned him for adjudication before Rava, but Rava said, "Rav Safra is a Sage and a scholar. He would not stop his studies to work for others, so it is assumed that he worked for himself."<br />
<br />
Art: Mr. Bannister Junior and Mr. Parsons as Scout and Sheepface in The Village Lawyer by Samuel de Wilde
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/145.txt

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/145.txt`

Bava Batra 145 – Groomsman's Gifts
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiO7O-XxTfKtpZOvq6J53vwYTtqj3guf-g2WG3ScSdJGMYLCs6DsRg59CQ-K17Y6IxG0Fo0Uc_mwX746T235oDL30UjaBloAdz2RgBQhMB3gvq4bnGUQYdM8SpwLW4HBHfGUdpVzmq6hL0/s1600-h/Harmen+HALS+-+Peasants+at+a+Wedding+Feast.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiO7O-XxTfKtpZOvq6J53vwYTtqj3guf-g2WG3ScSdJGMYLCs6DsRg59CQ-K17Y6IxG0Fo0Uc_mwX746T235oDL30UjaBloAdz2RgBQhMB3gvq4bnGUQYdM8SpwLW4HBHfGUdpVzmq6hL0/s320/Harmen+HALS+-+Peasants+at+a+Wedding+Feast.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In Talmudic times, it was customary for friends of a groom to act as his groomsmen, that is, to bring him gifts in celebration of his wedding and to join him for seven-day wedding feasts. It was understood that the groom would reciprocate when his groomsmen celebrated their own weddings.<br />
<br />
If some of the brothers performed as groomsmen during their father's lifetime – the father providing the necessary funds to do so - then when the original groom reciprocates with gifts of his own – they are returned to the common estate.<br />
<br />
Five things were said about a groomsman's gift: its reciprocation is enforceable in court, it is returned only at the time of marriage, it does not involve any question of interest, the seventh year does not cancel it, and the firstborn does not take a double portion of it.<br />
<br />
Art: Peasants at a Wedding Feast by Harmen HALS
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/146.txt

Bava Batra 146 – Is Talmud Study Hard?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhqd-jU72MVHz8jSee3CWOnKUUMVvzvmWRIQLvLVJxjOSzbbyPxeftSpHjF8wYWRsFsEOZpo-IPLtSdUblxx-qtrUnQMS09CiOHI3eNRWZMQZFdZ9m_9BXuEx6ObmlG15t0ck6gytDQeZs/s1600-h/Carl+Spitzweg+-+The+Poor+Poet.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhqd-jU72MVHz8jSee3CWOnKUUMVvzvmWRIQLvLVJxjOSzbbyPxeftSpHjF8wYWRsFsEOZpo-IPLtSdUblxx-qtrUnQMS09CiOHI3eNRWZMQZFdZ9m_9BXuEx6ObmlG15t0ck6gytDQeZs/s320/Carl+Spitzweg+-+The+Poor+Poet.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">"<a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/15-15.htm">All the days of a pauper are bad</a>" - this is the Talmudist because he arduously toils, trying to understand the differences between different rulings. "<a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/15-15.htm">But he of good heart has a continuous feast</a>" – this is the Mishnaist, who just learns the rulings themselves – so says Rabbi Zeira. But Rava says the opposite - since the Mishnaist experiences greater frustration, not being able to rule on practical questions of law.<br />
<br />
If a seriously ill person signed away all property to others but retained a little land for himself, his gift to others stands even if he should recover from his illness. Since he retained some land, he did not really expect to die, and his gift is a regular gift. However, if he gave away everything, this indicates that his gift was conditional upon him actually dying, and if he recovers, the gift does not stand.<br />
<br />
Art: The Poor Poet by Carl Spitzweg
</span>

---

Bava Batra 147 – Explaining the Intentions in a Will
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjA1gqs-bzep0znkKSd0GMv_n-wah3xfLfuJembUbMljB_t7liyRKrMN9sJWZuJ8CJSpYfatfhhLr69tHo1wSedbBq19YFEk0zVFo66dKMXScw2o-0ldXI-hPe8dvyoy9UXDutbFujytqY/s1600-h/%D0%98.%D0%95.%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BD+-+%D0%9D%D0%B5+%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%21+-+Repin+-+They+did+not+expect+him.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjA1gqs-bzep0znkKSd0GMv_n-wah3xfLfuJembUbMljB_t7liyRKrMN9sJWZuJ8CJSpYfatfhhLr69tHo1wSedbBq19YFEk0zVFo66dKMXScw2o-0ldXI-hPe8dvyoy9UXDutbFujytqY/s320/%D0%98.%D0%95.%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BD+-+%D0%9D%D0%B5+%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%21+-+Repin+-+They+did+not+expect+him.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/01/bava-batra-146-is-talmud-study-hard.html">The intentions of a seriously ill person are assessed and then followed</a>. This is Rabbi Shimon Ben Menasya's opinion, as seen below.<br />
<br />
One whose son had gone abroad and he heard that his son died, and who wrote over all his possessions to others – and then his son came back – his gift is nevertheless valid, the assessment of his mind being irrelevant. Rabbi Shimon ben Menasya says, "His gift is not valid, because if he would have known that his son was alive, who would not have made the gift."<br />
<br />
All agree that if he said "I was under impression that I had a son, but now I discovered that I don't have a son, and my possessions shall go to so-and-so" - and then it was discovered that his son is alive - that his gift is not valid.<br />
<br />
Art: They did not expect him by Repin (</span><span style="font-size: large;">И.Е.Репин - Не ждали!)</span>

---

Bava Batra 148 – Changing One's Will
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg8kguD3I3DQTxCdROlWdGRnAax_W1X22elz2JaI2xdVN2YclO6hLY3RJmvPWM9E0z9QW6qRDvy47nNLwEY_EqbcjXl2SZg6hEnu8_hm_nva_FcZtMEStI_5VMf-0hIEvqeGqFS3DH3Ot4/s1600-h/Jehan+Georges+Vibert+-+The+Sick+Doctor.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg8kguD3I3DQTxCdROlWdGRnAax_W1X22elz2JaI2xdVN2YclO6hLY3RJmvPWM9E0z9QW6qRDvy47nNLwEY_EqbcjXl2SZg6hEnu8_hm_nva_FcZtMEStI_5VMf-0hIEvqeGqFS3DH3Ot4/s320/Jehan+Georges+Vibert+-+The+Sick+Doctor.jpg" /></a>
</div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a seriously ill person announced that all of his possessions should go to a particular person but then changed his mind, saying that some possessions should go to someone else, what is the law? Has the ill person retracted his entire gift to the first person, or has he retracted only the part he explicitly willed to someone else?<br />
<br />If it counts as complete retraction, the first person receives nothing, whether the sick person dies or recovers, and the second person receives his share: if the sick person recovers, as a gift, and if he dies, as an inheritance.<br />
<br />
However, if it is a partial retraction, then if the sick person dies, the two receive their shares, but if he recovers, both receive nothing - as in <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/01/bava-batra-146-is-talmud-study-hard.html">the case of a sick person who leaves something over</a>. <br />
<br />
The law follows the first possibility.<br />
<br />
Art: The Sick Doctor by Jehan Georges Vibert</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/149.txt
<a id="src-00163"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/149.txt`

Bava Batra 149 – Actions of a Seriously Ill Person
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0qk9dPfCbWShAn05c1ZpVQ_9guaCraMPQ0B1yPZO5Jq9868Pr_skDPzWD2-vaQFPfVY8T03ctT4qb4yVCyYbB_SCsu1TUUb2gGMHRFsNp33R7F7UqwdO1g1UWGI0lLCwrnIFX4gDenFw/s1600-h/Pablo+Picasso+-+Poor+People+on+the+Seashore.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0qk9dPfCbWShAn05c1ZpVQ_9guaCraMPQ0B1yPZO5Jq9868Pr_skDPzWD2-vaQFPfVY8T03ctT4qb4yVCyYbB_SCsu1TUUb2gGMHRFsNp33R7F7UqwdO1g1UWGI0lLCwrnIFX4gDenFw/s320/Pablo+Picasso+-+Poor+People+on+the+Seashore.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a seriously ill person consecrates all his possessions to the Temple treasury and then recovers, does his bequest stand? Do we say that whenever the Temple Estate is involved, the person is likely to grant possession with complete resolve, and thus, the bequest stands? Or does he value his own interests more, and the gift is revocable if he recovers?<br />
<br />
If you say that the gift to the Temple stands if he recovers, what if he declares all his belongings ownerless? Both the rich and the poor can avail themselves of his possessions, so his act is somewhat meritorious - does it stand if he recovers?<br />
<br />
If you say that in the above case, the merit is not enough and he does not resolve to give completely, what if he distributes all only to the poor? Is there a complete resolve?<br />
<br />
All these questions remain unanswered.<br />
<br />
Art: Poor People on the Seashore by Pablo Picasso
</span>

---

Bava Batra 15 – Who Wrote the Books of Scripture? (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi4v1ssGNqVjoVVV1iAwA1n2LJ-gxCUE_a9Z1pFiv7Atcjfd2-i4CbNX7OQp1H6J0y3_LgGaYP9KtTfYi9WhDxabhUoEQ06j6LEpfVv4mY18ItHVk_fLrXrrQDwpySaKVqfSrJaIEfM4E0v/s1600-h/Joos+van+Craesbeeck+-+Young+Man+Writing.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5378215734018584050" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi4v1ssGNqVjoVVV1iAwA1n2LJ-gxCUE_a9Z1pFiv7Atcjfd2-i4CbNX7OQp1H6J0y3_LgGaYP9KtTfYi9WhDxabhUoEQ06j6LEpfVv4mY18ItHVk_fLrXrrQDwpySaKVqfSrJaIEfM4E0v/s320/Joos+van+Craesbeeck+-+Young+Man+Writing.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 254px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">Moses wrote his book (the Pentateuch) and the Book of Job; Joshua wrote his book and the last eight verses of the Pentateuch, which describe events that took place after Moses' death.&nbsp;</span><br />
<span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span>
<span style="font-size: 130%;">Samuel wrote his book, and the Book of Judges and Ruth. David wrote the Book of Psalms, where he included the work of ten other authors.</span><br />
<span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span>
<span style="font-size: 130%;">Hezekiah and his assistants wrote the books of Isaiah, Proverbs, Song of Songs, and Ecclesiastes; the Men of the Great Assembly – a group of 120 Sages active during the first years of the Second Temple – wrote the Books of Ezekiel, the Twelve Prophets, Daniel, and the Scroll of Esther.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Young Man Writing by Joos van Craesbeeck</span></div>

---

Bava Batra 150 – These Give Away All Their Possessions
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhE4RoRPj9BH94b40evO7yx7yBqVOZXXqgLydL6cKA_e3Pr3ui6TtO59bc4ovp-eMT3Ll-1tEV_4w7t9Cuipdmu3ZU2Kv9PaUeNIJ70Ir_0Ah669zZQy8h8g9yRCjJqpTvweHRAfQWHEyk/s1600-h/James+Jacques+Joseph+Tissot+-+A+Convalescent.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhE4RoRPj9BH94b40evO7yx7yBqVOZXXqgLydL6cKA_e3Pr3ui6TtO59bc4ovp-eMT3Ll-1tEV_4w7t9Cuipdmu3ZU2Kv9PaUeNIJ70Ir_0Ah669zZQy8h8g9yRCjJqpTvweHRAfQWHEyk/s320/James+Jacques+Joseph+Tissot+-+A+Convalescent.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">These categories of people are treated differently depending on whether they give away all or only some of their possessions.<br />
<br />
* A seriously ill person – his gift (in case he recovers) is valid only if he distributed all that he had;<br />
* A person's gift to his slave – the slave goes free, but only if he gets all of his master's possessions, for otherwise, the master may have kept the slave and with him the gift that he gave;<br />
* If a man gives everything to his wife, he has only appointed her an administrator over his estate;<br />* A woman who sequesters her possessions by giving them to a third party when she gets married to keep them out of her husband's reach – if she gives all, she can get them back. Otherwise, it is a regular gift.<br />
<br />
Art: A Convalescent by James Jacques Joseph Tissot</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/151.txt
<a id="src-00166"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/151.txt`

Bava Batra 151 – Will in Anticipation of Death
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg8a35A_tgCJlYeENDju5mhRP65JTNiR7PrdZzUzYXJdoYqpYkRnLpWS0XiVdZsDNT5xV3FuDjOPwT_-YeVHzRi20jD0-37TdBeaCqFA1WjDtfQq1FiZglxJu8XbFzkqOC1iH0Oy1gkUCM/s1600-h/Johannes+Vermeer+-+Girl+with+a+Red+Hat.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg8a35A_tgCJlYeENDju5mhRP65JTNiR7PrdZzUzYXJdoYqpYkRnLpWS0XiVdZsDNT5xV3FuDjOPwT_-YeVHzRi20jD0-37TdBeaCqFA1WjDtfQq1FiZglxJu8XbFzkqOC1iH0Oy1gkUCM/s320/Johannes+Vermeer+-+Girl+with+a+Red+Hat.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Dimi bar Yosef's sister had an orchard. Whenever her health worsened, she would transfer the orchard to him as a sickbed gift, and when she recovered, she would retract the gift.<br />
<br />
Once, she felt weak and sent a message to him, "Come, acquire the orchard from me," but Rav Dimi did not come. She sent a message: "Come, acquire it in any way you wish." Rav Dimi did go and asked her to give him only a portion and perform a formal act of acquisition, <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/01/bava-batra-146-is-talmud-study-hard.html">hoping to make the gift irreversible</a>. She did all that, then recovered and reneged on the gift, but Rav Dimi did not want to return it.<br />
<br />
She went to Rav Nachman, who ruled that since she said, "Woe, I am dying!" she made the gift only under the impression that she was dying and thus may still retract.<br />
<br />
Art: Girl with a Red Hat by Johannes Vermeer<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/152.txt
<a id="src-00167"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/152.txt`

Bava Batra 152 – Strengthening the Will
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiqmsfBPZOnL-xlWXPT064U0TDvTz_-twWnqu-nrJue1EHFQYg0_MId7llEaWRjcGicdUL5j0qonlsL_kkD-dCK6iv7lxDe_jN4vAVQS_lXZIaLpgloEuu93pxbvLC3hUjRNtM5noJco2I/s1600-h/Eastman+Johnson+-+The+Little+Convalescent.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiqmsfBPZOnL-xlWXPT064U0TDvTz_-twWnqu-nrJue1EHFQYg0_MId7llEaWRjcGicdUL5j0qonlsL_kkD-dCK6iv7lxDe_jN4vAVQS_lXZIaLpgloEuu93pxbvLC3hUjRNtM5noJco2I/s320/Eastman+Johnson+-+The+Little+Convalescent.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a seriously ill person drafted a sickbed will in which he distributed all his property, it takes effect after his death, and no further action is needed. What happens if he also performed a symbolic acquisition and wrote about it in his will?<br />
<br />
Rav says that he is “riding on two steeds,” giving his will both the power of a sickbed bequest and the gift of a healthy person. Shmuel, however, says that he may have intended the acquisition to take effect after his death, and gifts cannot be given after death.<br />
<br />
Here are the rules then:</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
* A formal acquisition done without explanation invalidates the will;<br />
* A formal acquisition, explained to reinforce the bequest, makes the recipient feel good but is retractable upon the ill person's recovery;<br />
* A written will, delivered to the recipient, together with a formal acquisition, makes it irrevocable.<br />
<br />
Art: The Little Convalescent by Eastman Johnson
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/153.txt
<a id="src-00168"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/153.txt`

Bava Batra 153 – Was He Sick When Writing a Will?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjW_58JctNYqNCooWoDrzyBYL3FmGPyvY9GtQMrQxCxNHEejQC0QG41ZknB8yT-i2ogCfp4W6sSIptdHyirLEXa2UWXJhh7Acv_qp12LcZqtmtUu50zU2IRIqeiwPOvJCbe8Enx9UUoh1Y/s1600-h/H.+Lessing+-+The+Sick+Bed.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjW_58JctNYqNCooWoDrzyBYL3FmGPyvY9GtQMrQxCxNHEejQC0QG41ZknB8yT-i2ogCfp4W6sSIptdHyirLEXa2UWXJhh7Acv_qp12LcZqtmtUu50zU2IRIqeiwPOvJCbe8Enx9UUoh1Y/s320/H.+Lessing+-+The+Sick+Bed.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A sickbed will ordinarily state that the donor wrote it "when he was sick and lying in bed," whereas the ordinary gift document generally specifies "while healthy." <br />
<br />
Someone wrote a gift document but did not record that he was seriously ill or healthy, and then a dispute arose about the validity of the gift. The donor said, "I was sick when I wrote the document, and I have since recovered; hence, my recovery nullifies the gift," but the recipients said, "You were healthy, and the gift is therefore valid."<br />
<br />
The giver must bring proof that he was seriously ill – these are the words of Rabbi Meir, but the Sages say that since recipients wish to collect from the giver, who is presently in possession of the property, they are the ones who must prove their claim.<br />
<br />
Art: The Sick Bed by H. Lessing<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/154.txt
<a id="src-00169"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/154.txt`

Bava Batra 154 – One Who Forbids Something Can Also Allow It
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEih8ZZPDIlrKEGjz4AIH0FdSPZRs0Fx26bqKMCCQ8PvtI3GTNw98XGhgoSbyVrzHg2v3Evwn4MfkcDuBKECFl9dsvhxEzdWnqTjaJATHjxZAGHTDMhbKU-4qzbbJjM0u9_uKpx6Q55_aSQ/s1600-h/Richard+Caton+Woodville+-+The+Sailors+Wedding.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEih8ZZPDIlrKEGjz4AIH0FdSPZRs0Fx26bqKMCCQ8PvtI3GTNw98XGhgoSbyVrzHg2v3Evwn4MfkcDuBKECFl9dsvhxEzdWnqTjaJATHjxZAGHTDMhbKU-4qzbbJjM0u9_uKpx6Q55_aSQ/s320/Richard+Caton+Woodville+-+The+Sailors+Wedding.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The rule "The mouth that forbids it is the mouth that allows it" can be illustrated as follows. In a case where a woman told the court that she was married but added that she divorced or that her husband died, her first statement makes it forbidden for her to marry other men, but the second one makes it allowed. If we believe the first statement, we should also believe the second one.<br />
<br />
<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/01/bava-batra-153-was-he-sick-when-writing.html"> When one says, "(1) I did bequest you this gift, (2) but I was sick then, and now that I recovered that gift is invalid</a>,<span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;"><a href="#" target="_blank">"</a>&nbsp;</span>we should follow the "mouth" rule and believe him. However, Rabbi Meir considers the gift document as valid without certification. If so, we know (1) from the document itself and do not believe the man on (2).<br />
<br />
Art: The Sailor's Wedding by Richard Caton Woodville</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/155.txt
<a id="src-00170"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/155.txt`

Bava Batra 155 – To Sell Inherited Land One Needs to be Grownup
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjz2uyp3rpGCOx3TNHOzL-Cce5y1SICv9RP0-Of8aLgURvb50x2JImsDqQ_80nszfPCiKIAZGibAdkImfI6VmzkLyAdxSx-7oqGR604_dYAtLGl9Xdq3SInH2xhbfZfUjIjSqAst0v3Z4U/s1600-h/Cornelis+Ketel+-+Double+Portrait+of+a+Brother+and+Sister.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjz2uyp3rpGCOx3TNHOzL-Cce5y1SICv9RP0-Of8aLgURvb50x2JImsDqQ_80nszfPCiKIAZGibAdkImfI6VmzkLyAdxSx-7oqGR604_dYAtLGl9Xdq3SInH2xhbfZfUjIjSqAst0v3Z4U/s320/Cornelis+Ketel+-+Double+Portrait+of+a+Brother+and+Sister.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Since young people do not know the value of land, they can be easily deceived by money offers. The Sages, therefore, instituted that one can not sell land inherited from a father until one is twenty. In addition, to make a sale, one needs to be physically mature. This usually happens at 12 for girls and 13 for boys, but may come later.<br />
<br />
One person in Bnei Brak sold land he inherited from his father and later died. The members of the father's family challenged the sale, saying that the seller had been a minor at the time of his death. Everyone admitted he was twenty, but the family claimed he did not have two pubic hairs.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Akiva told them, "Firstly, you are not permitted to defile him through an examination. Secondly, it won't help since signs of maturity change after death."<br />
<br />
Art: Double Portrait of a Brother and Sister by Cornelis Ketel
</span>

---

<a id="src-00171"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/156.txt`

Bava Batra 156 – Disagreement About the Laws of a Seriously Ill Person
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEinpmAOPjy7Cu69oN7TjF9Y6qkQCFvYGkGcAKqalHtM6PXhKfDJ6mVi4O805k-CzCzdAmOnHsOv0d7eE5ewXndcdy8kSPy22CrKdtaB2BQv96eAktmZBX4bphVkk1CgV23M7L6WPfCOOiQ/s1600-h/Richard+Parkes+Bonington+-+The+Use+of+Tears+-+The+Love-Sick+Maid.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEinpmAOPjy7Cu69oN7TjF9Y6qkQCFvYGkGcAKqalHtM6PXhKfDJ6mVi4O805k-CzCzdAmOnHsOv0d7eE5ewXndcdy8kSPy22CrKdtaB2BQv96eAktmZBX4bphVkk1CgV23M7L6WPfCOOiQ/s320/Richard+Parkes+Bonington+-+The+Use+of+Tears+-+The+Love-Sick+Maid.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Someone who is seriously ill has the same laws as a healthy person, and his sickbed will is invalid. Instead, he must gift his possessions in a regular way, that is, with money, a document, or an act of ownership for land, and with pulling to oneself for movables – this is the opinion of Rabbi Elazar. Rabbi Elazar disputes the principle discussed on the previous twenty pages that a seriously ill person can effect the transfer of his property.<br />
<br />Rabbi Eliezer says that if a seriously ill person gave his possessions away orally on Sabbath, his words are upheld since, on Sabbath, he may not write. Rabbi Eliezer is a third opinion. Rabbi Yehoshua says that if he can distribute his possessions orally on Sabbath, then all the more so he can do it on weekdays. Rabbi Yehoshua agrees with the previous twenty pages.<br />
<br />
Art: The Use of Tears - The Love-Sick Maid by Richard Parkes Bonington
</span>

---

Bava Batra 157 – Inheritance: Who Died First?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjhDhSM8ZLk-pwOJWDRH75CdYN2mTsOLxjkYZ12HxQqKpugaNBa-WEyghAu-Hpdf7wYzAPpMSrdTGbVqMPp1wUctQoLIOC_zyhWksbEeN2L6DQ7Wv7ZpTB0_DnO6nABeDdKnXOsOCsfzfE/s1600-h/Ilya+Efimovich+Efimovich+Repin+-+Cry+of+prophet+Jeremiah+on+the+Ruins+of+Jerusalem.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjhDhSM8ZLk-pwOJWDRH75CdYN2mTsOLxjkYZ12HxQqKpugaNBa-WEyghAu-Hpdf7wYzAPpMSrdTGbVqMPp1wUctQoLIOC_zyhWksbEeN2L6DQ7Wv7ZpTB0_DnO6nABeDdKnXOsOCsfzfE/s320/Ilya+Efimovich+Efimovich+Repin+-+Cry+of+prophet+Jeremiah+on+the+Ruins+of+Jerusalem.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Consider the following case. A house collapsed  on a son and his father, and it is not clear who died first. The son had nothing, but he had debts and the obligation to pay Ketubah to his wife.<br />
<br />
The son's creditors claim that perhaps his father died first. Then, the inheritance passed to the son before he died, and they could collect. The father's inheritors claim that perhaps the son died first. Thus, when the father died, they inherited his property directly, leaving nothing for the son's creditors. <br />
<br />
Beit Shammai&nbsp;<span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">says that the father's heirs and the son's creditors divide the money, but Beit Hillel says that the property remains in the possession of the father's heirs.&nbsp;<a href="#" target="_blank">We can understand Beit Hillel's reasoning</a></span>, but what is Beit Shammai's reasoning? They say that a loan document is considered as if it has already been collected, which bolsters the creditors' claim.<br />
<br />
Art: Cry of the prophet Jeremiah on the Ruins of Jerusalem by Ilya Efimovich Efimovich Repin
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/158.txt
<a id="src-00173"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/158.txt`

Bava Batra 158 – The House Collapsed On Mother and Son
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivNOBkmhfBGl-kLOAZutLMv2I0mpkBhsdl7YHDo5IWJ7xFE5aS5v9WWe8RyHq9rXZm2CTcJgay1cEspTODe4Tqq6H5CTMSfURWlBZSXGCdFRLsI2TeKvO6QmJ83-dafLCFaIwdkVQfywI/s1600-h/Van+Gogh+-+Backyards+of+Old+Houses+in+Antwerp+in+the+Snow.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivNOBkmhfBGl-kLOAZutLMv2I0mpkBhsdl7YHDo5IWJ7xFE5aS5v9WWe8RyHq9rXZm2CTcJgay1cEspTODe4Tqq6H5CTMSfURWlBZSXGCdFRLsI2TeKvO6QmJ83-dafLCFaIwdkVQfywI/s320/Van+Gogh+-+Backyards+of+Old+Houses+in+Antwerp+in+the+Snow.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Consider the case where a house collapsed on a son and his mother. Since it is not known who died first, the son's paternal brothers claim that perhaps the mother died first, the son inherited her, and they should inherit him. The mother's relatives (for example, her paternal brothers) claim that perhaps the son died first, so he never inherited anything, so they inherit the estate. <br />
<br />
Unlike in the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/01/bava-batra-157-inheritance-who-died.html">case of a father and son</a>, here the claims of both sides are equally based on "perhaps," and therefore, both Beit Shammai and Beit Hillel agree that they divide it.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Akiva says that Beit Hillel and Beit Shammai also argue in this case, but Ben Azzai said to Rabbi Akiva, "We are in enough pain over <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/01/bava-batra-157-inheritance-who-died.html">what they disagree</a>, and now you come to dispute a unanimous decision?"<br />
<br />
Art: Backyards of Old Houses in Antwerp in the Snow by Van Gogh
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/159.txt
<a id="src-00174"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/159.txt`

Bava Batra 159 – A Hard-to-Understand Ruling From Israel
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhp25QsVSA9cckHV_KpMp6_ETEjZ1ol8I1Apvg_8rEbZGZPQZHP5cbmYWSOsCNNNjbY_NnEeiMZneSZ7PvXS_DOTCLrA47TklGfijpSriep-urZeCgn_gNF0YFmfDNvIubfk-lZpqVFklI/s1600-h/Arthur+Boyd+Houghton+-+Grandfathers+Jack+in+the+Box.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhp25QsVSA9cckHV_KpMp6_ETEjZ1ol8I1Apvg_8rEbZGZPQZHP5cbmYWSOsCNNNjbY_NnEeiMZneSZ7PvXS_DOTCLrA47TklGfijpSriep-urZeCgn_gNF0YFmfDNvIubfk-lZpqVFklI/s320/Arthur+Boyd+Houghton+-+Grandfathers+Jack+in+the+Box.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">They sent a ruling from Israel: If a son borrowed against his father's property and subsequently died, his son can seize it from purchasers.<br />
<br />
Now, what is hard to understand here? The son stood to inherit his father.&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: medium;">He sold some properties that would be coming to him in the future. Later, he died and thus never inherited those properties. Now, his son (a grandson) can tell the buyers, "My father sold you property that he stood to inherit but never inherited, so the sale is void. I inherit it not from my father but directly from my grandfather." In this case, the rule that the grandson inherits directly from the grandfather is derived from the following: "<a href="http://bible.cc/psalms/45-16.htm">In place of your fathers shall be your sons</a>..."<br />
<br />
So what is difficult? That "<a href="http://bible.cc/psalms/45-16.htm">In place of your fathers</a>..." refers to blessings, not monetary laws.<br />
<br />
Art: Grandfather's Jack in the Box by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Arthur Boyd Houghton</span>

---

Bava Batra 16 – The Suffering of Job (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJ4lR7uCyAzlWEKlhgHlHLNOGOWaq7D3i8GwCmyosJii01mPzYzFMj6AqDVxo2S9vUTTqHrtGZiQYHFcedoRIyvbZMnV6sUIbCrcgvBhQo07RqIfIq0xyhl0IqBoRv9hiNxrUqPqSe57WZ/s1600-h/Repin+-+Job+and+His+Friends.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5378451214813169250" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgJ4lR7uCyAzlWEKlhgHlHLNOGOWaq7D3i8GwCmyosJii01mPzYzFMj6AqDVxo2S9vUTTqHrtGZiQYHFcedoRIyvbZMnV6sUIbCrcgvBhQo07RqIfIq0xyhl0IqBoRv9hiNxrUqPqSe57WZ/s320/Repin+-+Job+and+His+Friends.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 228px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">When Satan was allowed to inflict extreme pain on Job's body without allowing him to die, it was most difficult for him, similar to a servant told by his master, "Break a keg of wine but save the wine within it."<br /><br />The intentions of Satan were for the sake of Heaven. When Satan saw that the Holy One, Blessed be He, was partial to Job, he said to himself, "God forbid that He will forget the mercy He has for Abraham." Therefore, he set out to demonstrate Job's failings.<br /><br />Rav Acha bar Yakov taught this in Papunia, and Satan came and kissed his feet in appreciation.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Job and His Friends by Repin</span></div>

### content/bava_batra/160.txt
