Bava Batra 18 – Preventing Future Damage (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvga5VtjIp1Nz4AqIdlgeFfz0I8vOsMSYYlAvtQ7WqIlNoZaDrsGWzMC-dQbc6_SlMwvqX73_rP9-D8gXU7Fv1JsyssmhFTylmKDqsgTCGW606YhqWpeMi8ZiPjlmV1nxHRxs3qrFOGFns/s1600-h/Eastman+Johnson+-+Five+Boys+on+a+Wall.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvga5VtjIp1Nz4AqIdlgeFfz0I8vOsMSYYlAvtQ7WqIlNoZaDrsGWzMC-dQbc6_SlMwvqX73_rP9-D8gXU7Fv1JsyssmhFTylmKDqsgTCGW606YhqWpeMi8ZiPjlmV1nxHRxs3qrFOGFns/s320/Eastman+Johnson+-+Five+Boys+on+a+Wall.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">When one observes a certain distance between his potentially damaging objects and his neighbor's wall or pit, does he have to do it only when the wall or pit is already there, or is it true even before the wall is built or the pit is dug out? Abaye says, "Only when it's there." Rava says, "Even before it's there."</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">Question against Rava from a previous ruling: <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra17.html" target="_blank">Olive press refuse... must be distanced three hand-breadths from a neighbor's wall</a>, which implies that the wall must be there! Rava answers: "No, this is true even before the wall is there, and this ruling is still needed to teach us that these materials are harmful to a wall."
<br /><br />
Art: Five Boys on a Wall by Eastman Johnson</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/19.txt
<a id="src-00195"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/19.txt`

Bava Batra 19 – Urinating Against a Wall (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpTEAX5kiMD9m-qnA3cp11-VR0dWiCDWahFWCnCT-9X9IUMnOYHn12XZdyZV_LsOH8xlzmzGdiz2OpVW5y0vH_UMF_VFUfoVIHD5klaLvKIxGPaZ64-K7_HLKOdwgsl2rl4AcbYRYXX0Oy/s1600-h/Julian+Alden+Weir+-+At+the+Water+Trough.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpTEAX5kiMD9m-qnA3cp11-VR0dWiCDWahFWCnCT-9X9IUMnOYHn12XZdyZV_LsOH8xlzmzGdiz2OpVW5y0vH_UMF_VFUfoVIHD5klaLvKIxGPaZ64-K7_HLKOdwgsl2rl4AcbYRYXX0Oy/s320/Julian+Alden+Weir+-+At+the+Water+Trough.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;"></span><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbah bar bar Chanah said: "A person is permitted to urinate at the side of his fellow's wall." It is thus written, "<a href="http://bible.cc/1_kings/21-21.htm">in the house of Achav everyone who urinates against a wall</a>," meaning every male, which implies that this is a usual practice.<br />
<br />
But we have learned a rule that a person may not pour water or urine at the side of his fellow's wall closer than three hand-breadths from the wall! Answers Rabbah: pouring from a pot is not allowed, but urinating is. <br />
<br />
But another rule states that a person may not urinate next to his fellow's brick wall closer than 3 hand-breadths and 1 hand-breadth from a stone wall! Rabbah is disproved. But he quoted a verse! The verse is saying that Achav will not even have dogs.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: At the Water Trough by Julian Alden Weir</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/2.txt
<a id="src-00196"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/2.txt`

Bava Batra 2 – Privacy Rights in a Courtyard (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEikoFUhC9GC_Jj4rKrAwN7kSH9gdwjzQKbdaXW28lJ8jILv4JHAheoEZ-pCSRFccyld0pJmTRv-iUAonrbOtNtdjLobBVd9B2yx1op9KOim3RyqsNWoujg3hfvK9Gp4aVdETxM2lRxyD8Zk/s1600-h/Edward+Hopper+-+Night+Windows.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5373188058077275538" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEikoFUhC9GC_Jj4rKrAwN7kSH9gdwjzQKbdaXW28lJ8jILv4JHAheoEZ-pCSRFccyld0pJmTRv-iUAonrbOtNtdjLobBVd9B2yx1op9KOim3RyqsNWoujg3hfvK9Gp4aVdETxM2lRxyD8Zk/s320/Edward+Hopper+-+Night+Windows.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 272px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">Observing one's activities is considered a form of trespass on his domain. Thus, the Rabbi required that fences and walls be built between neighboring properties to prevent such violations. Private places, such as a person's home, where intimate acts are constantly performed, are clearly protected by the law of privacy. A courtyard, however, is considered a semi-private place.<br /><br />Partners who agreed to make a partition in a courtyard they own jointly must build a wall in the center of the courtyard, each providing half of the land upon which to build. This is true, however, only if they agreed to a partition. Since courtyards are semi-private, one cannot force the other  to do so since visual trespass in this situation is not actionable.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Night Winder by Edward Hopper</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/20.txt
<a id="src-00197"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/20.txt`

Bava Batra 20 – Damage Despite Precautions (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg8OB3ul_Ok-hSZZobITYXCl_ZTLSK6C_v_BA72A85IjeF0UjWytLPnErBuzrnykQAFSJZfSaOK56OKWwx35LupMDZFBAJ765xAomlmJSlyqUNYEwGmESoyhnuVPcu_FbXXHCmxpuA-hCfL/s1600-h/%C3%89douard+Manet,+The+Dead+Toreador,+1864.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg8OB3ul_Ok-hSZZobITYXCl_ZTLSK6C_v_BA72A85IjeF0UjWytLPnErBuzrnykQAFSJZfSaOK56OKWwx35LupMDZFBAJ765xAomlmJSlyqUNYEwGmESoyhnuVPcu_FbXXHCmxpuA-hCfL/s400/%C3%89douard+Manet,+The+Dead+Toreador,+1864.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">A wall can separate from a ritual impurity of a corpse lying on the other side, but if there is an opening more than a hand-breadth, the impurity goes through. If, however, some object is put into the opening, making it smaller, the wall again separates from impurity. These objects can be growing grass, small scraps of fabric, flesh dangling from an animal, a bird, an idolater, salt, or a Torah scroll. But <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra17.html" target="_blank">one is not allowed to plant grass near the wall</a>! - its root is far from the wall.<br />
<br />
One cannot set up an oven in a house unless there are 4 amot (6 feet) from it to the ceiling. If, after observing <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra17.html" target="_blank">all precautions listed</a>, he damages the property of another, he must pay for the damage. Rabbi Shimon says, "The Sages stated all the precautions with their measurements to make him exempt."</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Dead Toreador by Eduard Manet<br />
<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/21.txt
<a id="src-00198"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/21.txt`

Bava Batra 21 – Restrictions on Commercial Activities in a Courtyard (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiA_7pPfeCJCRvFCbOQUoyjR9UzQ0Dr4-3NxyiqYvt-76XwRtK0Jrjx-y9rPK9oNw8Dpv2h7w-yVC7pMc-oKTaS2Xfs26C5_o9I9JBdCdH0XePdDHK8TVlD5pXXldFWU3wjmhT3ud9OL58-/s1600-h/John+George+Brown+-+The+Village+Cobbler.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiA_7pPfeCJCRvFCbOQUoyjR9UzQ0Dr4-3NxyiqYvt-76XwRtK0Jrjx-y9rPK9oNw8Dpv2h7w-yVC7pMc-oKTaS2Xfs26C5_o9I9JBdCdH0XePdDHK8TVlD5pXXldFWU3wjmhT3ud9OL58-/s320/John+George+Brown+-+The+Village+Cobbler.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">If a courtyard resident has set up a store in the courtyard, one of the other residents can block him by claiming, "I cannot sleep due to the noise of your customers who go in and out of the courtyard.” <br />
<br />
But a courtyard resident may manufacture utensils in his home and go out and sell them in the marketplace, and one cannot block him by claiming, “I cannot sleep due to the noise of the hammer,” or “I cannot sleep due to the noise of the children.”<br />
<br />
Why can </span><span style="font-size: medium;">the children </span><span style="font-size: medium;">go in and out while the customers can't? These are schoolchildren coming to learn the Torah. This ruling was taught after Yehoshua ben Gamla, a high priest, mandated the installation of teachers in every town, and he is remembered for good for preserving Torah study.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Village Cobbler by John George Brown</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/22.txt
<a id="src-00199"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/22.txt`

Bava Batra 22 – Town Commerce Restrictions (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2ZKfdo4FaRUEwVgXCyfdBllB3xGsQWrvO7-eR9akyJq974HKQoNlofPizlOXXtkaIOL96bMJ64pzIQR_pF_xsAQfU3hJANGm1Kr2wvBPI3R-ahp0v_u0prRl08usH82wvDosXmHbzP9Tb/s1600-h/Thomas+Baines+-+The+%27Ma+Roberts%27+and+an+Elephant+in+the+Shallows,+Lower+Zambezi+1859.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2ZKfdo4FaRUEwVgXCyfdBllB3xGsQWrvO7-eR9akyJq974HKQoNlofPizlOXXtkaIOL96bMJ64pzIQR_pF_xsAQfU3hJANGm1Kr2wvBPI3R-ahp0v_u0prRl08usH82wvDosXmHbzP9Tb/s320/Thomas+Baines+-+The+'Ma+Roberts'+and+an+Elephant+in+the+Shallows,+Lower+Zambezi+1859.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">A tradesman who resides outside of a town where his type of business has already been established can be barred from plying his trade in that town.</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Dimi, a Sage, brought his figs to a town that wanted to give him exclusive trading rights. They sent Rav Adda bar Abba to test him. He asked, "If an elephant swallows a willow-reed basket and then ejects it through its rectum, is it susceptible to ritual impurity, or is it like manure? Rav Dimi didn't know, so Rav Adda patronized him. Rav Dimi's figs spoiled, and Rav Adda died. Every Sage involved took the blame for Rav Adda's death on himself – because they wanted to discharge their karmic debt.</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">One who builds a wall opposite the windows of his neighbor's house must ensure that the wall is either higher or lower than the windows so that he can't stand up on it or hang from it to look inside.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The 'Ma Roberts' and an Elephant in the Shallows, Lower Zambezi by Thomas Baines</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/23.txt
<a id="src-00200"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/23.txt`

Bava Batra 23 – Indirect Damages (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLrZMDlBxp-aS7dIJj6rhF7BfqHCvFespfjN_FXhd00BVbbgeYEt9ZXjCTn-8aPcaXjiuVXkbJrDoZdno2X7tiJImCK3x4BqKAB6VTAi6KCPRGIsb9rBFXuyX4T3s2YQXdB2GFr0tBtXdM/s1600-h/Frederick+Barnard+-+Barnaby+Rudge+and+the+Raven+Gri.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLrZMDlBxp-aS7dIJj6rhF7BfqHCvFespfjN_FXhd00BVbbgeYEt9ZXjCTn-8aPcaXjiuVXkbJrDoZdno2X7tiJImCK3x4BqKAB6VTAi6KCPRGIsb9rBFXuyX4T3s2YQXdB2GFr0tBtXdM/s320/Frederick+Barnard+-+Barnaby+Rudge+and+the+Raven+Gri.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">One who causes indirect damages is not liable to pay, but it is nevertheless forbidden, and one is accountable for them in the Heavenly court. He may lose the same amount or be reincarnated to pay this karmic debt. This is known from the following case.<br />
<br />
Rav Yosef had date palms, under which blood-letters used to let blood. The ravens would come and eat blood, then smear it on dates. Rav Yosef demanded that the blood letters go elsewhere. Abaye took up their defense:<br />
<br />
<b>A</b>. But this is only indirect damage!<br />
<b>Y</b>. Doing indirect damage is still forbidden.<br />
<b>A</b>. By being there for three years, they have established squatters' rights</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"> <b>Y</b>. There are no squatters' rights for damages.<br />
<b>A</b>. Only for offensive damages such as smoke or an outhouse.<br />
<b>Y</b>. I have a delicate nature, so for me, blood on dates is just as offensive.<br />
<br />Art: Barnaby Rudge and the Raven Gri by Frederick Barnard<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/24.txt
<a id="src-00201"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/24.txt`

Bava Batra 24 – Distance Regulations (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhBl5B5GY4k3k0eDo_xwVcm0wRDAY9z449ynaNDWTJjzLZKoEVWloMY_TcHktycZDsJYT15M2bJpl3dqalXrt-l6qVlV2m0BrdZILTSbCJWV2TAdQkK62gGb2p7y3Ve05MLkO_4Tm0YUWAx/s1600-h/Henry+Mosler+-+Peasant+Girl+and+Doves.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhBl5B5GY4k3k0eDo_xwVcm0wRDAY9z449ynaNDWTJjzLZKoEVWloMY_TcHktycZDsJYT15M2bJpl3dqalXrt-l6qVlV2m0BrdZILTSbCJWV2TAdQkK62gGb2p7y3Ve05MLkO_4Tm0YUWAx/s320/Henry+Mosler+-+Peasant+Girl+and+Doves.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">If a young dove was found within fifty amot (100 feet) of a dovecote, it belongs to the owner of the dovecote; if farther than fifty amot – it belongs to the one who found it. Rabbi Yirmiyah asked, "What if one of its legs is within fifty amot, but the other leg is outside of fifty?" - and for asking this question, the Sages ejected Rabbi Yirmiyah from the house of study.</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">One must distance a permanent granary fifty amot from a city, and a temporary granary must be far enough from his neighbor's saplings or his plowed field so that the chaff that flies from the granary will not cause any damage.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Peasant Girl and Doves by Henry Mosler</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/25.txt
<a id="src-00202"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/25.txt`

Bava Batra 25 – It is on the Damaged Party to Protect Itself (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjeBv4iUroefCnfLRiABeCYfZLJPuRCGaaxr7Mdw8QBeUE4Pqea5EGg24qGiZKlLr2mfpd1wYR1vWY2Z-2ETi3Kf6plpL4uLiPzHpL_MsUqk9yKnQ0X_keOeMUINsKJfLbn8wBgX6EWHKu7/s1600-h/William+Trost+Richards+-+Leverington+Cemetery.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjeBv4iUroefCnfLRiABeCYfZLJPuRCGaaxr7Mdw8QBeUE4Pqea5EGg24qGiZKlLr2mfpd1wYR1vWY2Z-2ETi3Kf6plpL4uLiPzHpL_MsUqk9yKnQ0X_keOeMUINsKJfLbn8wBgX6EWHKu7/s320/William+Trost+Richards+-+Leverington+Cemetery.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;"></span><span style="font-size: medium;">One must distance animal carcasses, graves, and a tannery fifty amot (100 feet) from a town to not disturb its residents with their foul order. <br />
<br />
One must distance a flax pool from vegetables and mustard seeds from his neighbor's bees. Water from soaking flax is toxic to the vegetables. Bees digest mustard, and it causes the honey to become pungent. Alternatively, it causes the bees to consume the honey.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yosi allows damaging agents to be put on one's property when the damage is indirect, like in the case of flax and mustard, putting on the damaged party the obligation to protect itself, and his view becomes law.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Leverington Cemetery by William Trost Richard</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/26.txt
<a id="src-00203"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/26.txt`

Bava Batra 26 – Tree Roots in the Neighbor's Field (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi3hclNmX-fMbf_H-gE6LM4ytobNsgE-UuJuNpZBiHGeodA1BgwIwCbCCu86vTI1k9LZH3WWoq-kD15voh5uomYtGmpvCrQtW8jyptXSRrEuqRMZWk5paQqtiwhjYSqGIp58YsBV8qUN5vE/s1600-h/Camille+Pissarro+-+Apple+Trees+at+Pontoise.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi3hclNmX-fMbf_H-gE6LM4ytobNsgE-UuJuNpZBiHGeodA1BgwIwCbCCu86vTI1k9LZH3WWoq-kD15voh5uomYtGmpvCrQtW8jyptXSRrEuqRMZWk5paQqtiwhjYSqGIp58YsBV8qUN5vE/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Apple+Trees+at+Pontoise.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;"></span><span style="font-size: medium;">The <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra17.html">previous ruling</a> dealt with planting a tree in a location where its roots might damage a neighbor's pit. This one discusses a field with plants but without a pit.<br />
<br />
One must not plant a tree near his neighbor's field unless he distances the tree four amot (6 feet) from his neighbor's boundary. This distance is needed to provide sufficient space for cultivating his planting without encroachment on his neighbor's property. If there is a fence, no distance is required.<br />
<br />
If the tree roots extend into the neighbor's property, the neighbor may excavate three hand-breadths deep and remove the roots to facilitate his plowing. If the neighbor was digging a pit and came upon roots, he may cut downwards to whatever depth he finds necessary.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Apple Trees at Pontoise by Camille Pissarro</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/27.txt
<a id="src-00204"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/27.txt`

Bava Batra 27 – First-Fruit Must be From Your Land (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhoSwpEsJBT5fQwhiocpFfJ3HI6gXl-SlhcXAwYdLMuuNRkI6sSjSm72PnCM4l5c98IcLKNcUBdlxaLaEdXkzN_f69aKR_GBpLT-Y1l9_hLz8kjgkD6PMgjCZALaa-vwBu-Z53YXh0Yoi8Q/s1600-h/Levi+Wells+Prentice+-+Apples,+Hat,+and+Tree+1898.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhoSwpEsJBT5fQwhiocpFfJ3HI6gXl-SlhcXAwYdLMuuNRkI6sSjSm72PnCM4l5c98IcLKNcUBdlxaLaEdXkzN_f69aKR_GBpLT-Y1l9_hLz8kjgkD6PMgjCZALaa-vwBu-Z53YXh0Yoi8Q/s320/Levi+Wells+Prentice+-+Apples,+Hat,+and+Tree+1898.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">Ulla said: "A tree within sixteen amot (~30 feet) of a boundary is a 'thief' because it draws nutrients illegally from a neighboring field." One does not bring first fruit from it&nbsp; – because it should be "...<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/26-2.htm">from your field</a>..." and because stolen produce is unfit for Temple service.</span><br />
<br /><span style="font-size: medium;">A question against Ulla: Rabbi Akiva said, "Even a minute measure of land is <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/02/discovery-how-i-was-cause-of-my-own.html">subject to the requirements</a> of first fruit, and it is <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/08/daf-in-100-words-gittin-36.html">fit to write prosbul on its account</a>.</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">Ulla answers: "Rabbi Akiva is talking about wheat, not a tree." Only wheat can grow on a minute measure of land.</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">However, one of Yehoshua's conditions when dividing Israel was that the practice of planting trees near the border should be tolerated by neighbors, thus making the first fruit fit.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Apples, Hat, and Trees by Levi Wells Prentice</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/28.txt
<a id="src-00205"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/28.txt`

Bava Batra 28 – Presumptive Ownership of Real Estate - Chazakah (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg9r-I_D0MbttPom06XSy_dfa3gDrwoT4hzS0KUiRZwb7eHtjSiSqVrGAYiImuBIxZFeZPAlgqTMDQxXDVNYKTU6sjo52IMiEiFM8s_9QgJCnKlIq9DmHB4cC9qbpfznnAqAD1XnvC5JUCM/s1600-h/Paul+Cezanne+-+Man+In+A+Room.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg9r-I_D0MbttPom06XSy_dfa3gDrwoT4hzS0KUiRZwb7eHtjSiSqVrGAYiImuBIxZFeZPAlgqTMDQxXDVNYKTU6sjo52IMiEiFM8s_9QgJCnKlIq9DmHB4cC9qbpfznnAqAD1XnvC5JUCM/s320/Paul+Cezanne+-+Man+In+A+Room.jpg" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">When a person seeks to exact property from another one, the burden of proof is on the claimant. In other words, it is logical to presume that the one who currently holds the object in his possession is the rightful owner. <br />
<br />
In the case of real property, physical "possession" of it is impossible. Current occupancy is also inconclusive since preventing people from ever entering one's property is impossible. Instead, presumptive ownership is assigned to the last person known to have held the property. Thus, when that person claims that the current occupant is an illegal squatter, the burden of proof is on the occupant. If, however, the current resident established a "chazakah," usually by continuous uncontested occupancy for three years, the burden of proof is shifted to the previous owner.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Man in a Room by Paul Cezanne</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/29.txt
<a id="src-00206"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/29.txt`

Bava Batra 29 – The Length of Residence for Presumptive Ownership (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj05Bn168VoyjcpkukHgRMcrcXiF9SD2Tx0c22l8mNSc8D6A_UV9KmDLl8g_DXu-Na1khTVb4r_JERfJNhkKoawvfUYG0AYa78-0IO0JI1tKalpNgTm3vRq8V-s4Z6qgDHc_A7qSEqryt1t/s1600-h/Grigori+Vasilievich+Soroka+-+Reception+room+of+a+Manor+house.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj05Bn168VoyjcpkukHgRMcrcXiF9SD2Tx0c22l8mNSc8D6A_UV9KmDLl8g_DXu-Na1khTVb4r_JERfJNhkKoawvfUYG0AYa78-0IO0JI1tKalpNgTm3vRq8V-s4Z6qgDHc_A7qSEqryt1t/s320/Grigori+Vasilievich+Soroka+-+Reception+room+of+a+Manor+house.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">Presumptive ownership of houses, ditches, and bathhouses - or any other property that yields benefits continually - is established after three years of uncontested occupancy from day to day. For other properties, it depends on their everyday use; for example, presumptive ownership for a field is established after harvesting three crops.<br />
</span><span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
Why three years? For three years after purchasing a property, a person is careful with his deed but longer than that, he is only careful to keep his deed if his property occupancy has been challenged. Therefore, after three years of the unchallenged use of a property, we do not insist that the occupant produce documentary proof of his ownership; instead, we rely on his very occupancy as proof.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Reception Room of a Manor House by Grigori Vasilievich Soroka</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/3.txt
<a id="src-00207"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/3.txt`

Bava Batra 3 – Visual Trespass is Actionable in Court (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVejTqravSQamkuGH2JSLQPZJk3WemyInmr0ndN8FM9uMFNwgcWMSSYOrR36KVW_oon7wV302n3NQCjYDJXcTUJV0281KUgEwGQiWPz0cy5D1Yb2CPUG1rzM0HreC0q0uw0QY5Yg6QNPpX/s1600-h/Caspar+David+Friedrich+-+Landscape+with+Crumbling+Wall.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5373579656998430914" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVejTqravSQamkuGH2JSLQPZJk3WemyInmr0ndN8FM9uMFNwgcWMSSYOrR36KVW_oon7wV302n3NQCjYDJXcTUJV0281KUgEwGQiWPz0cy5D1Yb2CPUG1rzM0HreC0q0uw0QY5Yg6QNPpX/s320/Caspar+David+Friedrich+-+Landscape+with+Crumbling+Wall.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 214px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">Contrary to the <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra2.html" target="_blank">conclusion reached before</a>, now we have decided that visual trespass is damaging. In the case of two partners who agreed to make a partition in their jointly owned courtyard, the “partition” is  understood as a division, not a wall.<br /><br />Now, the case reads as follows. Once they agreed to divide the yard, even though they did not stipulate to build the wall, they must make a stone wall against the objections of either party. This is true even if they have not agreed to divide since any one of them can separate at will. However, the previous ruling  deals with a tiny yard of less than 8 by 4 amot (about 16 by 8 feet), which is only divisible if they agree to divide it.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Landscape with Crumbling Wall by Caspar David Friedrich</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/30.txt
<a id="src-00208"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/30.txt`

Bava Batra 30 – Presumptive Ownership (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2LyUK19LkoCyvzMVcanaUPoKQmIj89ob6OwppQVikGUlFuK7AdvTULNAs5pDXjwu22GKNSnpdKAi_vWZ2FF7UZPdNb04BJYoJrJpupquvFQxAvkPBPdeCRPyDI09CPn2L1k0XZ8F7pqA8/s1600-h/Edward+Hopper+-+Rooms+for+Tourists.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2LyUK19LkoCyvzMVcanaUPoKQmIj89ob6OwppQVikGUlFuK7AdvTULNAs5pDXjwu22GKNSnpdKAi_vWZ2FF7UZPdNb04BJYoJrJpupquvFQxAvkPBPdeCRPyDI09CPn2L1k0XZ8F7pqA8/s320/Edward+Hopper+-+Rooms+for+Tourists.jpg" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">One man told the other, "What are you doing in this house?" The occupant replied, "I bought it from you, and I have used it for three years needed to establish chazakah (presumptive ownership.)" The original owner responded, "I was residing in the inner rooms all this time." <br />
<br />
The litigants came before Rav Nachman, who said to the occupant, "Prove your exclusive use of the house by producing witnesses that you lived there alone, and you will have established chazakah."<br />
<br />
Rava said to Rav Nachman, "Is that the law? The burden of proof rests upon the one who seeks to exact payment from his fellow, that is, on the previous owner!" But the law is like Rav Nachman's since his view always prevails over Rava's.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Rooms for Tourists by Edward Hopper<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/31.txt
<a id="src-00209"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/31.txt`

Bava Batra 31 – Presumption, Amended Pleadings
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgt86BPjOnLyzy9f1AmRVH7WQEia-yWfTYCHLt2jtpn_Y6a-wTtaE7aY1ENSw_Ud7EOUHXgUTxZS2b4nT3A0dnbrLijaC7nG2PbtNT06APvkckIskqML4R2Tyq1XYCIZ7atA1jhZGsRepTT/s1600-h/John+William+North+-+A+Field+of+Barley+1866.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgt86BPjOnLyzy9f1AmRVH7WQEia-yWfTYCHLt2jtpn_Y6a-wTtaE7aY1ENSw_Ud7EOUHXgUTxZS2b4nT3A0dnbrLijaC7nG2PbtNT06APvkckIskqML4R2Tyq1XYCIZ7atA1jhZGsRepTT/s320/John+William+North+-+A+Field+of+Barley+1866.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Two litigants were disputing ownership of a property. One said, "It was the land of my forefathers," and produced witnesses. The other one produced witnesses that he used the land for three years needed to establish presumptive ownership (chazakah.)<br />
<br />
Rabbah said, "Why should he lie?" The current occupant could have kept the land, claiming that he bought it, so we should believe him when he says that he inherited it. But Abaye said, "Why should he lie?" can't be used to contradict witnesses.<br />
<br />
The current occupant then changed his claim, saying, "Yes, the land indeed belonged to your forefathers, but I bought it from them, and I feel as secure as if it were my forefathers" - this claim was accepted.<br />
<br />
The general rule is that one cannot enter a claim that contradicts his previous claim entirely, but he can add information or amend the previous claim by reinterpreting it.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Field of Barley by John William North<span>&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;</span></span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/32.txt
<a id="src-00210"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/32.txt`

Bava Batra 32 – Presumption and “Why Would He Lie?” argument (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_uoO1ffDRepoyyKAk7ANqKS4i96A2Hxue3MhgEkoQA1Dq81SxrzxQVpR0zSgyViiwgy2fvzhma2AqAlunvS1vpe7HTkk91zM05IiR8RpRW1ib6_g893T5kX2d4r_9YQsR9Ugd8UYr3zRQ/s1600-h/Fritz+Wagner+-+The+Contract.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_uoO1ffDRepoyyKAk7ANqKS4i96A2Hxue3MhgEkoQA1Dq81SxrzxQVpR0zSgyViiwgy2fvzhma2AqAlunvS1vpe7HTkk91zM05IiR8RpRW1ib6_g893T5kX2d4r_9YQsR9Ugd8UYr3zRQ/s320/Fritz+Wagner+-+The+Contract.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One man asked the other, "What are you doing on this land?" The other replied, "I bought it from you, and here is the deed." The challenger said, "It is a forged deed, and, as you don't claim to have chazakah, you must vacate the property."<br />
<br />
The occupant leaned over and whispered to Rabbah, "Yes, it is a forged document. However, I originally had a valid deed, and it got lost. I wanted to bring some documents to court."<br />
<br />
Rabbah said, "Why would he lie?" He could have said that the deed was valid, and he would have believed (either the forgery was perfect or the deed was given before the sale). <br />
<br />
Generally, "Why would he lie?" is believed, but the claimant must take a Rabbinically imposed oath that he is telling the truth.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Contract by Fritz Wagner<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/33.txt
<a id="src-00211"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/33.txt`

Bava Batra 33 – Presumption - Rumor Breaks It (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEikNSsO7O13GSUBzW4z_hhrWVaKM35qh6u8CAFIka8LiS0FknVSWzGNhBfcbWc53SWJmT2d0EM46wHwMOVmYhKgaJWB_YXUIXnr8W7DkqHRAUzkMpCNgPHWD1wFWknhCMiCwDf0nJ3bz_fo/s1600-h/Nikolaj+Alekseevich+Kasatkin+-+The+Orphans.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEikNSsO7O13GSUBzW4z_hhrWVaKM35qh6u8CAFIka8LiS0FknVSWzGNhBfcbWc53SWJmT2d0EM46wHwMOVmYhKgaJWB_YXUIXnr8W7DkqHRAUzkMpCNgPHWD1wFWknhCMiCwDf0nJ3bz_fo/s320/Nikolaj+Alekseevich+Kasatkin+-+The+Orphans.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A rumor emerged involving Rava Bar Sharshum that he was using land that belonged to orphans. Abaye told him, "Tell me, what are the circumstances?" <br />
<br />
Rava explained, "I held their father's land as security for loan repayment and harvest collection. Thus, When the loan was completely paid, I kept the land because their father owed me another loan."<br />
<br />
"Had I returned the land, I would be able to collect the second loan only with an oath, and it is proper to <a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/10-20.htm">avoid even truthful oaths</a>. You should believe me on the strength of the 'Why would he lie?' argument, for I could have said a better lie, that I bought that land."<br />
<br />
Abaye ruled, "The rumor functions as protest and ruins your chazakah, the three years of which count only without protests. Therefore, return the land."<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Orphans by Nikolay Alekseevich Kasatkin</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/34.txt
<a id="src-00212"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/34.txt`

Bava Batra 34 – The Case of the Silver Ingot of Rav Abba (Civil)
<span style="font-size: large;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgNu6rLb3iDtPgSxPXZUeYdbaYC3ox3iZjwtSSKwCCyFVp8CiB8IhPc__y6F8kr0GEMzK-0BdZlD0wLi1FY1ePMF8W3Pt90yv65sPAie0xL8FbrMDKUuyfDkK1KVDuAPvKGZr4pIyjVCx-Q/s1600-h/Karl+Witkowski+-+Stealing+Apples.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgNu6rLb3iDtPgSxPXZUeYdbaYC3ox3iZjwtSSKwCCyFVp8CiB8IhPc__y6F8kr0GEMzK-0BdZlD0wLi1FY1ePMF8W3Pt90yv65sPAie0xL8FbrMDKUuyfDkK1KVDuAPvKGZr4pIyjVCx-Q/s320/Karl+Witkowski+-+Stealing+Apples.jpg" /></a></span><span style="font-size: medium;">One man snatched a silver ingot from his fellow. There was one witness to the snatching, but the defendant said, "Yes, I snatched it, but it was my ingot that I snatched!"<br />
</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> <br />
Rabbi Ami considered the case:<br />
<br />
* Should he be required to pay? But there aren't two witnesses!<br />
* Exempt him based on "Why would he lie?" –&nbsp; he could deny having snatched it altogether? This argument is weakened by the witness.<br />
* Make him swear that he did not snatch it? But he himself admits that he did!<br />
* Make him swear that the ingot was his? We can't concoct oaths!<br />
<br />
Rav Abba offered a solution. The snatcher is obligated to take an oath but can not do so, and all such people must pay.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Stealing Apples by Karl Witkowski</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/35.txt
<a id="src-00213"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/35.txt`

Bava Batra 35 – Let He Who Is Stronger Prevail (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhk4S8yrHy2fnVnseOuP4FVXfkksujyTpaKhbTtYj6P7x1o6IjLOmOZoviqIjr1La6XjHxA0zz7DW36H_4f48KGD1G7bBJSMx4AlX7UzJ5BAqzvHtERZp5gjMVJbNtHbPCGG1Q7ZF5Ri4v5/s1600-h/Adriaen+Brower+-+Peasants+Fighting.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhk4S8yrHy2fnVnseOuP4FVXfkksujyTpaKhbTtYj6P7x1o6IjLOmOZoviqIjr1La6XjHxA0zz7DW36H_4f48KGD1G7bBJSMx4AlX7UzJ5BAqzvHtERZp5gjMVJbNtHbPCGG1Q7ZF5Ri4v5/s320/Adriaen+Brower+-+Peasants+Fighting.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In a case where ownership of a property is disputed – for example, one side says, “It belonged to my forefathers," and the other side says, “It belonged to my forefathers,” but neither litigant can prove his claim – the court withdraws and allows the litigants to fight over possession of the property. </span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">Once one gets the object, can the other one take it back? Some say “no” - because the court would not allow a perpetual feud. Others say, “Yes, he can take it back.”</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">One rationale for this principle is that the true owner would eventually come up with the proof of his claim. Furthermore, the true owner would strive more vigorously to retain his property, while the thief would not, knowing that his victory may be short-lived because the owner may subsequently prove his claim.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Peasants Fighting by Adriaen Brower</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/36.txt
<a id="src-00214"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/36.txt`

Bava Batra 36 – Does Plowing Establish Presumptive Ownership? (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgbnxKfgOZb0kk9kwqdQ0GGc8JLbmnVfBybOTntKx8OPSvtN-2whLky59JtVz9yHzBlFLsMI8sPM-fn2-CqarI1JkV70VbuK_ph36RboiNklTbn6eBbfMnY9-R6slAgVLfNXFGBTnVEDv2Z/s1600-h/Frederick+Carl+Frieseke+-+Man+Plowing.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgbnxKfgOZb0kk9kwqdQ0GGc8JLbmnVfBybOTntKx8OPSvtN-2whLky59JtVz9yHzBlFLsMI8sPM-fn2-CqarI1JkV70VbuK_ph36RboiNklTbn6eBbfMnY9-R6slAgVLfNXFGBTnVEDv2Z/s320/Frederick+Carl+Frieseke+-+Man+Plowing.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When one plows somebody else's field, and the other does not protest, is this indicative of the presumptive ownership of the one who plows? <br />
</span><span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
Some say "yes" because a man would not see another plow his land and remain silent. Some say "no" because the owner may be saying to himself that the more the occupant plows, the softer the soil becomes, and the better crop he, the owner, will be able to produce from the fields when he returns to it.<br />
<br />
Rav Ashi said, "I asked all the great scholars of the generation, and they said that plowing establishes chazakah." Rav Nachman bar Yitzhak answered, "Is it proper to rule based on a poll? Others don't think this way." And the final decision is that plowing does not establish chazakah.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Man Plowing by Frederick Carl Frieseke</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/37.txt
<a id="src-00215"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/37.txt`

Bava Batra 37 – Selling the Land but Keeping the Trees (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiOW8Eulg8pfpo30_ZV3ES6bkDyrPLMTOUJb1ZM3cO_iMzDx4bH-khwOui1QNLqic8lv7QwNzBg3PT1ar88DnCFhO0MeHy6Wlkcr-ri_2LOlntvRKhgnUQZSuiSzNIc0N1yfQieuHV1JVoJ/s1600-h/Camille+Pissarro+-+Les+chataigniers+a+Osny+-+The+Chestnut+Trees+at+Osny+-+1873.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiOW8Eulg8pfpo30_ZV3ES6bkDyrPLMTOUJb1ZM3cO_iMzDx4bH-khwOui1QNLqic8lv7QwNzBg3PT1ar88DnCFhO0MeHy6Wlkcr-ri_2LOlntvRKhgnUQZSuiSzNIc0N1yfQieuHV1JVoJ/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Les+chataigniers+a+Osny+-+The+Chestnut+Trees+at+Osny+-+1873.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one sells his land and retains the trees for himself, he keeps a certain amount of land around the trees. So, if his trees die, he is entitled to plant others. <br />
<br />
Does this not contradict Rabbi Akiva's ruling that a seller sells generously, which we have learned from the following: when one sells a house or a field, but not a well located in its midst, then <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra64.html" target="_blank">Rabbi Akiva says that he sells the entire house, leaving himself no right-of-way in it at all</a>?<br />
<br />
In fact, even Rabbi Akiva would agree to the ruling about trees. The tree weakens the surrounding soil, and the seller worries that if the tree dies, the buyer may tell him, "Uproot your tree and be gone!" Thus, the seller reserves land around the trees for himself.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Chestnut Trees at Osny by Camille Pissarro</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/38.txt
<a id="src-00216"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/38.txt`

Bava Batra 38 – Owner's Protest (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjkanXNIcBf17pCwm1w88bGsVADzlYFICbkqaNelkyanYJaAX5ZQw0IMuB1PExbZyFPXaXT50T1WQfwfHCPtzBEEnBa365MjDFYTeMauMksyZHC9ygINC2gvS57VyoFb2RK-KV_lLeOa_iu/s1600-h/Jacek+Malczewski+-+Portrait+of+Two+Young+Men.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjkanXNIcBf17pCwm1w88bGsVADzlYFICbkqaNelkyanYJaAX5ZQw0IMuB1PExbZyFPXaXT50T1WQfwfHCPtzBEEnBa365MjDFYTeMauMksyZHC9ygINC2gvS57VyoFb2RK-KV_lLeOa_iu/s320/Jacek+Malczewski+-+Portrait+of+Two+Young+Men.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Presumptive ownership (chazakah) is only valid in the absence of the alleged owner's protest. If the owner protests at least once in three years, the occupant is put on notice, and his chazakah is ineffective. In other words, if the occupant really bought the field, he should keep the deed, and his negligence to do so in inexcusable in the face of a protest, thus his three years of occupancy don't help.<br />
<br />
It is sufficient to protest in front of two witnesses without the occupant present. These witnesses have friends, their friends have friends, and the word travels till it reaches the occupant. If, however, the owner is in a province that has little communication with the province where his field is, he will not bother to protest since his protest can't reach the occupant anyway, and thus, the chazakah can't be established at all. Examples of such regions are Judea and Galilee, which at the time had little travel between them.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Portrait of Two Young Men by Jacek Malczewsky</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/39.txt
<a id="src-00217"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/39.txt`

Bava Batra 39 – How to Lodge an Effective Protest and Confidentiality Agreements (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDSYd-9Y9U_IU-4OL6qJPXfOw9IN82kpYVRTj_6KFhIGlGvMkvxA9GtNbZzoKuJzHlHfoVzrpmBb5IXfu60xVBWMUHh039Gt4rIJC0q-bqUNBhH548161GdGMmqKWWv-uu0fNlhf4RxqE/s1600-h/Lucian+Freud+-+Two+Irishmen.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDSYd-9Y9U_IU-4OL6qJPXfOw9IN82kpYVRTj_6KFhIGlGvMkvxA9GtNbZzoKuJzHlHfoVzrpmBb5IXfu60xVBWMUHh039Gt4rIJC0q-bqUNBhH548161GdGMmqKWWv-uu0fNlhf4RxqE/s320/Lucian+Freud+-+Two+Irishmen.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the original owner tells two witnesses, "So-and-so is a thief," this is not an effective protest. If, however, he says, "So-and-so is a thief, for he has taken possession of my land through an act of theft, and tomorrow I shall claim it from him in court," this is an effective protest. The threat to sue is unnecessary, but this is how people usually conclude their protest.<br />
<br />
If the protester tells the witnesses, "Don't tell the occupant that I lodged a protest," we assume that he means not to say to him directly, but they may tell others. Thus, this protest is effective. If the witnesses promise on their own, "Not a word of protest will leave our mouths," there is still a chance that they will reveal it inadvertently. Only if they are told, "Keep this completely confidential," can they be relied upon to keep it secret.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Two Irishmen by Lucian Freud</span></div>

---

Bava Batra 4 – King Herod Rebuilds the Temple (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhD5thBh4q0W9rARFBRzQ80u3lo83PLduL5jAahrehLBQaezEeLXb1y7pSbIiB8BuDm0Mi1kO1s3ymxWejAienE4bxpbJK9xf8wtof5jOG-3n8BWhFCzsLkLXyu24reG7b26FO6dLxHKTKF/s1600-h/Roberts+-+Temple.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5373940605398573138" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhD5thBh4q0W9rARFBRzQ80u3lo83PLduL5jAahrehLBQaezEeLXb1y7pSbIiB8BuDm0Mi1kO1s3ymxWejAienE4bxpbJK9xf8wtof5jOG-3n8BWhFCzsLkLXyu24reG7b26FO6dLxHKTKF/s320/Roberts+-+Temple.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 270px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">King Herod feared that the Sages might question his fitness to be a king, leading to a rebellion, and killed all of them, leaving Bava ben Buta, whom he blinded. He then pretended to be a commoner and came to test Bava ben Buta. </span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">H. See, master, what is this wicked slave doing?</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">B. What shall I do to him?</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">H. Curse him.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">B. “</span><span style="font-size: 130%;"><a href="http://bible.cc/ecclesiastes/10-20.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span">Even in your thoughts, do not curse a king</span></a></span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">...”</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">H. But this man is not a king.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">B. “...</span><span style="font-size: 130%;"><a href="http://bible.cc/ecclesiastes/10-20.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span">even in your bedroom do not curse the rich</span></a></span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">...”, and “... </span><span style="font-size: 130%;"><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-28.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span">a prince among your people you shall not curse</span></a></span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">.” </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">H. If I had known that the Sages were so circumspect, I would not have killed them. What is my remedy?</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">B. Rebuild the Temple.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">And so King Herod started.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Temple by Roberts</span></div>

<a id="src-00219"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/40.txt`

Bava Batra 40 – Secret Gift (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9TxBiT2FqGF38wZCSuN0471syXDlHIB4UwOWJKpdMnP-WUH0e-UOqzScWY46YgBi58qeWVeOASjB5aShDQVwEYNw2nZNQhrKAAqcRJ27kaLyXlo0NsNQF3ymBws0YyY42Xw6OzQ61GNQ/s1600-h/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Mr.+and+Mrs.+Isaac+Newton+Phelps+Stokes.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9TxBiT2FqGF38wZCSuN0471syXDlHIB4UwOWJKpdMnP-WUH0e-UOqzScWY46YgBi58qeWVeOASjB5aShDQVwEYNw2nZNQhrKAAqcRJ27kaLyXlo0NsNQF3ymBws0YyY42Xw6OzQ61GNQ/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Mr.+and+Mrs.+Isaac+Newton+Phelps+Stokes.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A gift document written in secret cannot be used to collect the gift. The giver may have already given the property to someone else and is now hiding from the first recipient, and then the gift is not his to give. Or, he may write this gift document to fool all later recipients of this property. Because of these suspicions, a secret gift document is considered void.<br />
<br />
One woman told a man, "I will marry you only if you give me all your property." His son wanted a share. The man then told witnesses, "First, hide yourself and write a gift of all my property to my son." Both gifts were annulled: to the woman – because it was given under duress, to the son – because it was only for subterfuge.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Mr. and Mrs. Isaac Newton Phelps Stoke by John Singer Sargent</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/41.txt
<a id="src-00220"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/41.txt`

Bava Batra 41 – Presumption of Ownership Must Be Accompanied by a Claim (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhlFPZ6_U4NSoAeSrNI00aDSUbf2wNXLfrdQXusioBZkiwyYGVnTHq1N8kbeJLVvkGr4d48tw1qS8I6w-EU-C42x5dRqawJ9Z_s0Vtp6HJnVE99wNPB6eKBN9C7WagQidCmrkHSTYwPEV0/s1600-h/Louis+Charles+Moeller+-+A+Notty+Question.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhlFPZ6_U4NSoAeSrNI00aDSUbf2wNXLfrdQXusioBZkiwyYGVnTHq1N8kbeJLVvkGr4d48tw1qS8I6w-EU-C42x5dRqawJ9Z_s0Vtp6HJnVE99wNPB6eKBN9C7WagQidCmrkHSTYwPEV0/s320/Louis+Charles+Moeller+-+A+Notty+Question.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Any chazakah not accompanied by a claim is not a meaningful chazakah and does not entitle the occupant to keep the property. How so?<br />
<br />
If the previous owner said to the occupant, "What are you doing on my property?" - and the occupant replied, "I am here because nobody ever said anything to me," - his chazakah is not meaningful, and he must vacate the property.<br />
<br />
If, however, the occupant replied, "You sold this land to me," "You gave it to me as a gift," "Your father sold it to me," or "Your father gave it to me as a gift," - it is a meaningful chazakah, and the occupant keeps the property. One who comes into a property by inheritance does not require a supporting claim.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Notty Question by Louis Charles Miller</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/42.txt
<a id="src-00221"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/42.txt`

Bava Batra 42 – Rules of Chazakah (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgKWuTCM4OG6R-OIfNCmXvVAGumhSyZVRGgZNBFYhkocEXbgJjitiuw-_IeG_f9dRj2gYzFoGv1X4WSZbsJiQvsmEzhS6Yg1TcWzAzkDur_aKuhRZp66AdmnekvDDMaVAeM-nD44AjiPmk/s1600-h/August+Renoir+-+Aline+Charigot+And+Renoir.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgKWuTCM4OG6R-OIfNCmXvVAGumhSyZVRGgZNBFYhkocEXbgJjitiuw-_IeG_f9dRj2gYzFoGv1X4WSZbsJiQvsmEzhS6Yg1TcWzAzkDur_aKuhRZp66AdmnekvDDMaVAeM-nD44AjiPmk/s320/August+Renoir+-+Aline+Charigot+And+Renoir.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Suppose three people owned a field in succession, each one for a year. In that case, they combine to establish a chazakah against the original owner, provided their purchases were recorded in deeds. The original owner can't claim that the quick succession of owners was proof of their illegitimate occupancy without him needing to protest. Instead, the public knowledge of their sales should have caused his protest.<br />
<br />
Some people have legitimate access to other people's property, so they can never establish chazakah, even if they have the movables in their possession or if they occupy the real property. Thus, craftsmen, sharecroppers, and property administrators cannot establish a chazakah. Similarly, a husband cannot establish a chazakah on his wife's property, nor can a wife establish a chazakah on her husband's property, a father on his son's property, or a son on his father's property.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Aline Charigot and Renoir by August Renoir</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/43.txt
<a id="src-00222"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/43.txt`

Bava Batra 43 – Partners CAN Establish Chazakah (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi3PRIRywTWhA_6IKC-3omQH4a8RgjqwD_NjRi8tMrEn7QEGf5BBkW0EFuO164W1F9f6HMFhuEWewo61D2_XQxuYeoL-99iR-euMWwXe0OtH2pXzWa8pwbz-UqCvQgCOLkrL-tRyGCZfxg/s1600-h/Wlodzimierz+Tetmajer+-+In+The+Wheat+Field.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi3PRIRywTWhA_6IKC-3omQH4a8RgjqwD_NjRi8tMrEn7QEGf5BBkW0EFuO164W1F9f6HMFhuEWewo61D2_XQxuYeoL-99iR-euMWwXe0OtH2pXzWa8pwbz-UqCvQgCOLkrL-tRyGCZfxg/s320/Wlodzimierz+Tetmajer+-+In+The+Wheat+Field.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Shmuel said the following three rulings: partners can establish chazakah against each other, testify on behalf of the other, and become paid custodians one for the other. <br />
<br />
How can Shmuel contradict the <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra42.html" target="_blank">accepted rule that partners cannot establish chazakah</a>? – His version of this ruling was that they can. </span><span style="font-size: medium;">Shmuel</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> explains that it is normal for partners to expect regular returns from their field. If one occupied it for three consecutive years, he is believed to say that he bought his partner out, for otherwise, they would alternate more frequently.<br />
<br />
How can he testify for his partner if he is interested in the outcome? He needs to renounce his share.<br />
<br />
How are they <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_metzia/bava_metzia34.html" target="_blank">paid custodians liable for theft</a>? If they guard the field in turns, then each pays the other with his work.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: In the Wheat Field by Wlodzimierz Tetmajer<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/44.txt
<a id="src-00223"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/44.txt`

Bava Batra 44 – The Seller of a Field Cannot Testify for the Buyer (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg7f0CxaNU4kk_7y2LvE_rNBBBX0_9HslvXlBuWx3fgLwq2lfixRbDMdeuKlicX5oDlP2pkUH-K95kLC4aLWP7NZ9Oz9ITQB0u-_5pHSYt9IUx1QMHw1EevAeztsN4JzCntGSuLcrNVpz4/s1600-h/Jos%C3%A9+Benlliure+Ortiz+-+Autorretrato+con+camisa+blanca+-+Self-portrait+with+white+shirt.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg7f0CxaNU4kk_7y2LvE_rNBBBX0_9HslvXlBuWx3fgLwq2lfixRbDMdeuKlicX5oDlP2pkUH-K95kLC4aLWP7NZ9Oz9ITQB0u-_5pHSYt9IUx1QMHw1EevAeztsN4JzCntGSuLcrNVpz4/s320/Jos%C3%A9+Benlliure+Ortiz+-+Autorretrato+con+camisa+blanca+-+Self-portrait+with+white+shirt.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one borrows money, his real property becomes a guarantee for his repayment of the loan, but not his movables. Even if he promises to repay with "the shirt on his back," still, if he does not have that shirt, he can't repay with it. However, even if he sold the field in the interim, physically, the field is still there, and the lender can repossess it.<br />
<br />
Because of that, the seller of a field cannot testify on behalf of the buyer. If someone can prove that the seller never owned the field and he is, in fact, a thief, then that field is not a guarantee for the seller's loans, and the seller becomes a "bad person who borrows and does not repay" - a situation that people try to avoid.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Self-portrait with a white shirt by Jose Benlliure Ortiz</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/45.txt
<a id="src-00224"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/45.txt`

Bava Batra 45 – The Chazakah of a Craftsman (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVPM6KNZKnYmq6uGKMMcG6YHH-RsG2xtDqjUCydQRP1ow814yfDWKb1V6DhKrP0Bo9hI_5VQ_y93ymYgQBmics7L3kSCt9vceuUPd31xYbVjgTTG-PUjR4nhFpYG9ia_I6csZD-Fevzlo/s1600-h/Johann+Georg+Hinz+-+Treasure+C.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVPM6KNZKnYmq6uGKMMcG6YHH-RsG2xtDqjUCydQRP1ow814yfDWKb1V6DhKrP0Bo9hI_5VQ_y93ymYgQBmics7L3kSCt9vceuUPd31xYbVjgTTG-PUjR4nhFpYG9ia_I6csZD-Fevzlo/s320/Johann+Georg+Hinz+-+Treasure+C.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A craftsman does not establish a chazakah in an article known to have belonged to someone simply by having it in his possession.<br />
<br />
Said Rabbah, "This is only true when the original owner gave the craftsman the article in the presence of witnesses. But if not, the craftsman could have denied receiving the article altogether and is believed on the strength of the "Why would he lie?" argument.<br />
<br />
Said Abaye, "If so, he should be believed even if there were witnesses, for had he wanted to lie, he could have said that he returned the article."<br />
<br />
They differ about the following question: if someone deposits an article with his fellow in the presence of witnesses, does the custodian need to return it also in the presence of witnesses? The accepted answer is "no," meaning Abaye's ruling prevails.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Treasure Chest by Johann Georg Hinz</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/46.txt
<a id="src-00225"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/46.txt`

Bava Batra 46 – Discovery Request Against a Craftsman (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhqRZcJaS80mXcvP2dq3G2-nBEBy2ti_MKB5U5m5zvGg5t1nnzWF4Jf54aiqic-36T784PnB0s2NgaJuyln9HMg6_55ZCxp5iQ5Wj5W5JZLdezi-POPF43C41yeE1SMZTnRsTeINCCeS8E/s1600-h/Pieter+The+Younger+Brueghel+-+A+Flemish+Proverb+-+A+Wife+Hiding+Her+Infidelity+From+Her+Husband+Under+A+Blue+Cloak.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhqRZcJaS80mXcvP2dq3G2-nBEBy2ti_MKB5U5m5zvGg5t1nnzWF4Jf54aiqic-36T784PnB0s2NgaJuyln9HMg6_55ZCxp5iQ5Wj5W5JZLdezi-POPF43C41yeE1SMZTnRsTeINCCeS8E/s320/Pieter+The+Younger+Brueghel+-+A+Flemish+Proverb+-+A+Wife+Hiding+Her+Infidelity+From+Her+Husband+Under+A+Blue+Cloak.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Abaye said to Rava: "Come, and I will show you the practice of the cheats of Pumbedita" (these cheats were craftsmen).<br />
<br />
If someone says to one of them, "Give me back my cloak, which I gave you to repair," he answers, "It never happened." And if the claimant persists, "But I have witnesses who saw it in your possession!" - he retorts, "That cloak which they saw was a different one."<br />
<br />
And if the claimant says, "Produce the cloak to ascertain if it is, in fact, mine," - the craftsman says to him, "I will not produce the cloak because of your unfounded claims, as it would be unfair to the owner."<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Wife Hiding Her Infidelity From Her Husband Under A Blue Cloak (A Flemish Proverb) by Peter The Younger Brueghel</span></div>

---

Bava Batra 47 – Interested Party in a Lawsuit (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEisw-dmi4nRGzl-t_HJheLz21DHisR3uuCiedH8BI9k8GDqirbh_GTx5MuBQ-hHvbudyxRlMwp5DxhLf_bHvTg85YjIXW5CssuKRG0ZpdaUVily-dImNdmLDw1pKrm6jwTmhJ5s-r-a9qk/s1600-h/Henry+Herbert+La+Thangue+-+In+The+Orchard+Haylands+Graffham.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEisw-dmi4nRGzl-t_HJheLz21DHisR3uuCiedH8BI9k8GDqirbh_GTx5MuBQ-hHvbudyxRlMwp5DxhLf_bHvTg85YjIXW5CssuKRG0ZpdaUVily-dImNdmLDw1pKrm6jwTmhJ5s-r-a9qk/s320/Henry+Herbert+La+Thangue+-+In+The+Orchard+Haylands+Graffham.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A person is disqualified from testifying in a matter in which he has a material interest. Can a sharecropper testify on behalf of his employer concerning the land on which he is working?<br />
<br />
If there is unharvested fruit in the field, he cannot testify. The sharecropper has a material interest because if someone else proves to be the actual owner of the field, the sharecropper will not collect his full share of the unharvested fruit.<br />
<br />
However, he can testify if there is no fruit in the field. Though advancing his employer's cause might protect his job as a sharecropper in this field, he knows that many other sharecropping jobs are available to him. Moreover, he knows that his employer is not obligated to continue to employ him. Therefore, his interest in the outcome of the case is negligible.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: In The Orchard Haylands Graffham by Henry Herbert La Thangue</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/48.txt
<a id="src-00227"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/48.txt`

Bava Batra 48 – Is a Forced Action Valid? (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3Ilj8upGLxTc3PocRvo0eAabCqtMyxDbx-Cqu46HKOWoPGa2xdWZBNr0GSCcvGwNirTaRTYFFdqd5UI8MXCF-AdtVGx4UNMP6XsaW3oEQ-Ce7KfSiqex8X6RTkGPHOuPMVc5pkBItKgM/s1600-h/William+Henry+Knight+-+The+Argument.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3Ilj8upGLxTc3PocRvo0eAabCqtMyxDbx-Cqu46HKOWoPGa2xdWZBNr0GSCcvGwNirTaRTYFFdqd5UI8MXCF-AdtVGx4UNMP6XsaW3oEQ-Ce7KfSiqex8X6RTkGPHOuPMVc5pkBItKgM/s320/William+Henry+Knight+-+The+Argument.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If they subjected him to distress until he finally relented and sold them what they demanded, his sale is valid, and he cannot retract.<br />
<br />
What is the reason?<br />
<br />
* Is it because any sale is forced since the seller needs money? - No, it could be different when it is against his will.<br />
* Is it because a recalcitrant husband forced to give a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Get_%28divorce_document%29">Get</a> is indeed divorced? - This is not valid proof because it is a mitzvah to heed the directive of the Sages.<br />
<br />
Rather, it is derived from the following ruling: if they subjected a </span><span style="font-size: medium;">woman</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> to distress until she agreed to be married, the marriage is valid. This proof stands. However, the Sages later annulled such a marriage: he behaved improperly; therefore, they behaved improperly with him.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Argument by William Henry Knight</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/49.txt
<a id="src-00228"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/49.txt`

Bava Batra 49 – Witnesses Can't Change their Minds (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-NjUoR6sZJHzmI3a9ieq8iSKeMwoJuBmvNqdmqPB2xjjx7vZ2PmV1L1pqaIYlNtq-hBsqDflXoMumM00cHkYJ8fXlDOGMW9UQ01H92_tFSBM8sKOE0T05wjh1tKpaN8ZvKIwxqNVIgxA/s1600-h/+Sandor+Liezen-Mayer+-+Queen+Elisabeth+Signs+The+Condemnation+To+Death+To+Mary+Stuart+-+1879.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-NjUoR6sZJHzmI3a9ieq8iSKeMwoJuBmvNqdmqPB2xjjx7vZ2PmV1L1pqaIYlNtq-hBsqDflXoMumM00cHkYJ8fXlDOGMW9UQ01H92_tFSBM8sKOE0T05wjh1tKpaN8ZvKIwxqNVIgxA/s320/+Sandor+Liezen-Mayer+-+Queen+Elisabeth+Signs+The+Condemnation+To+Death+To+Mary+Stuart+-+1879.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Tabbi distressed Pappi until he relented and sold him what he demanded. Rabbah bar bar Chanah signed two documents: a notification that the sale was executed under duress, as well as the document of purchase.<br />
<br />
Said Rav Huna: both documents have legal force. But how can it be? Instead, Rav Huna meant that the forced sale would be valid if not canceled by the prior notification – since it was Rav Huna who introduced <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/10/bava-batra-48-is-forced-action-valid.html">the forced sale rule</a>.<br />
<br />
But we have a rule that a witness, having testified, can't offer a new testimony contradicting his first one. How could Rabbah sign on both documents? - Exactly! Since he signed on the notification of duress first, his signature on the sale document becomes invalid.</span><div><br /></div><div>Art: Queen Elizabeth Sign The Condemnation To Death To Maria Stuart by Sandon Liezen Mayer</div>

---

Bava Batra 5 - Fence Cost Settlement (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjEqp36jp9Qc33pId3eFXdXLNirF7vYyAqemSVYVSukcsFYf3Mmf061HDGK1rcYDjC9vp2azzkm_U7kpkf3o19iqKMIRMhqJNrG52jPwcZDcmy4kCYuSTJf4oRbwQkpkvqaAoWccAKEQl_d/s1600-h/Pierre+Bonnard+-+Behind+the+Fence.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5374315627278842098" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjEqp36jp9Qc33pId3eFXdXLNirF7vYyAqemSVYVSukcsFYf3Mmf061HDGK1rcYDjC9vp2azzkm_U7kpkf3o19iqKMIRMhqJNrG52jPwcZDcmy4kCYuSTJf4oRbwQkpkvqaAoWccAKEQl_d/s320/Pierre+Bonnard+-+Behind+the+Fence.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 287px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">Ravina had four fields that surrounded Runia's field. He built fences around them and demanded reimbursement from Runia since Runia's field was now wholly fenced.<br /><br />Runia refused since he had done nothing to indicate his satisfaction with the fences. Ravina asked for the cost of the fence material if it was bought cheaply. Then, for the hire of a watchman. Runia kept refusing.<br /><br />One day, Runia was harvesting dates in his field. Ravina sent his sharecropper to take a cluster of dates, and Runia shouted at him. Ravina said, "You have shown that you want the dates protected." They went to Rava's court. Rava told Runia, "If you want to settle for what Ravina offered – good, and if not, you will have to pay half of the real cost of the fence."</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Behind the Fence by Pierre Bonnard</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/50.txt
<a id="src-00230"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/50.txt`

Bava Batra 50 – No Chazakah for Damages (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg7ZU9-F-ZSnI6o_Mp6dXxvV1dYcZfls-Cnh7UZoZFTFyvCKGGV0mmeWcJicwlijkuIPcqxBPtJ5ehqgfmUS6sz4CavYYMFx9aN1Obkxudxwy07Jl1niSSyWnT7eThlmpTi5OdoOwAJnaQ/s1600-h/Cecco+del+Caravaggio+-+Woman+with+a+Dove.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg7ZU9-F-ZSnI6o_Mp6dXxvV1dYcZfls-Cnh7UZoZFTFyvCKGGV0mmeWcJicwlijkuIPcqxBPtJ5ehqgfmUS6sz4CavYYMFx9aN1Obkxudxwy07Jl1niSSyWnT7eThlmpTi5OdoOwAJnaQ/s320/Cecco+del+Caravaggio+-+Woman+with+a+Dove.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One cannot establish a chazakah on the property of a married woman. If someone occupies her property for three years without her protest, she can say that she expected her husband to protest, so her absence of protest is of no consequence. She does not have to protest her husband's use of her land either. However, if her husband ruins her field with ditches, she has to protest; otherwise, her absence of protest will be interpreted as an admission that he had bought the land.<br />
<br />As a rule, however, one can't establish the right to damaging behavior. For example, if one installs a kiln that emits heavy smoke, he cannot claim to have established a chazakah. The neighbor can protest and block this after any time period. The same applies to an outhouse if its odor disturbs the neighbor.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Woman With A Dove by Cecco del Caravaggio</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/51.txt
<a id="src-00231"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/51.txt`

Bava Batra 51 – When One Sells Land to his Wife (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgeZ4QfQRAnxSHJFIacoxNM9H5L-sJ3C-0Ta_kYiQeuBSOu_Pil4HUPtcZRgvG07if64mVpkQOZ5mZl_UrqghAxtvOOaxApG-9QItzUIAzgvsC7IewGN4JvfrZKE89sM0AXuCRfHTdrxGA/s1600-h/Quentin++Massys+-+The+Moneylender+and+his+Wife+-+detail.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgeZ4QfQRAnxSHJFIacoxNM9H5L-sJ3C-0Ta_kYiQeuBSOu_Pil4HUPtcZRgvG07if64mVpkQOZ5mZl_UrqghAxtvOOaxApG-9QItzUIAzgvsC7IewGN4JvfrZKE89sM0AXuCRfHTdrxGA/s320/Quentin++Massys+-+The+Moneylender+and+his+Wife+-+detail.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a man sold land to his wife, and she bought it with money that he knew nothing about till now, he can claim that he only wanted to discover the source of her hidden funds, but not to really sell the field, and thus reverse the sale. However, the sale is final if she buys it with money he had known from before.<br />
<br />
The best way to sell the field to one's wife is to write both terms in the contract, "the field is sold to you" and "the field is given to you." The sale term will help her if the field is repossessed by the husband's lenders – by giving her the right to be reimbursed by the husband. The term "given" will help against a neighbor's&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/08/immediate-neighbor-of-property-has.html">right to buy an adjoining field</a>. <br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Moneylender And His Wife (detail) by Quentin Massys</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/52.txt
<a id="src-00232"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/52.txt`

Bava Batra 52 – Two Meanings of Chazakah (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_sce440ZJz-unnfTNgEcSBw6WafBnow2L6_hWI7g9ZmwgYfEAGA9mTNHuALWdIua7lhOv8mCcjsyxv2JnK52OVw_n5-hh4cKKeXSc75PpAse_kjyuNMxlSip5lrPFBUn0fXsmpS8e9Yc/s1600-h/Winslow+Homer+-+Children+On+A+Fence.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_sce440ZJz-unnfTNgEcSBw6WafBnow2L6_hWI7g9ZmwgYfEAGA9mTNHuALWdIua7lhOv8mCcjsyxv2JnK52OVw_n5-hh4cKKeXSc75PpAse_kjyuNMxlSip5lrPFBUn0fXsmpS8e9Yc/s320/Winslow+Homer+-+Children+On+A+Fence.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The chazakah, or presumption of ownership, discussed so far had a challenge against it. For example, a case where a seller, that is, the previous owner, claims "I did not sell the land," and the purchaser, that is, the occupant, claims, "purchased it" - this is the chazakah of proving title, which requires three years to take effect.<br />
<br />
But regarding a chazakah against which there is no challenge, for example, one who gives a gift, or two brothers who divide an estate – where the purpose of chazakah is merely to acquire the property in question – if one locked, fenced, or breached the property even to a minor extent – this is considered chazakah.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Children On A Fence by Winslow Homer</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/53.txt
