**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/53.txt`

Bava Batra 53 – Is the Presence of the Giver Required? (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgahv7KNty6x52ixnFplD5LAG-W5nxCdRIruBUtw-K3cYR8u6FVqpT6jMP5HvUmKYIijsAc45Txw8qBtqSkf26pvZUgrRFNhHLXgxSJAVTKwGkrBuJsOYvTrGqf70vRQnBbOFG2hkDO7HE/s1600-h/Pieter+the+Elder+Bruegel+-+Giving+Presents+at+a+Wedding.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgahv7KNty6x52ixnFplD5LAG-W5nxCdRIruBUtw-K3cYR8u6FVqpT6jMP5HvUmKYIijsAc45Txw8qBtqSkf26pvZUgrRFNhHLXgxSJAVTKwGkrBuJsOYvTrGqf70vRQnBbOFG2hkDO7HE/s320/Pieter+the+Elder+Bruegel+-+Giving+Presents+at+a+Wedding.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">After a price has been agreed upon, some indication of the seller's readiness to transfer the property is necessary. This can be accomplished by the seller instructing the buyer to go and <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/10/bava-batra-52-two-meanings-of-chazakah.html">perform an act of chazakah</a> upon the land. But where the seller is present, he does not have to say anything, and his silence alone indicates his acquiescence.<br />
<br />
What is the rule for a gift?<br />
<br />
Rav says that the giver gives the gift generously out of fondness for the recipient, so no further instruction is necessary, and the chazakah can be performed in his absence. Shmuel says that since the giver receives no money, his instruction is undoubtedly required. Actually, Shmuel agrees that the gift is given generously. However, no gift is possibly being given at all.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Giving Presents At A Wedding by Pieter the Elder Bruegel</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/54.txt
<a id="src-00234"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/54.txt`

Bava Batra 54 – Acquiring Land by Lying Down on It (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjKuHUn_4CW08w5p7jbvgoJhleMe_vS6lvVt25dE0nWZFuUti0BBYAAeUNSux9OLWJ70zMqrBsxD1rSRBbeiXQb6Atjp2PZhaXephAjEWRfw1xDlEt8qBRE0YxC7toKuxvNwdtmPN0icv8/s1600-h/James+Goodwin+Clonney+-+Offering+Baby+a+Rose.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjKuHUn_4CW08w5p7jbvgoJhleMe_vS6lvVt25dE0nWZFuUti0BBYAAeUNSux9OLWJ70zMqrBsxD1rSRBbeiXQb6Atjp2PZhaXephAjEWRfw1xDlEt8qBRE0YxC7toKuxvNwdtmPN0icv8/s320/James+Goodwin+Clonney+-+Offering+Baby+a+Rose.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Said Rav Amram, "The following ruling was told to us by Rav Sheshet, and he enlightened our eyes by adducing proof of it."<br />
<br />
<i><b>The rule</b></i><br />
<br />
A convert is <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/04/bava-kamma-110.html">like a new-born child</a>: he has severed connection with his old family, and if he has not created a new one yet, he has no inheritors. One who spreads out mats on the ownerless land of a deceased convert and lies down upon them has acquired the land.<br />
<br />
<i><b>Proof</b></i><br />
<br />
One can acquire a Canaanite slave using a propriety act, such as having the slave put on a shoe for him, remove his shoe, or lift him. We see that supporting the weight is a propriety act – and so it is with the land: spreading the mats and lying down on it constitutes a proprietary act. <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/10/kiddushin-23-can-canaanite-slave-woman.html" target="_blank">Compare this to a slave woman</a>.<br />
</span><div><br /></div><div>Art: Offering Baby a Rose by James Goodwin Clonney</div>

---

### content/bava_batra/55.txt
<a id="src-00235"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/55.txt`

Bava Batra 55 – The Legal Force of Secular Law (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjMjydWWSPbOzmU3Wt12WeJQqPYzzhMlCr-Tj_rme0zOdyDl9eWY3aMRZdZ7tJSX33URXO36x_8HhLkJI_cb78ZF4DarV6mUgcOXUTJ9OwPRvKG5vKR1R_2mgPKtrmwoVlnxqQbG4DWWl4/s1600-h/Kirk+-+A+Persian+in+Thought.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjMjydWWSPbOzmU3Wt12WeJQqPYzzhMlCr-Tj_rme0zOdyDl9eWY3aMRZdZ7tJSX33URXO36x_8HhLkJI_cb78ZF4DarV6mUgcOXUTJ9OwPRvKG5vKR1R_2mgPKtrmwoVlnxqQbG4DWWl4/s320/Kirk+-+A+Persian+in+Thought.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><b>The law of the kingdom is the law</b><br />
<br />
All tax and civil laws that prevail in a country have legal force in Jewish court, since the country's citizenry voluntarily accepts upon itself to abide by the government's laws. Thus, a Jew who takes possession of property according to the provisions of local law is not guilty of theft even if the Torah law would consider the property belonging to another Jew. This applies, however, only to the laws sanctioned by the constitution of the country but not when monarchy appropriates property by force.<br />
<br />
<b>The chazakah of the Persians is not effective until forty years have elapsed</b><br />
<br />
Although in Persia only recorded real estate transactions were recognized as valid, anyone who occupied a property for forty years was considered to be its legitimate owner.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Persian in Thought by Kirk</span></div>

---

Bava Batra 56 – False Witnesses for Chazakah (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjJFjSU0mfe6wcFQrsoDdeb6RMI0Bi08cXskC8tG_-9-BqkAiBC1jYmanify-fC3DtPejhGFAfKkEQzVLbVM-NJ7qkcHg6D_1mbs48FoTupNa7Qu2d6EtcqNxNjLIkJS8rofzQ5wW2Ejzo/s1600-h/Hermann+Kauffmann+-+Workers+Talking+Politics.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjJFjSU0mfe6wcFQrsoDdeb6RMI0Bi08cXskC8tG_-9-BqkAiBC1jYmanify-fC3DtPejhGFAfKkEQzVLbVM-NJ7qkcHg6D_1mbs48FoTupNa7Qu2d6EtcqNxNjLIkJS8rofzQ5wW2Ejzo/s320/Hermann+Kauffmann+-+Workers+Talking+Politics.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If two witnesses testified on behalf of a person that he used a property for three years, and they were found to be false witnesses, they pay the original owner everything.<br />
<br />
Ordinarily, when two pairs of witnesses offer conflicting testimony, the result is a stalemate; the court does not know which pair to believe. However, when the second pair impugns the first pair's ability to have witnessed the event altogether, the second pair is believed, and the first witnesses are designated false (plotters). Whatever penalty they sought to impose against their victim is assessed against them.<br />
<br />
In our case, they sought to deprive the original owner of the field by falsely testifying that the occupant had established a chazakah. Accordingly, they must pay the field's value to the owner, who receives these punitive damages in addition to the field itself, which he retrieves from the occupant.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Workers Talking Politics by Hermann Kauffmann<br />
<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/57.txt
<a id="src-00237"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/57.txt`

Bava Batra 57 -  Activities that Establish Presumption of Ownership (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgu3v1OSUjKB0tnXj2C_4tRaR_CAmcZ3XihVb_Z0RTPcBNUOqd6_3raBEIu6q1G7QERW0NeCQzdRx_mqaOLIZPErNlHxiQiCAksuwZp5MRVHvr9Yk6Fb_RehXDXsYu0IxYYhb0BZ4BSM50/s1600-h/Alexandre+Defaux+-+Feeding+the+Chickens.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgu3v1OSUjKB0tnXj2C_4tRaR_CAmcZ3XihVb_Z0RTPcBNUOqd6_3raBEIu6q1G7QERW0NeCQzdRx_mqaOLIZPErNlHxiQiCAksuwZp5MRVHvr9Yk6Fb_RehXDXsYu0IxYYhb0BZ4BSM50/s320/Alexandre+Defaux+-+Feeding+the+Chickens.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">These activities do not establish chazakah: if a person would place an animal in a courtyard belonging to someone else; if he would place an oven, millstones, or a stove in the courtyard; if he would raise a chicken or deposit his manure there. The property owner can claim that he saw no harm in allowing these items to remain.<br />
<br />
But if the user made a partition for his animals ten hand-breadths high, or he erected such a partition for an oven, stove or millstone; if he brought his chicken into the owner's house, or if he made for his manure in the courtyard a place either three hand-breadths deep or three hand-breadths high – this is a chazakah. If the owner did not protest these uses of his property for three years, it supports the user's claim that he acquired the right to use the purposes for those purposes.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Feeding the Chickens by Alexandre Defaux</span></div>

---

Bava Batra 58 – Rav Banaah and the Crypt of Abraham (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMDfiy5R_l4aW_491sr1bKZhulEWbiOWGmhk75rAJA-u820PGK04c69NE-TiAfVF8FvFAmTiHTLQQuUku998oxFnmxKW1KlobCGeEY5hajxGGRYtEKGDif8xuhQljWomn7Vxacvlshlxk/s1600-h/Charles+Angrand+-+A+Couple+in+the+Street.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMDfiy5R_l4aW_491sr1bKZhulEWbiOWGmhk75rAJA-u820PGK04c69NE-TiAfVF8FvFAmTiHTLQQuUku998oxFnmxKW1KlobCGeEY5hajxGGRYtEKGDif8xuhQljWomn7Vxacvlshlxk/s320/Charles+Angrand+-+A+Couple+in+the+Street.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Banaah would mark the boundaries of burial crypts by measuring them inside, so that people would not inadvertently walk over them and contract ritual impurity.<br />
<br />
When he reached the crypt of Abraham, he found Eliezer, the servant of Abraham, one of the seven righteous people who never died. Rav Banaah asked, What is Abraham doing?" and Eliezer replied, "He is lying in the arms of Sarah, and she is peering at his head." This symbolizes the true union of Abraham and Sarah, which transcended the physical limitations of their earthly marriage. <br />
<br />
Eliezer announced Rav Banaah, and Abraham said, "Let him enter. It is well known that there is no physical desire in this world." Rav Banaah surveyed the dimensions and departed.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Couple in the Street by Charles Angrand</span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/59.txt`

Bava Batra 59 – Privacy Rights Limit Renovations (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhixdxDnEqwaaMkwg40DlAgIXEk-UR1otdXrL02WT_b7rBcL-ewIvXqJgDNJ2cKOa3FxfbhIaIrIVFXMxpSztrHL7qr_TDA3xAXh-ZKk03Xu2A5zAie23jrL9OpJJ4Qa_usUs1_5Hd7GRE/s1600-h/Edward+Hopper+-+Room+in+New+York.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhixdxDnEqwaaMkwg40DlAgIXEk-UR1otdXrL02WT_b7rBcL-ewIvXqJgDNJ2cKOa3FxfbhIaIrIVFXMxpSztrHL7qr_TDA3xAXh-ZKk03Xu2A5zAie23jrL9OpJJ4Qa_usUs1_5Hd7GRE/s320/Edward+Hopper+-+Room+in+New+York.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One may not open his windows into a jointly owned courtyard, since he will be able to observe the activities of his partners in the courtyard below without their knowledge, thereby committing visual trespass. <br />
<br />
The person opening the window could argue to his partner: "In any event you need to conceal your actions in the courtyard from me, and windows will not result in any additional visual trespass."<br />
<br />
However, his partner can reply, "When you were in your house and your door was closed, I was able to use the courtyard for private activities. But now, if you open a window to the courtyard, even when you are in your home, I need to conceal myself from you."<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Room in New York by Edward Hopper</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/6.txt
<a id="src-00240"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/6.txt`

Bava Batra 6 – Privacy on the Roof (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjAX-RLYiD1VNF3fy_egSRnH6-OM1CMXwn9JXSgM2DrPV8_jSonWfyHECPsrCt02cj3oVUh2crY2k9qDxJpd1YTsvv5bv2gy1ZpnUCQRm-p-lvKr2kYc6CkbZa70df2QLMmSWVqzggijnhe/s1600-h/Thomas+Jones+-+Rooftops+in+Naples.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5374695094932475170" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjAX-RLYiD1VNF3fy_egSRnH6-OM1CMXwn9JXSgM2DrPV8_jSonWfyHECPsrCt02cj3oVUh2crY2k9qDxJpd1YTsvv5bv2gy1ZpnUCQRm-p-lvKr2kYc6CkbZa70df2QLMmSWVqzggijnhe/s400/Thomas+Jones+-+Rooftops+in+Naples.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 161px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 400px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">If two homes are standing on two opposite sides of a public domain, both owners must make a fence of four amot (about 6 feet) high across half of their roof. The fences must not be directly opposite each other. Instead, each must cover the adjoining side, preventing his neighbor from looking directly into his roof and preventing him from looking into his neighbor's roof. Furthermore, the fences must be slightly longer than half the roof, thus further obstructing the view.<br /><br />It would be impractical for each owner to build a fence and unenforceable to require only one owner to do so.<br /><br />Even though one owner can say, "What difference does my fence make? The public sees you anyway?" - the other one can reply, "I can hide from the public by doing my private acts at night, but I can't hide from you."</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Rooftops in Naples by Thomas Jones</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/60.txt
<a id="src-00241"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/60.txt`

Bava Batra 60 – Source for Laws of Privacy (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgz1XGyXvNfQjNJiaxzVEU1IlHEY5uH4hrtgGNA4Y694uB_LkDAilMtcJERcT01DHPxqBiS7V_5afTfc64HyhOBqKxKgW5tkzHvonIFQDR3rDf51RMZrEOi-gnaRZ09c34vKfAqWk_8iDc/s1600-h/Claude+Monet+-+Still+Life+with+Piece+of+Beef.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgz1XGyXvNfQjNJiaxzVEU1IlHEY5uH4hrtgGNA4Y694uB_LkDAilMtcJERcT01DHPxqBiS7V_5afTfc64HyhOBqKxKgW5tkzHvonIFQDR3rDf51RMZrEOi-gnaRZ09c34vKfAqWk_8iDc/s320/Claude+Monet+-+Still+Life+with+Piece+of+Beef.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Even if one is allowed by others to open a window or a door in a courtyard, he should not open a window opposite another's window nor a door opposite another's door.&nbsp; Why?<br />
<br />"<a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/24-5.htm">and Bilam raised his eye and saw Israel dwelling tribe by tribe...and he said...how goodly are your tents</a>!" Bilam saw that the openings of their tents were not aligned one opposite the other, and his words demonstrate how highly Torah values privacy.<br />
<br />
When the Temple was destroyed, many Jews became ascetics and resolved not to eat meat and not to drink wine. Rabbi Yehoshua asked them why. They said it because the Temple does not have it anymore. He replied, then, you should not eat bread, fruit, or drink water because these too were parts of the Temple service. Rather, in a house, leave a small part unpainted, and in a feast, skip a dish.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Still Life With a Piece of Beef by Claude Monet</span></div>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/61.txt`

Bava Batra 61 – When One Sells a House (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhGihiP4l6Fyo1H-oImdzpjEwGSOGkcKMiI_eXygwjTl8dKUQCzXWEDFWn3i8nH3a-gMMJuz5oKFjJxAp0iGZYPGSW7JHEFhvjlXeSwfsbRRI6SpJ32YhFJiqPuvprXmMyG4C-PJs07exA/s1600-h/Atkinson+Grimshaw+-+A+lady+in+a+garden+by+moonlight+-+1882.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhGihiP4l6Fyo1H-oImdzpjEwGSOGkcKMiI_eXygwjTl8dKUQCzXWEDFWn3i8nH3a-gMMJuz5oKFjJxAp0iGZYPGSW7JHEFhvjlXeSwfsbRRI6SpJ32YhFJiqPuvprXmMyG4C-PJs07exA/s320/Atkinson+Grimshaw+-+A+lady+in+a+garden+by+moonlight+-+1882.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The following rulings were promulgated for those times' architectural styles, usages, and practices. All such regulations depend on the prevailing custom at any given time or place. <br />
<br />
If one sells a house without specifying what is included in the sale, he has not sold the annex, even if it opens into the house. Nor has he sold a storeroom in the rear of the house. Such closets served as a storage area for valuables and did not function as part of the living area of the house. Neither has he sold the rooftop if it has a parapet around it at least ten handbreads high.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A lady in a garden by moonlight - by Atkinson Grimshaw</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/62.txt
<a id="src-00243"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/62.txt`

Bava Batra 62 – "I am not retaining anything" in Real Estate Contracts (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh1rbxCHvrFNkKTyHDaXCyNN8I34JroIfNBH03X7YYvJFi7BjSIvk3IljnsVEbSXna0i_02GCHe-fsPpzNA_4wjVrZRXtpHVDykftbGgjq9n3FG0snfu_qPTU2bwH9JJTS0apzBFVCErQ4/s1600-h/William+Bell+Scott+-+Albrecht+D%C3%BCrer+on+the+Balcony+of+his+House+1854.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh1rbxCHvrFNkKTyHDaXCyNN8I34JroIfNBH03X7YYvJFi7BjSIvk3IljnsVEbSXna0i_02GCHe-fsPpzNA_4wjVrZRXtpHVDykftbGgjq9n3FG0snfu_qPTU2bwH9JJTS0apzBFVCErQ4/s320/William+Bell+Scott+-+Albrecht+D%C3%BCrer+on+the+Balcony+of+his+House+1854.jpg" /></a>
</div><span style="font-size: medium;">Suppose one sells a "house" in a large apartment building to his fellow. Even though he defined the boundaries of the entire building in the deed, it is possible that he intended to sell just one apartment, and he drew the boundaries of the whole building only to utilize known landmarks. Since the seller stated that he was selling a "house" (as opposed to an "apartment building"), the boundaries written in a deed are regarded as imprecise, and the buyer acquires only one apartment.<br />
<br />
Therefore, it is recommended that the seller write some clause such as "I am not retaining anything for myself in this transaction," because with it, the seller relinquishes his possible claim that the boundaries he drew were imprecise.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Albrecht Durer on the Balcony of his House by William Bell Scott</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/63.txt
<a id="src-00244"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/63.txt`

Bava Batra 63 – No Unnecessary Terms in Legal Documents (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiWrhaY1rLddTJqEWnqdC-jLUOA5EVSv4rB3dD39MLMjjb-oSd_s-SDwTOGBi8vXrDQ2-fyAD3Ogg9pfX6n3zhxjTKQYIFmcio1seDXRsnstbb0ocU0dN7SSTtxH0YjPn_0OMfO6F_Gfug/s1600-h/Constantin+Hansen+-+View+over+Roman+Rooftops+-+Udsigt+over+Roms+tage.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiWrhaY1rLddTJqEWnqdC-jLUOA5EVSv4rB3dD39MLMjjb-oSd_s-SDwTOGBi8vXrDQ2-fyAD3Ogg9pfX6n3zhxjTKQYIFmcio1seDXRsnstbb0ocU0dN7SSTtxH0YjPn_0OMfO6F_Gfug/s320/Constantin+Hansen+-+View+over+Roman+Rooftops+-+Udsigt+over+Roms+tage.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an ineffectual clause appears in a legal document, it is reinterpreted in such a way that it is effectual.<br />
<br />
For example, if one sells a house to his fellow and says to him, "I am selling you this house with the stipulation that the fenced rooftop is mine" - the fenced rooftop is his. The clause "rooftop is mine" is redundant. It is already his, as <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/10/bava-batra-60-when-one-buys-house.html">we have learned before</a>. Therefore, this clause is reinterpreted to give him additional rights.<br />
<br />
Exactly which rights he gets is subject to a dispute: he may project beams from the roof into the adjacent yard, or he may rebuild it if it collapses, with the second view prevailing.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: View over Roman Rooftops by Constantin Hansen</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/64.txt
<a id="src-00245"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/64.txt`

Bava Batra 64 – Does the Seller Sell with a Generous or a Stingy Attitude? (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXyuLaAy8ouH5ZquS1Ca4AP_tFOMb8cPHt9EXUgvXwLUejVBJjlr7g4Ip3y-vYoKb1VFS-0bqogk5gVmvt9lEQMi8hTAwVVMt6s3FuxbIqmvGAh0-gzLi-_iXToeeg2g7DBS9tAONBB3M/s1600-h/+Jean-Baptiste-Simeon+Chardin+-+Woman+Drawing+Water+From+A+Copper+Cistern.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXyuLaAy8ouH5ZquS1Ca4AP_tFOMb8cPHt9EXUgvXwLUejVBJjlr7g4Ip3y-vYoKb1VFS-0bqogk5gVmvt9lEQMi8hTAwVVMt6s3FuxbIqmvGAh0-gzLi-_iXToeeg2g7DBS9tAONBB3M/s320/+Jean-Baptiste-Simeon+Chardin+-+Woman+Drawing+Water+From+A+Copper+Cistern.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one sold a house to his fellow, neither the house's pit nor its cistern (dug into the ground and used as water reservoirs) is included in the sale, even if the seller wrote in the deed, "I am selling the depth and height of the house." <br />
<br />
However, to get to the cistern, the seller has to purchase the right-of-way from the buyer, in the opinion of Rabbi Akiva. According to him, the typical inclination of one who sells something is to transfer it fully and generously without reserving anything for himself. In this case, he also transferred the right of way by not saying anything. The Sages disagree and say that typically, the seller wants to sell no more than he has to, retaining the right to pass through the house to reach the cistern.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Woman Drawing Water from a Copper Cistern by Jean Baptiste Simeon Chardin</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/65.txt
<a id="src-00246"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/65.txt`

Bava Batra 65 – The Bigger the Property Sold, the More is Included with it (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLMKIu82TzxMt5BYWb6-x4WorpN0gtyeHhmwrh_-1EJLzCwl9FdICY0AcmFfLHTun5uX5_-8JJxfbFzTgQdvrVCuPAaluzPaxbjF7Ja1-tzZEeaQcrq7BDEuYiKPi3hTwznMW-X8u2T3I/s1600-h/Marc+Chagall+The+Marketplace,+Vitebsk,+1917.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLMKIu82TzxMt5BYWb6-x4WorpN0gtyeHhmwrh_-1EJLzCwl9FdICY0AcmFfLHTun5uX5_-8JJxfbFzTgQdvrVCuPAaluzPaxbjF7Ja1-tzZEeaQcrq7BDEuYiKPi3hTwznMW-X8u2T3I/s320/Marc+Chagall+The+Marketplace,+Vitebsk,+1917.jpg" /></a>
</div><span style="font-size: medium;">In the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/10/bava-batra-64-does-seller-sell-with.html">discussion about the seller's attitude being generous or stingy</a>, the law follows Rabbi Nachman, who said that the seller sells generously. Rav Nachman was close to the Exilarch, the Jewish ruler of Babylonia, and observed many judges and court cases, so he knew which view was followed in practice.<br />
<br />
One who sold a house without specifying what was included in the sale has sold the attached mortar, not the movable mortar, nor the movable oven or stove. If the seller said, "I am selling the house and all contained therein," all movable objects are sold – but not the easily movable objects (carried away). Even easily movable objects are sold if one sells a courtyard with everything therein. If one sells a town, even his animals therein are included.<br />
<br />Art: The Marketplace, Vitebsk by Marc Chagall<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/66.txt
<a id="src-00247"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/66.txt`

Bava Batra 66 – A Mortar that was Carved then Attached to the Ground (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiwCpzjjFcnTGRvJzHyVnV90xQ5N29sBjvszsKn_L-_lrrNQC1g8ZA8TgKw93pwDz6_CM0Z90ogv-ZrpjzGQlM0aJJVQudj3nCrKEgez8JE9YPwN5DvWbMPmosm6QplGMSdaQ1KQOIThvY/s1600-h/Stoopa.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiwCpzjjFcnTGRvJzHyVnV90xQ5N29sBjvszsKn_L-_lrrNQC1g8ZA8TgKw93pwDz6_CM0Z90ogv-ZrpjzGQlM0aJJVQudj3nCrKEgez8JE9YPwN5DvWbMPmosm6QplGMSdaQ1KQOIThvY/s320/Stoopa.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who sells a house has sold the mortar – if that mortar was carved in a stone that formed part of the house's wall. However, if the mortar was made from an unattached piece of wood or stone and then attached to the ground, such mortar is not included in the sale.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Eliezer says, "Anything attached to the ground is considered the ground. Therefore, he has sold the mortar."<br />
<br />
What would the Sages say regarding food placed on this mortar if the mortar is ritually impure? Is it part of the house and thus part of the ground for ritual laws, even if not for commerce, and then the food is pure, or is the mortar not part of the ground for both selling and ritual, and the food is impure? - This remains unresolved.<br />
<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Utensils of Baba Yago From Russian Fairy Tales</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/67.txt
<a id="src-00248"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/67.txt`

Bava Batra 67 – One Sells an Olive Press (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhtxVu2_OltM_8HY1KZ08TsOsW8ALKGpa70-14i4b0FZ1cjbkweTEhyzlEA1wgHH6qZ-3WDXjn2lSR-Elv7trKTCaZaFRT8NYuPfH_QUUY4QKyCpMW4pXMiiMQu1Ilj9AaUux0_gjsQWrY/s1600-h/The-Production-Of-Olive-Oil,-Plate-13-From-Nova-Reperta-New-Discoveries-Engraved-By-Philip-Galle-1537-1612-C.1600.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhtxVu2_OltM_8HY1KZ08TsOsW8ALKGpa70-14i4b0FZ1cjbkweTEhyzlEA1wgHH6qZ-3WDXjn2lSR-Elv7trKTCaZaFRT8NYuPfH_QUUY4QKyCpMW4pXMiiMQu1Ilj9AaUux0_gjsQWrY/s320/The-Production-Of-Olive-Oil,-Plate-13-From-Nova-Reperta-New-Discoveries-Engraved-By-Philip-Galle-1537-1612-C.1600.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The building of an olive press was generally made solely for that purpose. Hence, the sale of this building includes all non-movable items used in the pressing process. <br />
<br />
One who sells the house of an olive press without specifying what is included in the sale has sold the vat, the crusher (used to pre-soften olives), and the "maidens." These items are automatically sold with the press because they are attached to the building where the press is housed.<br />
<br />
However, he has not sold the boards, the wheel, or the beam. These items are excluded from sale because they are not attached to the building.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">If he said, "I am selling you the house of the olive press and all that is contained therein," he has sold all of these items - but not unrelated items that are merely stored in the house.</span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Production of Oil by Philip Galle, engraving<br /></span><div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: medium;"></span></div><span style="font-size: medium;">
<br />
<br />
<br />
</span></div></div>

### content/bava_batra/68.txt
<a id="src-00249"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/68.txt`

Bava Batra 68 – One Sells a Town (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhmXpACgsegfFobFdOVS88J6w671v-RYQus36T6Kdd-PQ-_Oxvidvbc6v4C8Oydmuvs6Sg636i8a3Fg8g31-6O1RNtWXtv8khNRS7GsH6_Z3iuGJlUgCsIs2ZQ10ibKdd0vUaVBHB7r8Ds/s1600-h/Willem+Koekkoek+-+Figures+in+a+Dutch+Street.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhmXpACgsegfFobFdOVS88J6w671v-RYQus36T6Kdd-PQ-_Oxvidvbc6v4C8Oydmuvs6Sg636i8a3Fg8g31-6O1RNtWXtv8khNRS7GsH6_Z3iuGJlUgCsIs2ZQ10ibKdd0vUaVBHB7r8Ds/s320/Willem+Koekkoek+-+Figures+in+a+Dutch+Street.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who sells a town without specifying what is included in the sale has sold the houses, pits, ditches, vaults, bathhouses, dovecotes, and olive presses. Still, he has not sold the movable property in town, such as household implements and food, because he plans to take these with him.<br />
<br />
However, if he said, "I am selling you the town and all that is contained therein," then even if there were animals and slaves in the town at the time of the sale, they are sold along with the town.<br />
<br />
Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel says, "He has sold even the <i>santer</i>." What a santer is&nbsp;is a matter of dispute: either a town clerk, a slave owned by the city who kept information on boundaries and ownership of properties, or the fields that immediately surround the city.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Figures in a Dutch Street by Willem Koekkeok</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/69.txt
<a id="src-00250"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/69.txt`

Bava Batra 69 – Sale of a Field (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-g-Gjy23XpsFxN5fQp3JOnHlcFCI-W7mlcPfz4LfnQpfXseW5KkAj3vxSxG9e_vESFZy3LeF-dX0JnsQ1iQ_iOgdVM7QfohCwCbs7WZOGuGNZ0VEECIZUqsglpkihw-xYgVi5FlGWXpo/s1600-h/Camille+Pissarro+-+Bountiful+Harvest,+1893.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-g-Gjy23XpsFxN5fQp3JOnHlcFCI-W7mlcPfz4LfnQpfXseW5KkAj3vxSxG9e_vESFZy3LeF-dX0JnsQ1iQ_iOgdVM7QfohCwCbs7WZOGuGNZ0VEECIZUqsglpkihw-xYgVi5FlGWXpo/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Bountiful+Harvest,+1893.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who sells a field without specifying what is included in the sale has sold the stones for the use of the field, such as to hold the harvested sheaves. He has also sold the reeds in the vineyard inside that field, used to support the vines. He has sold produce attached to the ground, even if it is ready to be cut. He has sold the carob tree that has not been grafted and the virgin sycamore (planetree) that has not been pruned. All these items either serve the field or aren't significant in their own right.<br />
<br />
If he said, "I am selling you the field and all that is contained therein," he also sold cut harvest. Even so, he has not sold independent items, such as a pruned sycamore tree and a sturdy watchman's hut.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Bountiful Harvest by Camille Pissarro</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/7.txt
<a id="src-00251"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/7.txt`

Bava Batra 7 – Community-Enforceable Obligations (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjBwNfRrFBPEEnrm-vIvhiJXeHpPIgjbIjO9I7Ngb3nQee6MuuqLtwBGtD8LUDZ11UYA-OvaSEGe6N44EzBVi18QuzBRAHYx1xoCLQhhcwrnTA_1wbSMJlhrtyc0RwQmUGS1lZngq9wJntz/s1600-h/Guglielmo+Ciardi+-+At+The+Gateway.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5375105269038543858" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjBwNfRrFBPEEnrm-vIvhiJXeHpPIgjbIjO9I7Ngb3nQee6MuuqLtwBGtD8LUDZ11UYA-OvaSEGe6N44EzBVi18QuzBRAHYx1xoCLQhhcwrnTA_1wbSMJlhrtyc0RwQmUGS1lZngq9wJntz/s320/Guglielmo+Ciardi+-+At+The+Gateway.JPG" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 261px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">One whose home adjoins a common courtyard is obligated to contribute toward maintaining the privacy and security of this courtyard. If he is unwilling, he may be compelled to help build a gatehouse and a door for the courtyard.<br /><br />A gatekeeper would sit in the shade of the gatehouse and prevent passersby on the public road from gazing into the courtyard. The door was used to keep outsiders from actually entering the courtyard.<br /><br />How long must one be in the city to be treated like one of the city's citizens? - 12 months. But if he bought a house, he is immediately treated like one of the citizens.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: At the Gateway by Guglielmo Ciardi</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/70.txt
<a id="src-00252"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/70.txt`

Bava Batra 70 – Returning a Deposit (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhAXbe78PphpsifNe3kWgjkppAeRd4WTqT0F38RyfU74mazQE20NtpjItGSBeB9YkHEP3a3BekjXiEkeZhsoGYB40wqcIdeJTjTYc0lu6CoA5cqpN6ym3bwKzg4Bi1H5U13fyAdai4bWjA/s1600-h/Henry+Nelson+O%27Neil+-+Portrait+of+Henry+Pelham-Clinton+Holding+a+Document+in+His+Study+1850.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhAXbe78PphpsifNe3kWgjkppAeRd4WTqT0F38RyfU74mazQE20NtpjItGSBeB9YkHEP3a3BekjXiEkeZhsoGYB40wqcIdeJTjTYc0lu6CoA5cqpN6ym3bwKzg4Bi1H5U13fyAdai4bWjA/s320/Henry+Nelson+O%27Neil+-+Portrait+of+Henry+Pelham-Clinton+Holding+a+Document+in+His+Study+1850.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">It has been established that <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra45.html" target="_blank">one who accepts a deposit in the presence of witnesses is not required to return it in the presence of witnesses</a>. <br />
<br />
What is the rule if one records making his deposit in a document, and then the custodian tells him, "I have already returned it to you?" Do we say that if the custodian wished to lie, he could have stated that the deposit suffered an unavoidable mishap, in which case he would have been believed? Therefore, we believe him based on the "why would he lie?" argument?<br />
<br />
Or can the depositor ask, "Then why do I have this document in my hands?" "Why would he lie?" is not applicable?<br />
<br />
Perhaps the custodian retrieved the document because he knew that he could claim an unavoidable mishap and would be believed. Therefore, he is believed now.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Portrait of Henry Pelham Clinton Holding a Document by Henry Nelson O'Neil</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/71.txt
<a id="src-00253"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/71.txt`

Bava Batra 71 – Sale, Gift, Consecration (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjOx3QW9Ow97PyMrU4E7X9rCnwJ1Tn_zGlQrlDkqq523bz-BjEPNnHmM0fz2T1E0RFmUyOSVrx8wnhig1XKETQgc2hg4riwvN4z2XksL-WiQ8TAT7jpn8PQWaePLgZyzJS5YiVFWyZwSww/s1600-h/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Pressing+the+Grapes+-+Florentine+Wine+Cellar.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjOx3QW9Ow97PyMrU4E7X9rCnwJ1Tn_zGlQrlDkqq523bz-BjEPNnHmM0fz2T1E0RFmUyOSVrx8wnhig1XKETQgc2hg4riwvN4z2XksL-WiQ8TAT7jpn8PQWaePLgZyzJS5YiVFWyZwSww/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Pressing+the+Grapes+-+Florentine+Wine+Cellar.jpg" /></a>
</div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who sells a field without specifying what is included in the sale has not sold the water pit, the wine press, and the dovecote in this field because these are separate properties in their own right. Those items are not included in the sale, even if they are in disuse at the time of the sale.<br />
<br />
When one gives the primary item as a gift, he gives it all, even items not included in the case of sale. A gift recipient is embarrassed to ask about details, and it is on the giver to withhold any items he wants to keep.<br />
<br />
One who consecrates a field is generous like a giver. Rabbi Shimon says he is like a seller.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Pressing the Grapes - Florentine Wine Celler by John Singer Sargent</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/72.txt
<a id="src-00254"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/72.txt`

Bava Batra 72 – Consecration According to Rabbi Shimon (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-Nsr2ZZF1y5KznHPqjOZc0onl5EwxrcDT5jMCj8VamqfeO8i21rN-o4f9lFgXf7KKETEUJeVcaqSsVnc1RUtxPtOuUhZGrlLsrZATP9Sc0bJYDPqHgNt4nYYFuH2-bRKJJRNj4FGgYUk/s1600-h/John+Williamson+-+Sycamore,+Catskill+Clove,+Below+Haines+Falls.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-Nsr2ZZF1y5KznHPqjOZc0onl5EwxrcDT5jMCj8VamqfeO8i21rN-o4f9lFgXf7KKETEUJeVcaqSsVnc1RUtxPtOuUhZGrlLsrZATP9Sc0bJYDPqHgNt4nYYFuH2-bRKJJRNj4FGgYUk/s320/John+Williamson+-+Sycamore,+Catskill+Clove,+Below+Haines+Falls.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra71.html" target="_blank">Rabbi Shimon said that the one who consecrates a field is like a seller</a>, his exact words were: "If one consecrates a field, he has not consecrated the pit and the wine press, but the grafted carob tree and cut sycamore (planetree) are included."<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon thinks that one who consecrates is stingy, like a seller, and keeps all he can for himself. Why is then the carob consecrated? He should have kept it, together with the land needed for it!<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon is saying this only for the sake of argument: "I myself say that the trees are not consecrated. You, the Sages, who say that the carob is consecrated, should agree to me that he keeps the pit and the wine press". And the Sages answer: "One consecrates so liberally that even the pit and wine press are included."</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Sycamore, Catskill Clove Below Haines Fall by John Williamson</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/73.txt
<a id="src-00255"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/73.txt`

Bava Batra 73 – Selling a Ship (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjmdyQHHyxqjtR9TYoES_ztT3oHPKJZlBuXakxITPmrG4Aknl_CsXlnLndmlHexrxFlLdMIGJP90WGyyt2hS6XBWMlB39M43jxdKEhyphenhyphenNnj_UOz9PRdO-e7DyzJrHsPs9t0561P28CtxLQQ/s1600-h/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Atlantic+Storm.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjmdyQHHyxqjtR9TYoES_ztT3oHPKJZlBuXakxITPmrG4Aknl_CsXlnLndmlHexrxFlLdMIGJP90WGyyt2hS6XBWMlB39M43jxdKEhyphenhyphenNnj_UOz9PRdO-e7DyzJrHsPs9t0561P28CtxLQQ/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Atlantic+Storm.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who sells a ship without specifying precisely what is included in the sale has sold the mast, the sail, the anchor, and the oars. He has not sold the ship's slaves nor the cargo. If he said, "I am selling the ship and all that is in it,"" - all of these are included.<br />
<br />
Said Rabbah bar bar Channah "Those who go down to sea told me that the wave that sinks a ship appears to have a fringe of white fire at its tip. But when one strikes it with a club upon which the following names of God are engraved, I Shall Be What I Shall Be, Yah, God of Legions, Forever – it subsides."<br />
<br />
He also related, "I saw a frog the size of the city of Akra. A sea monster came and swallowed it, and a female raven swallowed the sea monster. It flew up and sat on the branch of a tree. Come and see how strong that tree was!"<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Atlantic Storm by John Singer Sargent</span></div>

Bava Batra 74 – Stories of Rabbah bar bar Chanah (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgmZqhcGT8SWA6yBK3atPUC_Jogty8Afw4LLSwEZ7ABtTOIXMMe7yLf-C7PiCbKDwfFJMuMmOg_fXIDHwvcpEUKOhhTgkBgALwVES7ZLebvVR9zoI32gkx0eeq-kvEzuSBZ8wPgkDhHXHE/s1600-h/Franz+Marc+-+Donkey+Frieze,+1911.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgmZqhcGT8SWA6yBK3atPUC_Jogty8Afw4LLSwEZ7ABtTOIXMMe7yLf-C7PiCbKDwfFJMuMmOg_fXIDHwvcpEUKOhhTgkBgALwVES7ZLebvVR9zoI32gkx0eeq-kvEzuSBZ8wPgkDhHXHE/s320/Franz+Marc+-+Donkey+Frieze,+1911.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbah bar bar Chana told the following story.<br />
<br />
An Arab merchant told me, "Come, I will show you Mount Sinai." I went and saw that scorpions surrounded it, and they resembled white donkeys. I heard a Heavenly voice saying, "Woe to me (God) that I have sworn to exile My people, and now that I have sworn, who can annul the oath for Me?"<br />
<br />
When Rabbah returned, the Rabbis told him,&nbsp; - Every Abba (his proper name) is a donkey, and every bar bar Chanah is a fool. You ought to have declared, "It is annulled for You."<br />
<br />
And Rabbah, what did he think? That perhaps the Heavenly voice was talking about <a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/8-21.htm">the oath about the Flood</a>. <br />
<br />
And the Rabbis? If so, then why did the Heavenly voice say "Woe is to Me" about something that is for mankind's good?</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Donkey Frieze by Franz Marc<br />
<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/75.txt
<a id="src-00257"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/75.txt`

Bava Batra 75 – Acquiring a Ship (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjM2flZIsphpHYKIld1-aCd0tvSOzCnbjnbHEaEqjnlrSOGNnXlUuYRlu09wWODkjVsc_6qnmVALJkTzAwltUrbd82YZZkwqAjejOS3DM1C66kXxu5RIZEkQmVbU8GswsAsIJkGU-w64YY/s1600-h/Abraham+Willaerts+-+A+Shipowner+and+his+Family,+1650.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjM2flZIsphpHYKIld1-aCd0tvSOzCnbjnbHEaEqjnlrSOGNnXlUuYRlu09wWODkjVsc_6qnmVALJkTzAwltUrbd82YZZkwqAjejOS3DM1C66kXxu5RIZEkQmVbU8GswsAsIJkGU-w64YY/s320/Abraham+Willaerts+-+A+Shipowner+and+his+Family,+1650.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">What proprietary act effects the acquisition of a ship? Rav says, "Once the buyer has pulled the ship even a small distance, he has acquired it." But Shmuel says, "He has not acquired the ship until he pulls it away completely from the place it originally occupied."<br />
<br />
Is this the same disagreement as the two views on acquiring an animal by pulling: (1) the animal is acquired when it raises the front and hind leg, or (2) only when it walks its entire length?<br />
<br />
No, it is not the same! Once the animal starts to move, it will move the other two legs, but the ship may stop after the initial push. On the other hand, once a ship is moved, it moves as a whole, whereas an animal can put its legs back. The two disagreements are different, and both had to be recorded.<br />
<br />Art: A Shipowner and His Family by Abraham Wiillaerts<br />
<br />
</span>

---

<a id="src-00258"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/76.txt`

Bava Batra 76 – Acquiring a Ship: Control It, Pull It, or Lift It? (Civil)
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgTQfRRJ06ei1lWtyoh3viRujQJ4S5u9TPTimrkdnYBHSRrIiRD1vEAc9u_6MH2FKUBZClDJSBUF_M8MwzkvULFzIpjDdE1_LcXNeBpWhwHY5gZRf8ngyqbQiwet1CkNkFhcu43vomQ9S8/s1600-h/William+Anderson+-+A+Shore+Scene+with+Windmills+and+Shipping.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgTQfRRJ06ei1lWtyoh3viRujQJ4S5u9TPTimrkdnYBHSRrIiRD1vEAc9u_6MH2FKUBZClDJSBUF_M8MwzkvULFzIpjDdE1_LcXNeBpWhwHY5gZRf8ngyqbQiwet1CkNkFhcu43vomQ9S8/s320/William+Anderson+-+A+Shore+Scene+with+Windmills+and+Shipping.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">By (Torah) law, when one pays money, he acquires the object. The Sages, however, established that movable objects should be acquired by lifting, pulling into one's domain, or taking control over them. All the time that the buyer has not taken the delivery of his purchase, the seller, who already got paid, may not be careful to protect it. If, however, the object is still the seller's until delivery, he will be careful.<br />
<br />
If the ship is on public grounds, one cannot pull it into his domain; therefore, the seller can give control over it to the buyer. If the ship is in an area people can use as their own, the buyer should pull the ship into his domain. If the ship is not afloat, one can lift it or rent the area under it.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Shore Scene with Windmills and Shipping by William Anderson<br />
<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/77.txt
<a id="src-00259"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/77.txt`

Bava Batra 77 – Sale of a Debt Obligation
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvsVwz4PRAhEOUJXS5LSCfP62WXoWLvpQgL9jPaFBBFcqdHILsu8KDxyI7lQcwRJIJHj6-p7ADiGv4RLoj-Oi5LSPBrAWEHgudKxu14UAMZdqvBCNpNPDbmsysBMqQCovvd2mKMy7Y7vc/s1600-h/Rosa+Bonheur+-+Oxen+Pulling+a+Cart.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvsVwz4PRAhEOUJXS5LSCfP62WXoWLvpQgL9jPaFBBFcqdHILsu8KDxyI7lQcwRJIJHj6-p7ADiGv4RLoj-Oi5LSPBrAWEHgudKxu14UAMZdqvBCNpNPDbmsysBMqQCovvd2mKMy7Y7vc/s320/Rosa+Bonheur+-+Oxen+Pulling+a+Cart.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who sells a note of indebtedness to his fellow must write for him a document of sale that states, "Acquire the promissory note and whatever lien is in it." If he does not do so, the buyer acquires only the paper on which it is written for use, such as a bottle stopper. The sale would then become void because of the law against overcharge.<br />
<br />
If one says to his fellow, "Sell me this yoke for 200 <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zuz_%28Jewish_coin%29">zuz</a>," then it is evident that the yoke alone is not sold for this amount, and thus, the oxen are included. But the Sages say," The purchase price is no proof." It may be viewed as a gratuity that the buyer gives to the seller or an overpayment, in which case the sale would be voidable.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Oxen Pulling a Cart by Rosa Bonheur&nbsp;<br />
<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/78.txt
<a id="src-00260"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/78.txt`

Bava Batra 78 – Selling a Donkey
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiupZVJ1udGTKkXZkNyhnEmrR8ebECK3OI5_YtC1y122_IZft0ZN6HDx-dxSvnARX3sPn8spg2iO4qWS7M1ZOeiFOFOqf1IV84E74_3VtKiCr2v_oMvOG77l-yygdwsMAGD2h36RkbQkvg/s1600-h/Giovanni+Fattori+-+Nun+with+donkey.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiupZVJ1udGTKkXZkNyhnEmrR8ebECK3OI5_YtC1y122_IZft0ZN6HDx-dxSvnARX3sPn8spg2iO4qWS7M1ZOeiFOFOqf1IV84E74_3VtKiCr2v_oMvOG77l-yygdwsMAGD2h36RkbQkvg/s320/Giovanni+Fattori+-+Nun+with+donkey.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one sells a donkey to his fellow, he has not sold its gear. However, Nachum the Mede says he has sold his gear, too. <br />
<br />
All agree that the saddle, blanket, girth under the donkey's belly, and breast strap are sold. These are necessary for the use of the donkey. The argument is about the sack and saddlebag, specifically cargo gear. The first teacher holds that ordinarily, a donkey is used for riding, and the cargo gear is not included in the sale. Nachum holds that ordinarily, a donkey is used for transporting cargo; therefore, its cargo gear is included in the sale.<br />
<br />
Is the argument about the gear that is on the donkey or the gear that is not? This question remains unresolved, and the one who wants to extract money from his fellow needs to prove his right.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div>Art: Nun with Donkey by Giovanni Fattori</div>

---

### content/bava_batra/79.txt
<a id="src-00261"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/79.txt`

Bava Batra 79 – Selling a Donkey and its Foal
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgOvTSxAGt1Zf1xADUdHhByrV-QV0PMz5gqvr2lnOU1C9AIMHHT-VWsjSWsbjgfwkRZmZPM13Bz03LglYE9xCXrgYCQ7fIz4HK9fd9_uewWR84hQ48Cr-ZlGOJajU9JS0_f8uKskFn-Pss/s1600-h/Sergei+Ivanovich+Svetoslavsky+-+A+Spring+Day,+or+Beehives,+1899.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgOvTSxAGt1Zf1xADUdHhByrV-QV0PMz5gqvr2lnOU1C9AIMHHT-VWsjSWsbjgfwkRZmZPM13Bz03LglYE9xCXrgYCQ7fIz4HK9fd9_uewWR84hQ48Cr-ZlGOJajU9JS0_f8uKskFn-Pss/s320/Sergei+Ivanovich+Svetoslavsky+-+A+Spring+Day,+or+Beehives,+1899.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who sells a donkey has sold its foal, but if one sells a cow, he has not sold its calf. If one sells a dump, he has sold its manure. If one sells a pit, he has sold its waters. If one sells a beehive, he has sold the bees. If one sells a dovecote, he has sold the doves. In all these cases, the contents are considered subsidiary to and are sold along with the primary item that contains them.<br />
<br />
Why is a donkey different from a cow? In this case, he said, "I am selling you a nursing donkey." For the cow, this may be interpreted as buying the cow for its milk, but the non-kosher milk of a donkey is useless to the buyer, and therefore the "nursing" adds its foal to the sale.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Spring Day, or Beehives by Sergey Ivanovich Svetoslavsky</span></div>

---

Bava Batra 8 – Feeding the Unlearned (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiQpZm7jdPFxtxC7kbAKEcNLo2rZeqc6k2_PX1wfzoEMXlBWpIHKffZZ0sf5SIZlfBvu_p_QwSmRmUKIAuAuP_j1K9OudQegyt8n9JFP2e7V7SVEke0luPNownRSpsegTSJalnKRfjTdJpr/s1600-h/Charles+Perrandeau+-+Waiting+in+the+Clinic,+1888.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5375627642092342306" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiQpZm7jdPFxtxC7kbAKEcNLo2rZeqc6k2_PX1wfzoEMXlBWpIHKffZZ0sf5SIZlfBvu_p_QwSmRmUKIAuAuP_j1K9OudQegyt8n9JFP2e7V7SVEke0luPNownRSpsegTSJalnKRfjTdJpr/s320/Charles+Perrandeau+-+Waiting+in+the+Clinic,+1888.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 236px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">Rabbi Yehudah the Prince opened food storehouses to feed the poor during famine. However, he said that only the students of the Torah may enter and take food, but not unlearned folk, since he held that misfortunes come to the world only because of the unlearned people.<br /><br />His disciple, Rabbi Yonatan ben Amram, disguised himself and pushed his way in:<br /><br />- Master, please sustain me.<br />- My son, are you a student of the Torah or related areas?<br />- No.<br />- If so, on what merit shall I sustain you?<br />- Sustain me as you would a dog or  a raven.<br /><br />Rabbi Yehudah relented but later became distressed. His son Rabbi Shimon said, "Perhaps this is Rabbi Yonatan, who did not wish to benefit from his Torah." They found this was so, and Rabbi Yehudah announced, "Let everyone enter."</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Waiting in the Clinic by Charles Perrandeau</span></div>

### content/bava_batra/80.txt
<a id="src-00263"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/80.txt`

Bava Batra 80 – Buying Doves
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3Q4UElP5d0SccfrXMb-btKWcaFDExCcFod4h2vLHAC2q7jEjVm2caZTJcDaR-Qt3_G3JGWNPModwZ0Vx0LYLbKlfPn5ltglNYTcecjKG7ehqKZslv5Jj7yyFh_sEndY7bqA05r6RsFWY/s1600-h/Henry+Weekes+-Three+Ringed+Doves.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3Q4UElP5d0SccfrXMb-btKWcaFDExCcFod4h2vLHAC2q7jEjVm2caZTJcDaR-Qt3_G3JGWNPModwZ0Vx0LYLbKlfPn5ltglNYTcecjKG7ehqKZslv5Jj7yyFh_sEndY7bqA05r6RsFWY/s320/Henry+Weekes+-Three+Ringed+Doves.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one buys the production of a dovecote from his fellow,&nbsp; he must allow the first pair of doves that are produced to fly with the mother – that is, to remain with her; they are not included in the sale.<br />
<br />Doves tend to lay a pair of eggs almost every month of the year. These eggs hatch and produce one male and one female, which themselves begin to mate at the age of two months.<br />
<br />
In order to stay in the dovecote, the mother must have her daughter as a companion in addition to her mate. The daughter, too, must have her offspring as companions since her mother is not company enough. The buyer must, therefore, leave all these pairs and not take them for himself.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Three Ringed Doves by Henry Weekes</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/81.txt
<a id="src-00264"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/81.txt`

Bava Batra 81 – Buying Trees
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh16Bs4yOl2EXH8XKu70YXGrA2AnjWJDY4z3ptCiMWDcUMcsPQZ-k7oy_UXzQznDZv0zdaoqp7k0yikPuyECkVpjaAeCX9usls7i_aoWEyFyFiGw97hRHgnkDMddV3AExkeV6o_cYD_u5g/s1600-h/Corot+-+Park+at+Monsieur+Wall.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh16Bs4yOl2EXH8XKu70YXGrA2AnjWJDY4z3ptCiMWDcUMcsPQZ-k7oy_UXzQznDZv0zdaoqp7k0yikPuyECkVpjaAeCX9usls7i_aoWEyFyFiGw97hRHgnkDMddV3AExkeV6o_cYD_u5g/s320/Corot+-+Park+at+Monsieur+Wall.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If someone purchases two trees in his neighbor's field, he has not acquired any land - he has merely purchased the rights to their produce. Thus, if a tree dies, the buyer takes the dead wood, but he may not plant a tree on that site. Rabbi Meir, however, says that he has acquired land.<br />
<br />
Therefore, if the branches of the trees grow until they extend over the seller's land, the seller may not trim them, even if they block sunlight and thus damage his crops. Since the buyer gets no land, it is understood that the seller pledges his own land to provide for the tree's needs.<br />
<br />
If someone purchases three trees, he has acquired land since he surely intended to buy a field of trees. Therefore, if the branches grow over the seller's land, the seller may trim them.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Part at Monsieur Wall by Corot</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/82.txt
<a id="src-00265"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/82.txt`

Bava Batra 82 – Recitation over First Fruit
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiEWveSLr7We2XrqOLPaUnJuFegxTank8oNZEOvITy0M1jWVza90S-HvWNCeFLkzcc84qCGkOF_xj3k1cRkjrMm0G11Mo1Dr-u0mssXCDiQrEpUREkU4YK7wWlsFOPY41lXNkBxQCfLPg8/s1600-h/Guiseppe+Signorini+-+A+North+African+Fruit+Vendor.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiEWveSLr7We2XrqOLPaUnJuFegxTank8oNZEOvITy0M1jWVza90S-HvWNCeFLkzcc84qCGkOF_xj3k1cRkjrMm0G11Mo1Dr-u0mssXCDiQrEpUREkU4YK7wWlsFOPY41lXNkBxQCfLPg8/s320/Guiseppe+Signorini+-+A+North+African+Fruit+Vendor.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When one buys trees, the question of <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra81.html" target="_blank">whether he owns the land under them</a>&nbsp;is crucial for bringing the&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/09/bava-batra-27-first-fruit-must-be-from.html">first fruit from these trees</a>. <br />
<br />
If he owns the land, he also recites&nbsp;<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/26-3.htm">the prescribed verses</a>, thanking God for the Land He gave him. If he does not own the land, he brings the first fruit but cannot recite the verses. Why not? One should be allowed to recite Torah verses!&nbsp; - Either because his words "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/26-3.htm">the Land that You gave me</a>" will appear false, or because he may regard his fruit as definite first fruit, and because of that neglect his tithe obligations.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A North African Fruit Vendor by Guiseppe Signorini</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/83.txt
<a id="src-00266"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/83.txt`

Bava Batra 83 – Four Types of Errors in Sales
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiouty6rTsXg9PuZaroXw6wZn5ud8ZLWHV2RYmFv2FyUqaNH9qIJ55ObGJOakreN9Hu08QwN4_ByzM-6FC_tYjDWbHgJIMTppYsns5kArZ5hXFxWwy-8AGDutOKtmfW_oIUd4TrN4-C_hw/s1600-h/Christian+Krohg+-+Woman+Cutting+Bread.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiouty6rTsXg9PuZaroXw6wZn5ud8ZLWHV2RYmFv2FyUqaNH9qIJ55ObGJOakreN9Hu08QwN4_ByzM-6FC_tYjDWbHgJIMTppYsns5kArZ5hXFxWwy-8AGDutOKtmfW_oIUd4TrN4-C_hw/s320/Christian+Krohg+-+Woman+Cutting+Bread.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the seller sold what was purported to be superior wheat and it was found to be inferior, the buyer can retract. The seller might also want to void the sale if the price rises, but he does not have this option. It is not a fraudulent sale, where both can retract. Rather, it is more akin to a case of price fraud or overcharge&nbsp;since the buyer did receive wheat, albeit of inferior quality.<br />
<br />
Similarly, if he sold him inferior wheat, and it was found to be superior, the seller can retract.<br />
<br />
The "red" wheat is reddened by the sun, and it produces more flour, while the "white" wheat yields superior bread. If one agreed to sell red wheat and it was found to be white, or vice versa, both can retract.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Woman Cutting Bread by Christian Krohg</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/84.txt
<a id="src-00267"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/84.txt`

Bava Batra 84 – Buying a Pile of Produce
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjp3fykDW_5Z9Z0_g6-B5FkIR9mU5rur_QuS5WdJkmau46mqv-K4PK3SNdJ0BRUlhza_Q2sDHpZxvFiGA4ZzEooFNBvxqqoj3v9x7_d2zXShfjN6wz_zjxDTuJ2iy0_iDuL0oRK6QLAvoo/s1600-h/Carl+Larsson+-+The+Threshing+of+the+grain.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjp3fykDW_5Z9Z0_g6-B5FkIR9mU5rur_QuS5WdJkmau46mqv-K4PK3SNdJ0BRUlhza_Q2sDHpZxvFiGA4ZzEooFNBvxqqoj3v9x7_d2zXShfjN6wz_zjxDTuJ2iy0_iDuL0oRK6QLAvoo/s320/Carl+Larsson+-+The+Threshing+of+the+grain.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Suppose one sells produce to his fellow at an agreed-upon price. In that case, the seller agrees to sell a pile of produce to the buyer at such-and-such price per measure, and the buyer agrees to take it all and pay whatever the total comes to if the buyer pulls the produce to himself, even though he did not measure it; he acquired it. Since the price has been agreed upon, the measurement serves only to calculate the total amount of money owed.<br />
<br />
If he only measured it, he did not acquire it. However, this refers only to the seller. If the buyer measured it, his act of measurement would constitute lifting, the best possible way of formalizing acquisition, in which case he would have acquired it even without pulling it to himself.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Threshing of the Grain by Carl Larsson</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/85.txt
<a id="src-00268"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/85.txt`

Bava Batra 85 – One's Container Formalizes Acquisition
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg-w2C5WumscNsimgBZrDT35mLJwJ-ZvUWHGfr3gqwSS9HDnswFB5pjkZkDVraIj2NurZq5I5DomWjhRvXXr6iN6PHk2IE8DjOJPdp0n0fN9DeInGOc9OI2EcAHBD5L4UMFF2PynecnJ9E/s1600-h/Gustave+Courbet+-+The+Grain+Sifters.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg-w2C5WumscNsimgBZrDT35mLJwJ-ZvUWHGfr3gqwSS9HDnswFB5pjkZkDVraIj2NurZq5I5DomWjhRvXXr6iN6PHk2IE8DjOJPdp0n0fN9DeInGOc9OI2EcAHBD5L4UMFF2PynecnJ9E/s320/Gustave+Courbet+-+The+Grain+Sifters.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav and Shmuel both said, "A person's container can formalize acquisition for him in any place – except in the public domain." Rabbi Yochanan and Resh Lakish both said, "Even in the public domain."<br />
<br />
A person's </span><span style="font-size: medium;">container</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> can act as his courtyard to acquire items placed in it, provided that the </span><span style="font-size: medium;">container</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> is placed in a domain where the&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: medium;">owner has the right to place it. Thus, a buyer can acquire items in the seller's domain by placing them in his </span><span style="font-size: medium;">container</span><span style="font-size: medium;">, provided that the seller gives him the right to place the </span><span style="font-size: medium;">container</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> there. One can also place </span><span style="font-size: medium;">containers</span><span style="font-size: medium;"> in the public domain—but not keep them there permanently.<br />
<br />
However, they don't argue. The first ruling concerns a public thoroughfare, and the second concerns the quiet, recessed area of the public domain, to which people step to discuss business.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Grain Sifters by Gustave Courbet<br />
<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/86.txt
<a id="src-00269"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/86.txt`

Bava Batra 86 – Pulling is Ineffective if Lifting is Possible
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiHF0U6LPsThe_RHOo2NaezuUOVbtNT3pcKX-mW9RBUkhC-f20MykwZWGtbPBNVHNw1HX7i6TwTY1PYoJp0YNAtT6oEYe52eTUiHZmSkfDUPSCvkijC8BJ3TvYAjTJKWUq_5cQf9NGcmXE/s1600-h/+Winslow+Homer+-+Pulling+The+Dory.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiHF0U6LPsThe_RHOo2NaezuUOVbtNT3pcKX-mW9RBUkhC-f20MykwZWGtbPBNVHNw1HX7i6TwTY1PYoJp0YNAtT6oEYe52eTUiHZmSkfDUPSCvkijC8BJ3TvYAjTJKWUq_5cQf9NGcmXE/s320/+Winslow+Homer+-+Pulling+The+Dory.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">As we have <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/11/kiddushin-26-ways-of-acquisition.html">learned elsewhere</a>, movable items can be formally acquired by pulling them into the buyer's domain. However, this is only true for items that are generally not lifted. Items that are usually lifted can't be acquired by pulling at all.<br />
<br />
But is that true? Consider the following case: one who steals a bag of money on Shabbat by pulling it out of the house is not liable to pay since he is liable with his life for carrying on Shabbat. We see that he acquires the bag by pulling it, even though usually, money bags are lifted! <br />
<br />
Rebuttal: You know what we are dealing with here? A bag that's too big to be lifted. Therefore, the rule stands, and pulling is usually ineffective as a method of acquisition if lifting is possible.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Pulling a Dory by Winslow Homer</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/87.txt
<a id="src-00270"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/87.txt`

Bava Batra 87 – Selling Wine or Oil
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEishY7nv-b5eHu5a1hPdsg2FvLmf9i5YQ-NC3ns04FZYXrCU6y-8DmGYPL7OhI7y9pUWZjYoMldyTsrNyi5oACRJTZjCCXMuBxuBHL6EcUjB5eQc0iR7X54iVybihCuLwaciHmLamc6SEI/s1600/Paul+Cezanne+-+Still+Life+Post+Bottle+Cup+And+Fruit.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEishY7nv-b5eHu5a1hPdsg2FvLmf9i5YQ-NC3ns04FZYXrCU6y-8DmGYPL7OhI7y9pUWZjYoMldyTsrNyi5oACRJTZjCCXMuBxuBHL6EcUjB5eQc0iR7X54iVybihCuLwaciHmLamc6SEI/s320/Paul+Cezanne+-+Still+Life+Post+Bottle+Cup+And+Fruit.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one was selling wine or oil to his fellow, and after the price was fixed, the merchandise appreciated or depreciated, who stands to gain or lose? <br />
<br />
If the price changed before the measuring vessel was complete, it changed for the seller. If the price increases, the seller can retract and insist on a higher price. If it fell, the buyer can retract and hold out for a lower price. Once the measure is filled, the buyer acquires the merchandise, and the deal is final. <br />
<br />
But how can this ruling be true? If the container belongs to the seller, he owns the merchandise until the buyer takes delivery. And if it belongs to the buyer, he acquires every measure as it is poured in. The answer is that the container belongs to a middleman, who loans it to the seller while filling it, then loans it to the buyer after it's full.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Still Life - Post, Bottle, Cup, and Fruit by Paul Cezanne</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/88.txt
<a id="src-00271"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/88.txt`

Bava Batra 88 – Just Weights
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0tMvqaQ5dEChJwfdcVBgTDTe6CDLgLAvIFGE-y2kSDvNA7vxszyzMaQndPIpNCSqRFT_seL88EZZZCAY6KJeQ-mLf3ETThaQhlKjS6Ej3EFl5HSP2JTBKmYvtO6GOx5lh8yk0Q2JR8Z0/s1600/Quiringh+Gerritsz+van+Brekelenkam+-+An+Old+Man+Weighing+Gold+1667.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0tMvqaQ5dEChJwfdcVBgTDTe6CDLgLAvIFGE-y2kSDvNA7vxszyzMaQndPIpNCSqRFT_seL88EZZZCAY6KJeQ-mLf3ETThaQhlKjS6Ej3EFl5HSP2JTBKmYvtO6GOx5lh8yk0Q2JR8Z0/s320/Quiringh+Gerritsz+van+Brekelenkam+-+An+Old+Man+Weighing+Gold+1667.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A wholesaler must wipe his measures clean once every thirty days and a householder once every twelve months. This law applies to measures used for liquids that leave a residue, such as wine or oil. Since the residue tends to settle in the measure and congeal, the measure must be cleaned periodically. Since a wholesaler sells frequently, his measure tends to gather residue more quickly.<br />
<br />
Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel says that the opposite is true. Since the wholesaler uses the measure more frequently, the residue that gathers in it does not congeal between uses. Therefore, the wholesaler must wipe his measures once every twelve months and a householder – once every thirty days.<br />
<br />
The phrase “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/25-15.htm">A perfect and just weight you shall have</a>...” also teaches that the seller must act justly and give the buyer a little extra.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: An Old Man Weighing Gold by Quiringh Gerritsz van Brekelenkam<br />
<br />
<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/89.txt
<a id="src-00272"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/89.txt`

Bava Batra 89 – Honest Measures
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXP9WdyCFqJ3AWCGvuIt1hC3QNfdqXcgHJqCkAyAXfHOQzmJnZj0es1Qn3wAaGcAk2tukaKMi6iZVccqUYNVk9VZ2Q7-OWB76h88GzQovY2wd7YEKHgGlyx_6m_kacacEPohROV_iQw94/s1600/Thomas+Cowperthwait+Eakins+-+The+Courtship.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXP9WdyCFqJ3AWCGvuIt1hC3QNfdqXcgHJqCkAyAXfHOQzmJnZj0es1Qn3wAaGcAk2tukaKMi6iZVccqUYNVk9VZ2Q7-OWB76h88GzQovY2wd7YEKHgGlyx_6m_kacacEPohROV_iQw94/s320/Thomas+Cowperthwait+Eakins+-+The+Courtship.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The punishment for false measures is more severe than that for illicit relationships. Regarding "..<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/18-27.htm">all these</a>..." illicit relationships, a shorter form of "these" - "el" is used, but regarding false measures, "...<a href="http://scripturetext.com/deuteronomy/25-16.htm">all who do these</a>..." a more extended form, "eleh" is used. Why? One cannot remember all those he has cheated and return money to them.<br />
<br />
"<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/25-14.htm">You shall not have false measures in your house</a>..." - why in your house? It is forbidden everywhere! This teaches that "you shall not have in your house" because of false measures.<br />
<br />
In some places, sellers customarily add a little extra to the scale on which the produce is weighted, while in others, they add a little after weighing. Deviating from the prevailing custom is not recommended because it may lead an onlooker to make a mistake in the future.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Courtship by Thomas Cowperthwait Eakins</span></div>

---
