Bava Batra 9 – Importance of Charity (Civil)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhINPVPTY1K2GRBgfTCi3DhDpBIhScqSszYhzIdcjWROHkB0WSP0IhLlu-H5yNfFiI-MoobJaaYOIVKJ1i0AJ67r97c5u__QORujnMzZFUSkT8wZEMyI0-l0tpqqGsAXv6PleWM1Vtqif1F/s1600-h/Robert+Kemm+-+Alms+for+the+Poor.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5375832357433141042" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhINPVPTY1K2GRBgfTCi3DhDpBIhScqSszYhzIdcjWROHkB0WSP0IhLlu-H5yNfFiI-MoobJaaYOIVKJ1i0AJ67r97c5u__QORujnMzZFUSkT8wZEMyI0-l0tpqqGsAXv6PleWM1Vtqif1F/s320/Robert+Kemm+-+Alms+for+the+Poor.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 238px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">What does “<a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/59-17.htm" target="_blank">And He donned charity like a coat of armor</a>...” mean?  Why is charity compared to a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mail_%28armour%29" target="_blank">coat of armor</a>? To tell you that just as each scale combines to form a large coat of armor, so concerning giving charity, each coin combines with all others to comprise a large sum, that is, to be considered as a large gift, reflecting more favorably on the donor.<br /><br />One who gives a small coin to a pauper is <a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/58-7.htm" target="_blank">blessed with six Heavenly blessings</a>, and one who comforts him with words <a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/58-10.htm" target="_blank">gets eleven blessings</a>.<br /></span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Alms for the Poor by Robert Kemm</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/90.txt
<a id="src-00274"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/90.txt`

Bava Batra 90 – Market Distorters
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1fNsWO2CnZpXqdQCc57Vw1Jq7fVAgDxWRYEq0JKkqts0D627RA2gphWBSTS72ktt6BCHZdfFQNqOL2FgUixgsWfIouLc7nNQT72rERzwf8EmI0kqy0aQszMXffIYhIgRZJXJvA100W2g/s1600/Albert+Chevallier+Tayler+-+A+Day+at+the+Market.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1fNsWO2CnZpXqdQCc57Vw1Jq7fVAgDxWRYEq0JKkqts0D627RA2gphWBSTS72ktt6BCHZdfFQNqOL2FgUixgsWfIouLc7nNQT72rERzwf8EmI0kqy0aQszMXffIYhIgRZJXJvA100W2g/s320/Albert+Chevallier+Tayler+-+A+Day+at+the+Market.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Those who hoard produce, who lend on interest, who reduce the size of their measures, and who distort the markets, concerning them it says, "...<a href="http://bible.cc/amos/8-4.htm">you who swallow up the needy and cause the poor of the land to fail...God has sworn... I will never forget any of their deeds</a>." <br />
<br />
Hoarders are market manipulators who engineer price increases in food staples by hoarding large stores of food and then selling at these higher prices.&nbsp;<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-25.htm">Lending money on interest by one Jew to another is prohibited</a>. Reducing the size of the measure means cheating the buyer. Market manipulators are those who cause staple food prices to rise artificially. The prohibition does not apply to specialty food items, such as spices.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Day at the Market by Albert Chevallier Tayler</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/91.txt
<a id="src-00275"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/91.txt`

Bava Batra 91 – Importance of Settling the Land of Israel
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhQkCuzkMAT5KMlwcGsjcEiNbYX6HkzjrslhX3-zPh_e5r62naCIHQKB7oV8Xi4REPhKy1JonhjGN2Rq9q-ST23qvn_OGXJKlzSo3kjuJQct5aGxdSt5DXUE17-ADpXiK76KmGUsZfNV38/s1600/Jozef+Israels+-+Woman+at+the+Window.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhQkCuzkMAT5KMlwcGsjcEiNbYX6HkzjrslhX3-zPh_e5r62naCIHQKB7oV8Xi4REPhKy1JonhjGN2Rq9q-ST23qvn_OGXJKlzSo3kjuJQct5aGxdSt5DXUE17-ADpXiK76KmGUsZfNV38/s320/Jozef+Israels+-+Woman+at+the+Window.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One should refrain from exporting essential foods, such as wines, oils, and fine flour, out of the Land of Israel if this will lead to shortages and high prices. One may only leave the Land of Israel and go live outside the Land if food prices have doubled. Rabbi Shimon says that this is permitted only when one can't find wheat at all, but if wheat is available, even at very high prices, one should stay, provided that he can afford to feed his family.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai also used to say that Elimelech (the husband of Naomi in the book of Ruth) and his two sons were the most extraordinary men of their generation and the caretakers of their generation, and for what reason did they die? For moving out of the Land of Israel during famine, even though wheat was available to them.<br />
<br />
Painting: Woman at the Window by Jozef Israels<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/92.txt
<a id="src-00276"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/92.txt`

Bava Batra 92 – Implied Warranty
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi4rNDVZxvfjsERRdUTS1TdJADFj_M5Gzp9KFtNdZXnkmtjQx48Lnl6heuFX6Fb7QMLet6PkPjob6nIbc7nfid4hDlNlZZ6ONfnwmjYDI51F6V0qkrpHrKV0-4SvW0JaO6mobtHvhITBJE/s1600/Louise+Moillon+-+At+the+Market+Stall.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi4rNDVZxvfjsERRdUTS1TdJADFj_M5Gzp9KFtNdZXnkmtjQx48Lnl6heuFX6Fb7QMLet6PkPjob6nIbc7nfid4hDlNlZZ6ONfnwmjYDI51F6V0qkrpHrKV0-4SvW0JaO6mobtHvhITBJE/s320/Louise+Moillon+-+At+the+Market+Stall.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Implied_warranty" target="_blank">Sold products are expected to be fit for </a>their purpose. However, if one sells produce to his fellow without specifying whether he is selling it for planting or eating, and the buyer plants it, but it does not grow, the seller is not responsible for the loss. This is true even for flaxseed, which is usually purchased for planting. <br />
<br />
Normally, the law follows the principle of majority, assuming that the situation at hand is typical of the majority of such cases. However, in money matters, there is another principle: “To extract money from his fellow, the burden of proof lies with the claimant,” which&nbsp;trumps the principle of majority. Since the buyer cannot definitely prove his claim, the seller does not have to refund the purchase amount.<br />
<br />Art: At the Market Stall by Louise Moillon&nbsp;<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/93.txt
<a id="src-00277"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/93.txt`

Bava Batra 93 – Consequential Damages
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><br />
</div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEghivy1RQKZpK2QN2gK2upqHNPDoZ-PJW7KvM2IoOSZRV4hio2yhu2AKZRzDRtsK8hc3jT5S3CfQ9UlEIDXfxWm3vnWWy2-9_t7FHVls8EkArOxtz51HKd7RDPB7nBmvotGBP0EbAfrKfs/s1600/Georg+Flegel+-+Still+Life+with+Bread+and+Confectionary.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEghivy1RQKZpK2QN2gK2upqHNPDoZ-PJW7KvM2IoOSZRV4hio2yhu2AKZRzDRtsK8hc3jT5S3CfQ9UlEIDXfxWm3vnWWy2-9_t7FHVls8EkArOxtz51HKd7RDPB7nBmvotGBP0EbAfrKfs/s320/Georg+Flegel+-+Still+Life+with+Bread+and+Confectionary.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In the case of garden seed, <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/11/bava-batra-92-implied-warranty.html">which is always sold for planting and never for eating</a>, if the seller sold defective seed, what is his liability to the buyer? - Only the money for the seed itself, but not the buyer's expenses incurred during the unsuccessful planting. Others say that the seller must also pay the buyer's exbuyer's<br />
<br />
Who are these others? It is Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel who issued the following ruling: "If one takes wheat to a miller, and the miller did not moisten it before grinding and, as a result, processed it into bran, and the baker processed it into crumbly bread – he must pay the customer also the value of his embarrassment and the embarrassment of his guests – and such was a great custom that existed in Jerusalem."</span><br />
<br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Still-Life with Bread and Confectionary by Georg Flegel</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/94.txt
<a id="src-00278"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/94.txt`

Bava Batra 94 – Acceptable Percentage of Inferior Merchandise
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhobx35zToITQ7EGXOsNEedfHp5L4ykYgk15-eGKQM9MGjKOmWgpDysONuvkKG64rPbvoMRx0BhY_eLsdtwwS3u-VDoDu3P_Ynp6ON70L8Gc67p3JdcaKjdvWHZYINe3YmFOiaumT1GaJw/s1600/Giovanna+Garzoni+-+A+Plate+of+Figs.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhobx35zToITQ7EGXOsNEedfHp5L4ykYgk15-eGKQM9MGjKOmWgpDysONuvkKG64rPbvoMRx0BhY_eLsdtwwS3u-VDoDu3P_Ynp6ON70L8Gc67p3JdcaKjdvWHZYINe3YmFOiaumT1GaJw/s320/Giovanna+Garzoni+-+A+Plate+of+Figs.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one sells grain to his fellow, the buyer accepts upon himself impurity of one-quarter of a kav in a se'ah measure, which translates into 1/24; for figs, he accepts ten wormy ones per one hundred; for a cellar of wine, he accepts ten barrels of souring wine per hundred. All these are general guidelines without a prevailing local custom; however, if there is an accepted custom, it is binding.<br />
<br />
If the buyer suspects that the grain contains more impurities than 1/24 and begins to sift it, and it is found that it contains more than the allowed 1/24, he may sift all the grain and return ALL the impurities to the seller. Really, one expects to receive good quality grain, only that he would not bother to sift. Once he starts sifting, however, he can continue to sift all.<br />
<br />
Art: A Plate of Figs by Giovanna Garzoni<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/bava_batra/95.txt
<a id="src-00279"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/95.txt`

Bava Batra 95 – Selling a Wine Cellar As Is
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjJ6ELwpFYDIYm2F-TzWQSV-5jo0Vr0fjb8oD2bN0OpxhWgdmDW_jwJJyzYecF5TlbPGLm4nyAQNNB1jJEWiwssJLqziOQ4cmJZwlESd85a6oOjWy5lys1aWF0gxQDGoNsY2WgchglHnPI/s1600/Gabriel+Metsu+-+A+Woman+Drawing+Wine+From+A+Barrel.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjJ6ELwpFYDIYm2F-TzWQSV-5jo0Vr0fjb8oD2bN0OpxhWgdmDW_jwJJyzYecF5TlbPGLm4nyAQNNB1jJEWiwssJLqziOQ4cmJZwlESd85a6oOjWy5lys1aWF0gxQDGoNsY2WgchglHnPI/s320/Gabriel+Metsu+-+A+Woman+Drawing+Wine+From+A+Barrel.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_batra/bava_batra94.html">previous ruling</a> stated that when one sells a wine cellar, the buyer has to accept 10% of barrels that begin to sour. But compare it to the following.<br />
<br />
If a seller says, “I am selling you a cellar of wine,” he must give the buyer wine, which is good. If he says, “I am selling you THIS cellar of wine,” meaning AS IS, he may give the buyer quality wine as sold in stores for immediate consumption, that is, souring wine. <br />
<br />
So when does the buyer accept 10% inferior wine? When the seller said “as is,” the buyer mentioned that he needed wine for cooking—which means that it would be used slowly over time. “As is” allows all souring wine, but “for cooking” requires no more than 10%.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Woman Drawing Wine From A Barrel by Gabriel Metsu<br />
</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/96.txt
<a id="src-00280"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/96.txt`

Bava Batra 96 – Wine that Sours
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSOFANsyJYpyl9tc2Z3h9reXrTRebv2Q_hb-c-TVq6hKgKUpRIvtd1fsXm1lHw5I2x3fxMiJAw61Rg4RZb1aupF2TO5Z6ZqN6lTelDhlvF9TUgBmPm5W4yQsMrxyfQbJM83WPqbnevO9A/s1600/Frans+van+Mieris+II+1680+-+1763+-+Man+with+a+glass+of+wine.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSOFANsyJYpyl9tc2Z3h9reXrTRebv2Q_hb-c-TVq6hKgKUpRIvtd1fsXm1lHw5I2x3fxMiJAw61Rg4RZb1aupF2TO5Z6ZqN6lTelDhlvF9TUgBmPm5W4yQsMrxyfQbJM83WPqbnevO9A/s320/Frans+van+Mieris+II+1680+-+1763+-+Man+with+a+glass+of+wine.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Yehudah said, "The souring wine sold in shops still retains the blessing over wine, that is, "Who created the fruit of the vine." Rav Zevid said, "Why should I say a blessing over wine that has soured? Rather, the blessing is "Who created everything by His word." Rav Yehudah agrees that wine sold on the corners, which the thirsty, indiscriminate public consumes in haste, is not wine at all.<br />
<br />
If one bought a barrel of wine and it spoiled within three days, then Rav says that it was beginning to spoil at the time of the sale, and therefore, it is a mistaken purchase, which can be returned. Shmuel says that "it is on his shoulders." This means it was either spoiled while being carried or the spoilage was due to the owner's sins.<br />
<br /></span><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Man with a glass of wine by Frans van Mieris</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/97.txt
<a id="src-00281"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/97.txt`

Bava Batra 97 – Wine Made of Dregs
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUbsekJIZcJCbdwP8MuLFA14Plhir0NxZfwnablBnL6Zijq3KcNZlZEOTwzbQJiWDvctXHqfI2mXXneqK_AugD3DzwEhOPDxWnZOgZHd4JWDj06ztuviKji2S88S_ON_lDRGoiFKT82lQ/s1600/Pompeo+Massani+-+THE+WINE+MERCHANT.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUbsekJIZcJCbdwP8MuLFA14Plhir0NxZfwnablBnL6Zijq3KcNZlZEOTwzbQJiWDvctXHqfI2mXXneqK_AugD3DzwEhOPDxWnZOgZHd4JWDj06ztuviKji2S88S_ON_lDRGoiFKT82lQ/s320/Pompeo+Massani+-+THE+WINE+MERCHANT.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Water in which wine lees have been steeped is considered water, and the blessing over it is "Who created everything with His word." However, others say that if this water has the flavor of wine, the blessing is "Who created the fruit of the vine."<br />
<br />
If he poured three cups of water and when the liquid was decanted, four cups were produced, all agree that it is wine due to one cup of wine added from lees. If three cups were produced, all agree that it is water. They argue only when three and a half cups were decanted. The Sages say that three cups went in and three cups came out, so only one-sixth is wine from lees, while the other says that of the three cups that went in, one-half cup remained, and two half-cups of wine came out, making the mixture strong enough.<br /><br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Wine Merchant by Pompeo Massani</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/98.txt
<a id="src-00282"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/98.txt`

Bava Batra 98 – Building Contractor
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjFilr0RxE4wSJeVLT_x65YFBnxa8txkpaMHVrxtg_yOEkaPnyI3gfNJjtyR4b2TTTHSmpXTHUPeyTWTiqnVAJ3jT8hNEJzpO_FmUztzi0fanCsnYdj5InA8QDmwyF7h4VYzq9HRokcOTQ/s1600/+John+Constable+-+A+Cottage+in+a+Cornfield.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjFilr0RxE4wSJeVLT_x65YFBnxa8txkpaMHVrxtg_yOEkaPnyI3gfNJjtyR4b2TTTHSmpXTHUPeyTWTiqnVAJ3jT8hNEJzpO_FmUztzi0fanCsnYdj5InA8QDmwyF7h4VYzq9HRokcOTQ/s320/+John+Constable+-+A+Cottage+in+a+Cornfield.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who sells a lot to his fellow, or one who accepts a contract from his fellow regarding a lot, to construct for him a wedding house for his son or a widowhood house for his daughter, he must build a house measuring at least four elbows by six – these are the words of Rabbi Akiva. Rabbi Ishmael, however, says, "This is nothing but a cattle barn!"<br />
<br />
Incidentally, this ruling teaches that it is not proper for a son-in-law to live in his father-in-law's house. Instead, the groom's father usually built a small annex adjoining his house, where the newlywed couple could live. This accords with the teaching from the book of Ben Sira: "Lighter than bran is the son-in-law who lives in his father-in-law's house. Still lighter is a guest who invites another guest. And lighter yet is one who gives an answer before he has heard the question."<br /><br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Cottage in the Cornfield by John Constable</span></div>

---

### content/bava_batra/99.txt
<a id="src-00283"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_batra/99.txt`

Bava Batra 99 – Right-of-Way Through the Property of Another
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhE4PefhtKJHQ_A6INtzTaiEqB9AYomehPk0MQzWySC6At3xrhiES3W6w-PRf0zswmgmfRQ6CljmxGas6qqYzgrUgXiiDBJfcmuu7sUerpwCqpogNxc10EHWJ90wKN54XmmzG4tdHfHjQ8/s1600/Jean+Baptiste+Simeon+Chardin+-+Woman+at+the+Water+Cistern.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhE4PefhtKJHQ_A6INtzTaiEqB9AYomehPk0MQzWySC6At3xrhiES3W6w-PRf0zswmgmfRQ6CljmxGas6qqYzgrUgXiiDBJfcmuu7sUerpwCqpogNxc10EHWJ90wKN54XmmzG4tdHfHjQ8/s320/Jean+Baptiste+Simeon+Chardin+-+Woman+at+the+Water+Cistern.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">One who owns a water cistern within the house of his fellow (he either inherited it or bought it along with rights of access) may enter to draw water only at the time when people usually enter, that is, during the day. He may not bring his animal and give it to drink directly from the pit, but he must fill a container and give the animal to drink outside.<br />
<br />
The pit owner makes a lock for the cistern, and the homeowner makes his lock. The cistern owner makes the lock so that the homeowner will not rob him of his water. The homeowner makes the lock to avoid suspicions of impropriety concerning his wife.</span><br /><span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Woman at the Water Cistern by Jean Baptiste Chardin</span></div>

### content/bava_kamma/10.txt
<a id="src-00284"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/10.txt`

Bava Kamma 10 - An Animal Falls into the Pit (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_Rphw2C-v5kHtP5N4kNzCXCQHfGSVHlqA2AJzPMs5rbjmM7ekn1QXBOjbaZiT0A4-T_mOxr-6Yu9d9COqp8-6Q8MHQmhdewSTjbq_tp0G04Tk8DFtcYwDdTqNJK8QLGznWdrhxLiA9H3Z/s1600-h/Reynier+Coveyn+-+The+Butcher%27s+Shop.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5288757258858745618" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_Rphw2C-v5kHtP5N4kNzCXCQHfGSVHlqA2AJzPMs5rbjmM7ekn1QXBOjbaZiT0A4-T_mOxr-6Yu9d9COqp8-6Q8MHQmhdewSTjbq_tp0G04Tk8DFtcYwDdTqNJK8QLGznWdrhxLiA9H3Z/s320/Reynier+Coveyn+-+The+Butcher's+Shop.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 305px;" /></a>What is the case where one causes a portion of the damage but is liable for the complete damage? It is this <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-33.htm">case of a pit</a>:<br />
<br />
When an animal falls into the pit and dies, if the pit is at least 10 hand-breadths deep, the owner of the pit is liable. If one person digs the 9 hand-breadths and the second one adds 1 hand-breadth, the second one is liable for all the damage since he added the lethal quality to the pit.<br />
<br />
The pit owner pays the difference between the animal's worth when it was alive and the <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-36.htm">carcass' value</a>.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Butcher's Shop by Reynier Coveyn</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/100.txt
<a id="src-00285"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/100.txt`

Bava Kamma 100 -Dyer Ruins the Wool (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_t6I9qTqm_SkyFHw6f5iETdLKU3FsZqWU8LVgfqf3oAwiHZoXqLsoTc7Au55gdZvb3okT7RaPxJKWxGCC3lCTqoNGw9nNwSogDlb55GM5lmtLT3eAbB6nq2ar3g3dnz22sjVsxbg0G0RK/s1600-h/Mark+Rothko.jpeg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5322177998967338546" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_t6I9qTqm_SkyFHw6f5iETdLKU3FsZqWU8LVgfqf3oAwiHZoXqLsoTc7Au55gdZvb3okT7RaPxJKWxGCC3lCTqoNGw9nNwSogDlb55GM5lmtLT3eAbB6nq2ar3g3dnz22sjVsxbg0G0RK/s320/Mark+Rothko.jpeg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 310px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If one gives wool to the dyer, and it gets burned in the cauldron, the dyer pays the value of the wool – because he is a paid custodian responsible for accidents.<br />
<br />
If he dyed it poorly, the dyer gets the lesser of the improvement to the wool and his expenses. Since he knew that using inferior dye would result in an inferior product, he is a damager. His compensation claim is that he did, in fact, increase the value.<br />
<br />
If he was supposed to dye red, and he dyed black, Rabbi Meir says that he pays the value of wool, but Rabbi Yehudah awards the claim as above.<br />
<br />
Art: Untitled by Mark Rothko

---

### content/bava_kamma/101.txt
<a id="src-00286"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/101.txt`

Bava Kamma 101 - Thief Steals the Wool, Dyes It, and Returns It (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgiBYPtTX5ClCkcwncM7XzLX3R2_w_v4PEmaA2rMYUdVPX4qJuAH2nuDOYlWiQCMlEgPZ-ukdZds_ly5EWZaHjBAAX6sLLT-uq99deqRfnZNBiMC9m4XURRba7Uu1qv_oM_BbMsfBzFGzIa/s1600-h/Edwin+Lord+Weeks+-+Outside+An+Indian+Dye+House.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5322416678430734930" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgiBYPtTX5ClCkcwncM7XzLX3R2_w_v4PEmaA2rMYUdVPX4qJuAH2nuDOYlWiQCMlEgPZ-ukdZds_ly5EWZaHjBAAX6sLLT-uq99deqRfnZNBiMC9m4XURRba7Uu1qv_oM_BbMsfBzFGzIa/s320/Edwin+Lord+Weeks+-+Outside+An+Indian+Dye+House.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 271px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If one robbed wool and liquid dye belonging to someone and dyed that wool with the dye and now returns the dyed wool to the owner – is the improvement of dye considered material? <br />
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
That is, when the thief returns the dyed wool to the owner, is he returning both the dye and the wool? Or, perhaps, that improvement is not considered material, and thus, he is returning only the wool but not the dye – which has, in effect, disappeared? </div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
The question is relevant when the dyed wool became cheap. Does the thief have to pay for the dye? Talmud doesn't resolve the question.</div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: Outside An Indian Dye House by Edwin Lord Weeks</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/102.txt
<a id="src-00287"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/102.txt`

Bava Kamma 102 - Question about the laws of Shmita year (Torts)
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgSokf-mnvIWiG13G-y1esK99T4C_pYbZR4hdMUmCHuX9H4zuaEWbQWLLULVVfDTY4m7rYvVVuuSaffuNoCEvl_GdBneLxruZ7Nf5tWCkI61m5TZIA-SZjKMyKJeuuNCgqjnDLNO4vznZpW5fR9I-XqMxcQ97vIlt3t0Uo7_uvc8j5P45_owbKl0zFyl4O8/s729/the-harvest-1883.jpg!Large.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="600" data-original-width="729" height="263" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgSokf-mnvIWiG13G-y1esK99T4C_pYbZR4hdMUmCHuX9H4zuaEWbQWLLULVVfDTY4m7rYvVVuuSaffuNoCEvl_GdBneLxruZ7Nf5tWCkI61m5TZIA-SZjKMyKJeuuNCgqjnDLNO4vznZpW5fR9I-XqMxcQ97vIlt3t0Uo7_uvc8j5P45_owbKl0zFyl4O8/s320/the-harvest-1883.jpg!Large.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Every seven years, a farmer in Israel is supposed to give rest to the land. Foodstuff that grew of itself can be collected and eaten, but after the harvest is over, one cannot keep it in his home but should put it out in the street for everybody's consumption. Wood is included in the laws of shmita.<p></p><p>However, Rava noticed a contradiction. A rule about cane reeds and grapevine leaves states that if these are gathered for food, then they have the laws of shmita, but if they are gathered for kindling - they do not have the laws of shmita. He resolved the contradiction: the laws of shmita apply to produce where the benefit and consumption come simultaneously, just like with food.&nbsp;</p><p>For example, wood is burnt (and destroyed) in an oven, but the benefit (baking) comes later. On the other hand, dyestuff is destroyed when dissolved in water, and the benefit - dying the cloth - comes simultaneously. The laws of shmita apply only to stuff that is destroyed simultaneously with giving benefit.</p><p>Art: Harvest Camille Pissaro</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/103.txt
<a id="src-00288"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/103.txt`

Bava Kamma 103 - Title insurance using the name of the king (Torts)
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgtEKQZUABFm3YEULTpwmXSI4orz11PPHekx_wifgGbO2hN_J6oCtS1_mSjI_ByBCU9MJzWkxYT6dh0xCmrBhnKNWxyfr5Tzw_APL2kLdBaKBYbcobzuY9LIKpFE9hkHKT6C1y9yQkqVKiPXtAUv5wm4ZeCYx3rgLUQMNJgDBVu8uEuiS177fZT5a0arpUl/s900/the-ploughed-field.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="722" data-original-width="900" height="257" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgtEKQZUABFm3YEULTpwmXSI4orz11PPHekx_wifgGbO2hN_J6oCtS1_mSjI_ByBCU9MJzWkxYT6dh0xCmrBhnKNWxyfr5Tzw_APL2kLdBaKBYbcobzuY9LIKpFE9hkHKT6C1y9yQkqVKiPXtAUv5wm4ZeCYx3rgLUQMNJgDBVu8uEuiS177fZT5a0arpUl/s320/the-ploughed-field.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>A cryptic ruling: if one buys a field in the name of his fellow, we do not force him to sell; if he said "on condition," we force him to sell. Rav Sheshet explained it.<p></p><p>One comes to buy a field and says that he is buying it for the Exilarch (who was given a semi-royal authority over the Jews in Babylon.) He is really buying the land for himself, but he wants the deed to be written in the name of the Exilarch. He is doing it to discourage protesters to the sale, who might claim that they are the true owners of the land and not the seller.&nbsp;</p><p>The ruling then says we do not force the seller to write another bill of sale with the buyer's name. The seller might not want to write two bills of sale because it may look like he is selling the field twice. However, if the buyer stipulated that he would want two bills of sale, the seller has to produce them. But that is obvious? The seller can say that he thought the buyer was talking to the witnesses.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;The Ploughed Field by Van Gogh</p><p><br /></p>

---

<a id="src-00289"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/104.txt`

Bava Kamma 104 - A Robber and Perjurer Repents and Seeks to Repay (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhNdMOb09m1hSKoLCah8q0pHK7souI5zWwGfex1AvrdOzYcIpV9d4hgp6N39bLf7HiPZEJa4USYcdy8oRfFPN5aVthOst8RohLxJptVzJYEpGqmIR1Y9UoenD3FfqT1caT3SCcz3w6OIvjl/s1600-h/Van+Gogh+-+Miners+Wives+Carrying+Sacks.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5323672757112591010" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhNdMOb09m1hSKoLCah8q0pHK7souI5zWwGfex1AvrdOzYcIpV9d4hgp6N39bLf7HiPZEJa4USYcdy8oRfFPN5aVthOst8RohLxJptVzJYEpGqmIR1Y9UoenD3FfqT1caT3SCcz3w6OIvjl/s320/Van+Gogh+-+Miners+Wives+Carrying+Sacks.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 202px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>One who robs his fellow in the value of a prutah (5 cents) or more and then swears falsely to him, denying the theft, but later confesses and wishes to repent must pursue him to the farthest land. He may not give it to the victim's son nor to his agent, but he may give it to an agent of the court.<br />
<br />
The court then holds the stolen property until the victim calls for it. The Rabbis enacted that this should suffice to ensure that a potential penitent would not be discouraged.<br />
<br />
The agent above is informal, but a formal agent appointed with two witnesses can receive the payment.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Miners Wives Carrying Sacks by Van Gogh</div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/105.txt
<a id="src-00290"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/105.txt`

Bava Kamma 105 - Flaky Humans (Torts)
<p><a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_kamma/bava_kamma104.html" target="_blank"></a></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjWRoSnHNj2KtgCpgJaiDAZHiHHg6YAufN1UvPY9neyJfG9QNXgk5KESOpyKGvR1du5Po7fnsi2j_4QTDCTQOyCHO1_w5161_9EsOl-TsK_Q6EZJ4Ru6BmtrXFYS7Olp0XhW8kOWMZfE_56Ue6i7wQ47IoscBIMTHr2_KtKkIFXOsI05NkMVBLzkJUQ9TsA/s900/train-robbery-frederick-lyle-morris-disabled-veteran.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="900" data-original-width="694" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjWRoSnHNj2KtgCpgJaiDAZHiHHg6YAufN1UvPY9neyJfG9QNXgk5KESOpyKGvR1du5Po7fnsi2j_4QTDCTQOyCHO1_w5161_9EsOl-TsK_Q6EZJ4Ru6BmtrXFYS7Olp0XhW8kOWMZfE_56Ue6i7wQ47IoscBIMTHr2_KtKkIFXOsI05NkMVBLzkJUQ9TsA/s320/train-robbery-frederick-lyle-morris-disabled-veteran.jpg" width="247" /></a></div>We remember that one who robs his fellow of money, either by stealing, robbing, or not returning something deposited with him - <b>and swears that he did not do it</b> - but then repents, needs to fix it in a special way. He has to find the victim, restore what he stole, add one-fifth, and bring a guilt offering to the Temple.<p></p><p>What if he returned the principal but not the fifth and now swears that he returned the fifth? If he then confesses that he again took a false oath, he must restore the amount, add one-fifth, and bring another guilt sacrifice. This process can continue until the principal amount is reduced to less than a prutah (about five cents.)</p><p>Art:&nbsp;Train Robbery by Frederick Morris</p><p><br /></p><p><br /></p>

Bava Kamma 106 - One Who Swore Falsely May Not Have to Pay (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjkh_DKO_VVbotNLSuY5luXx8JQ9qrmWroJzGh8Vbjx4DwSNZga307QOuk1pkHNVEHrI1lfnon_6acTCJO8aVce-1bOtXXZCghYeSbHzqa19dmlM39QNIeOmRFhkqgH5Hln1fiwaKE9pcFk/s1600-h/Van+Gogh+-+Old+Man+In+Sorrow.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5324250627795291570" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjkh_DKO_VVbotNLSuY5luXx8JQ9qrmWroJzGh8Vbjx4DwSNZga307QOuk1pkHNVEHrI1lfnon_6acTCJO8aVce-1bOtXXZCghYeSbHzqa19dmlM39QNIeOmRFhkqgH5Hln1fiwaKE9pcFk/s320/Van+Gogh+-+Old+Man+In+Sorrow.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 254px;" /></a>If one says to his fellow, "You have my maneh (100 zuz, or $5,000) in your possession," and the other responds, "I do not have anything of  yours," - and he swears to that effect, and afterward witnesses come and attest to his guilt, he is exempt from payment:<br />
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
"...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-11.htm">and its owner shall accept it, and he shall not pay</a>..."    teaches that once the owner has received an oath, the defendant no longer pays money.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
This is logical regarding a loan, that is given to the borrower to be spent, but it is true even regarding deposit because <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-11.htm">the quote</a> is about a deposit.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Old Man In Sorrow by Van Gogh</div>
<div>
</div>

### content/bava_kamma/107.txt
<a id="src-00292"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/107.txt`

Bava Kamma 107 - People Are Not Brazen to Deny Loans Given to Them (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgyHSJcTEDXeErsOdAsGRBTOuCRvk0MVeXl3L5gobQaJJe4LCZNxUfgKYE_IITFwOhWhx2Sp11rRqU0uuSEGIrevXgdKSVmkDTIO5YV4-5Arni8D7phUJWvwsZdFtr98dsM56NNbQJiSNUY/s1600-h/Henri-Jules-Jean+Geoffroy++-+Give+Me+A+Bite.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5324638493913853746" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgyHSJcTEDXeErsOdAsGRBTOuCRvk0MVeXl3L5gobQaJJe4LCZNxUfgKYE_IITFwOhWhx2Sp11rRqU0uuSEGIrevXgdKSVmkDTIO5YV4-5Arni8D7phUJWvwsZdFtr98dsM56NNbQJiSNUY/s320/Henri-Jules-Jean+Geoffroy++-+Give+Me+A+Bite.jpg" style="float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 226px;" /></a><div><div>One who admits that he owes a part of the loan but not the complete amount has to swear to this effect, and after the oath in court, he is not liable to pay the rest.&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
There is a presumption that a person is not brazen enough to deny his obligation to the face of the creditor, who did him a favor by loaning money without interest. If he partially admits, that is because he is trying to evade part of the claim until he has money. Therefore, the Torah imposed an oath.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Later, people became more brazen, and the Rabbis imposed an oath for complete denial as well.</div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: Give Me A Bite by Henri-Jules-Jean Geoffroy</div>
</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/108.txt
<a id="src-00293"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/108.txt`

Bava Kamma 108 - Unpaid custodian (Torts)
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh5zYibRpJxu-Y2vyLY0xRfDn0uLCm9cExOWPMYOPE64QKVAmxmkH46O4UjAirzBRAIK3owTpxYhDoxhxoc8TO1RG6bOXoUe0rShJfClxCmPMNbAEQCCNzPlsDMnv4KINInVf2JzKXYDrpUjSjNJcPDUelBbOBwqtf3BBbEYbuaRXNehvrkQBg1mbF-DJMl/s900/the-last-moments-of-christopher-columbus-claude-jacquand.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="663" data-original-width="900" height="236" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh5zYibRpJxu-Y2vyLY0xRfDn0uLCm9cExOWPMYOPE64QKVAmxmkH46O4UjAirzBRAIK3owTpxYhDoxhxoc8TO1RG6bOXoUe0rShJfClxCmPMNbAEQCCNzPlsDMnv4KINInVf2JzKXYDrpUjSjNJcPDUelBbOBwqtf3BBbEYbuaRXNehvrkQBg1mbF-DJMl/s320/the-last-moments-of-christopher-columbus-claude-jacquand.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>When one entrusts an item to his fellow, the fellow becomes an unpaid custodian. If one then comes to retrieve the object and his fellow says, "It is lost," the fellow is not obligated to pay since he was doing a favor. But if one insists and asks his fellow to swear and the fellow accepts an oath, things become more complex.<p></p><p>If witnesses come and testify that the custodian consumed the deposit himself, he is obligated to pay for it double what he stole. If the custodian repents and confesses his false oath, he must pay the total amount, plus one-fifth of the value, and bring a guilt offering to the Temple.</p><p>What if one robs his father and swears to him that he did not do it, the father dies, and the son then repents his false oath? The son pays the principal plus one-fifth to his father's heirs (his brothers and uncles.) If he does not have the money to repay, he can borrow from others and give it to his brothers; his creditors will come and collect from his portion of the inheritance.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;The Last Moments of Christopher Columbus by Claude Jacquand</p>

---

### content/bava_kamma/109.txt
<a id="src-00294"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/109.txt`

Bava Kamma 109 - Son Robs His Father and Swears that He Didn't (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjRtufg_Xg7U3aBWG32DxBO6x3ggQj1Cxy9IIGq-_p5bN7Q0wM4wrmLtjSU_spJEVsOv58oVu6LUiXZBM5RnsQPnyQunYgZ-PorkyMD4VTGuZujMKxmz2mUhyphenhyphenL7I0BemdmmugN-mP6JViiV/s1600-h/Thomas+Rowlandson+-+Fathers+Displeasure.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5325521495755792882" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjRtufg_Xg7U3aBWG32DxBO6x3ggQj1Cxy9IIGq-_p5bN7Q0wM4wrmLtjSU_spJEVsOv58oVu6LUiXZBM5RnsQPnyQunYgZ-PorkyMD4VTGuZujMKxmz2mUhyphenhyphenL7I0BemdmmugN-mP6JViiV/s320/Thomas+Rowlandson+-+Fathers+Displeasure.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 287px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Imagine one robs his father and swears falsely to him, denying the robbery, and the father dies. The son then admits his guilt – he pays the principal and the one-fifth surcharge (for false oath) to his father's other sons or to the father's brothers – who are the next in line to inherit.<br />
<br />
Although the robber is his father's heir, he may not keep what he stole – for he must fulfill the dictate to return stolen property.<br />
<br />
If he doesn't wish or can't pay, he may borrow from others, repay, and his creditors may then come and collect the debt from his inheritance.<br />
<br /><div>Art:&nbsp;Thomas Rowlandson - Fathers Displeasure</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/11.txt

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/11.txt`

Bava Kamma 11 - The Value of a Carcass (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjJdah7TxeH-YQtndFbuExENc7dGXmsvhIp2UBcOf5sG4na4yg4EO2SImtKuX9ydu36y-dtKN8WDNA7RFCeVxJ9w6NEPNvvs5CJonxltV2E0153Ar3CfXCF681q8eO4tlaNIcQAzEO4cTGd/s1600-h/Jan+Victors+-++The+Butchers+Shop.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5289012697331173954" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjJdah7TxeH-YQtndFbuExENc7dGXmsvhIp2UBcOf5sG4na4yg4EO2SImtKuX9ydu36y-dtKN8WDNA7RFCeVxJ9w6NEPNvvs5CJonxltV2E0153Ar3CfXCF681q8eO4tlaNIcQAzEO4cTGd/s320/Jan+Victors+-++The+Butchers+Shop.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 290px;" /></a><div>How do we know that it is incumbent upon the owner of the pit to raise the dead ox from the pit and bring it to court for appraisal? Because the pit owner "...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-36.htm">shall return money to the animal's owner and the carcass</a> (will be his)."</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Since the payment for the damage, in this case, is the difference between the live animal and the worth of the carcass, the court estimates the worth of the carcass. Similarly, the courts evaluate the value of a broken object for a borrower but not for a thief or robber.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: The Butchers Shop by Jan Victors&nbsp;</div>

---

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/110.txt`

Bava Kamma 110 - One Who Robs a Convert Pays to the Priests (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiJvRC7lYEEDepuo-3UE98qFQpFM8kTn9D9OHXxmWHGBjgvUKogezOS8bzDK3aFQEbM63EHhdIjiwr1nYSiHPG2yycUdjMcK9pn0lNq1ciRpBtyYVnCB_o_SiCHvY-yosT5lWI1Y0gDcQy4/s1600-h/Thomas+Cowperthwait+Eakins+-+Baby+at+Play+1876.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5325740887567821986" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiJvRC7lYEEDepuo-3UE98qFQpFM8kTn9D9OHXxmWHGBjgvUKogezOS8bzDK3aFQEbM63EHhdIjiwr1nYSiHPG2yycUdjMcK9pn0lNq1ciRpBtyYVnCB_o_SiCHvY-yosT5lWI1Y0gDcQy4/s320/Thomas+Cowperthwait+Eakins+-+Baby+at+Play+1876.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 210px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">A convert to Judaism is considered a newborn child, not part of his old family nor yet of any new one.</span></div>
<br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one robs a convert and swears falsely to him in denial of the robbery and the convert dies without leaving heirs, the robber </span><a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/5-8.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">pays the principal and the one-fifth surcharge to the Kohanim and brings a guilt offering to the Altar</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: x-large;">. </span></div>
<br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Suppose the robber was bringing up the money and the guilt offering to Jerusalem, and he died en route. In that case, the money shall be given to the robber's sons because restitution to the Kohanim is only to atone for his guilt - while alive.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Baby at Play by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Thomas Cowperthwait Eakins</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

### content/bava_kamma/111.txt
<a id="src-00297"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/111.txt`

Bava Kamma 111 - Stealing for One's Children (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgMiurCu2e2y7R5pZsPD_1NzMjnXx1jPSV_1TaLeYLN0tNyTx_pu5u9UtzQnh2Q9PMgDP9s-kbYAFKuGd2IAXJYoDLqpE_N73eZzb3mrKc_vGNgvuikhw1IDKEDjErfz4KVMPZgM-HaVVC6/s1600-h/Evert+Pieters+-+The+Afternoon+Meal.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5326279366877268178" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgMiurCu2e2y7R5pZsPD_1NzMjnXx1jPSV_1TaLeYLN0tNyTx_pu5u9UtzQnh2Q9PMgDP9s-kbYAFKuGd2IAXJYoDLqpE_N73eZzb3mrKc_vGNgvuikhw1IDKEDjErfz4KVMPZgM-HaVVC6/s320/Evert+Pieters+-+The+Afternoon+Meal.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 279px;" /></a>Twenty-four priestly gifts were given to Aaron and his sons, and they were presented with a "generalization-specification-generalization" rule. One who upholds these gifts is considered as though he upheld the whole Torah, which is exposed with this rule.<br />
<br />
If one robs something and feeds it to his children, they are not liable to pay. If he left the item as an inheritance, they must return it. Once the stolen property is no longer extant, they are not liable to return it unless the father also left real estate property – for it is then mortgaged for his theft.<br />
<br />Art: The Afternoon Meal by Evert Pieters

---

### content/bava_kamma/112.txt
<a id="src-00298"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/112.txt`

Bava Kamma 112 - Defendant Needs to be Summoned and Present in Court (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2y4YjRjbMJJv7873rwZfS9_LLYSTfrIZfn5fU3KlF7Vvu5wAxlRicCuYMLZItKrZ-Vx2Ax4qpwO7dh3LH3mNwfBCQEdG-JLQyXhtW50vuBBSzO8I3QkWUFljicbCeDNV8BQ13sTiHci0N/s1600-h/Rembrandt+Van+Rijn+-+The+Moneychanger+-+detail+-+1627.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5326608275359073378" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2y4YjRjbMJJv7873rwZfS9_LLYSTfrIZfn5fU3KlF7Vvu5wAxlRicCuYMLZItKrZ-Vx2Ax4qpwO7dh3LH3mNwfBCQEdG-JLQyXhtW50vuBBSzO8I3QkWUFljicbCeDNV8BQ13sTiHci0N/s320/Rembrandt+Van+Rijn+-+The+Moneychanger+-+detail+-+1627.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 168px;" /></a>When one lends money to another Jew, he should "...<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/25-36.htm">not take from him interest and increase</a>..." and refund any interest if taken "...<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/25-36.htm">so that your brother may live with you</a>."<br />
<br />
Suppose the father leaves his children interest money, and they know it is interest. In that case, they are not obligated to return it – because they have acquired it through the combination of the owner losing hope to recover it and the change of ownership domain.<br />
<br />
The court can't accept witnesses' testimony in the absence of the defendant – unless he refuses to come and there are pressing circumstances.<br />
<br /><div>Art: The Moneychanger (detail) by Rembrandt Van Rijn</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/113.txt
<a id="src-00299"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/113.txt`

Bava Kamma 113 - Not Taking Charity from Stolen Money (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-V9Mku1DrDeTSPUerGBV4-ZIacxylIqKPwYPMWrS9zLRuqCfdUnfTCk7NpenRMkieJ4qvZ985UWr9W7dXgZoCe2z98Cwlb6Fp4ofeubGyrsbS2vf6EuFjexd-aS_Q76blxkS5PMPYNzTs/s1600-h/Fernando+Botero+-+Charity+1996.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5326847127983593954" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-V9Mku1DrDeTSPUerGBV4-ZIacxylIqKPwYPMWrS9zLRuqCfdUnfTCk7NpenRMkieJ4qvZ985UWr9W7dXgZoCe2z98Cwlb6Fp4ofeubGyrsbS2vf6EuFjexd-aS_Q76blxkS5PMPYNzTs/s320/Fernando+Botero+-+Charity+1996.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 282px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><div>A messenger of the court who delivers a court summons is believed to say that the defendant refused to come, and the court can excommunicate him based on that. But for money matters, two witnesses are required.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
One may not change his larger coins into smaller coins that are known to be stolen. One may not take charity from stolen money – because it encourages the thieves to steal since they erroneously believe that giving stolen money to charity justifies their wrongdoing and exempts them from compensating the owner. Examples are money from unjust arbitrary customs and tax collectors, who bought rights to collect what they want.</div>
</div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: Charity by Fernando Botero</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/114.txt
<a id="src-00300"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/114.txt`

Bava Kamma 114 - Objects That The Owners Despaired to Retrieve (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEje1hZvzT4ad6rGQTeb9mE0pGl2zQE2wOr40tbyLXrxz5Tmk_mr2JqknRl3MnomWeyYSBano6QMQdM4Q-X5_gchx9WAsecxWGeSdywohhOtc8k-oLIwNfKm3riyQJiBxH8H0Pm6ZRR-5_Ll/s1600-h/Charles+Hunt+-+A+Pat+For+The+Donkey.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5327236947518253730" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEje1hZvzT4ad6rGQTeb9mE0pGl2zQE2wOr40tbyLXrxz5Tmk_mr2JqknRl3MnomWeyYSBano6QMQdM4Q-X5_gchx9WAsecxWGeSdywohhOtc8k-oLIwNfKm3riyQJiBxH8H0Pm6ZRR-5_Ll/s320/Charles+Hunt+-+A+Pat+For+The+Donkey.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 241px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If (illegitimate) customs collectors confiscated someone's donkey but then, out of compassion, gave him an inferior one, or if bandits seized his garment and gave him another garment, they are his because it may be assumed that their owners have despaired of retrieving them. However, if he wants to return these out of piety, he can return them to the original owners and not the robbers.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
In the case of one who rescues things from a river or from bandits, if it is known that the owners have despaired of retrieving them, they are his.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Art: A Pat For The Donkey by Charles Hunt</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/115.txt
<a id="src-00301"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/115.txt`

Bava Kamma 115 - One Sees His Utensils and Books in the Possession of Another (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjtJr5BkwiAxVk-0b4HK-a0_Oc31grvOCiuJuEWBas-d-Y8m8xlnyCjuWTipguP-utWI6XWufp7-azCm4NxKN1xa2Njd-ooMTbJqeLSJSi5XK9w8FtD_Fvs2zcEkXrUyUtZequp-8nJ6uVl/s1600-h/John+Frederick+Peto+-+Books,+Mug,+Pipe+and+Violin.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5327611814037769042" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjtJr5BkwiAxVk-0b4HK-a0_Oc31grvOCiuJuEWBas-d-Y8m8xlnyCjuWTipguP-utWI6XWufp7-azCm4NxKN1xa2Njd-ooMTbJqeLSJSi5XK9w8FtD_Fvs2zcEkXrUyUtZequp-8nJ6uVl/s320/John+Frederick+Peto+-+Books,+Mug,+Pipe+and+Violin.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 263px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>
<div>
Suppose one recognizes his utensils and books in the possession of another, and a report of burglary concerning him was circulated in the city. In that case, the alleged purchaser must return the property to the claimant and swear to him how much he paid, and the claimant pays. Otherwise, the claimant is not believed, for we can say that he sold them to another, and this person purchased them from him.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If a river swept away his donkey and a more expensive donkey of his fellow, and he abandoned his and saved the donkey of his fellow, he receives only his rescue fee. If he stipulates payment for his donkey, he gets it.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Books, Mug, Pipe and Violin by John Frederick Peto</div><div>
<br />
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/116.txt
<a id="src-00302"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/116.txt`

Bava Kamma 116 - Saving Your Friend's Honey by Losing Your Wine (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7nso6FilbjDfekGLjn4pyGhNixee6vyxHl5QIg4n4I5G312pNHs1sq0o1V38zTlmThTiFOcbgv2pbs5Prkxqf64TqF5cBiDNoFCXzJ4aFBiaYmvtCjj0kKMhgJ0pSHwE1HkUZlaKNutN2/s1600-h/Judith+Leyster+-+A+Youth+With+The+Jug.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5327994534623491522" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7nso6FilbjDfekGLjn4pyGhNixee6vyxHl5QIg4n4I5G312pNHs1sq0o1V38zTlmThTiFOcbgv2pbs5Prkxqf64TqF5cBiDNoFCXzJ4aFBiaYmvtCjj0kKMhgJ0pSHwE1HkUZlaKNutN2/s320/Judith+Leyster+-+A+Youth+With+The+Jug.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 217px;" /></a>
<div>
One was with a barrel of wine, the other with a jug of honey, and the barrel of honey cracked. If the wine owner poured out his wine and saved the honey, he received only the laborer's fee. If he said, "I will save your honey, but you must pay me for my wine," - the other is obligated to pay.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
But compare this to the one fleeing from a prison, who can promise the ferryman an inordinate amount for taking him over the river and then say, "Just kidding," and pay only the fair? &nbsp;- That's different because the ferryman loses only his time.</div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art;&nbsp;Judith Leyster - A Youth With The Jug</div>
<div>
</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/117.txt
<a id="src-00303"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/117.txt`

Bava Kamma 117 - Extortionists Take A Field Away from the Robber (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgvwrhpEsbhBdTu8Y0BadGBXTmYaanVH-FvxyBAGyac-qv-t0fsayHg8nEdHpJ_XaQ0xcd22tFSczugT1Wyw_LJbVykh0bj_jJ9Gjnx8hz6K988w0_e_H70WHuSWCFz-H7MGWhRN8y_sLPO/s1600-h/Andrew+Wyeth+-+Christina%27s+World.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5328328345370598514" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgvwrhpEsbhBdTu8Y0BadGBXTmYaanVH-FvxyBAGyac-qv-t0fsayHg8nEdHpJ_XaQ0xcd22tFSczugT1Wyw_LJbVykh0bj_jJ9Gjnx8hz6K988w0_e_H70WHuSWCFz-H7MGWhRN8y_sLPO/s320/Andrew+Wyeth+-+Christina's+World.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 226px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>
<div>
If one steals a field from his fellow, and the extortionists then take it from him, then if it is a province-wide plague, meaning that the extortionists have appropriated the fields of others as well, the robber can say to the owner, "Behold, what is yours is in front of you." But if the field was taken on the account of the robber, then the robber is obligated to provide the owner with another field.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
But we already understand that "if not, the thief pays!" Rather, it is yet another case where he did not take the field away but showed it to the extortionists.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Christina's World by Andrew Wyeth</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/118.txt
<a id="src-00304"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/118.txt`

Bava Kamma 118 - Thief Returns Stolen Object and Tells the Owner (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXwxuSv905JGsQDu1cytosioNGmv9rWZkRkd4HND1ZcIk4NklxZaD7zTMNj-wqmv5yUKJECPGkZmjBC21kSzCNW7A9Qr_Jrs5nTCMtjUsiahbLUh2LLM8aSR0yKhWDUSslnlXSB-1OtKNs/s1600-h/Elisabeth+Sophie+Cheron+-+Self+Portrait.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5328862266848138514" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXwxuSv905JGsQDu1cytosioNGmv9rWZkRkd4HND1ZcIk4NklxZaD7zTMNj-wqmv5yUKJECPGkZmjBC21kSzCNW7A9Qr_Jrs5nTCMtjUsiahbLUh2LLM8aSR0yKhWDUSslnlXSB-1OtKNs/s320/Elisabeth+Sophie+Cheron+-+Self+Portrait.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 289px;" /></a>If a river inundated a stolen field, the thief can say, "Here is your field," but Rabbi Eliezer obligates him to pay.<br />
<br />
If one stole a lamb from a flock and returned it without notifying the owner, and that lamb subsequently died or was stolen, the thief is responsible for it.<br />
<br />
If the owner was aware of the theft but then counted the flock and found it complete, the thief is not liable for any future mishap. But if the owner was unaware of the theft, counting does not help since the thief has taught the lamb to go astray, and the owner needs to know which lamb it was.<br />
<br /><div>Art: Self Portrait by Elisabeth Sophie Cheron</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/119.txt
<a id="src-00305"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/119.txt`

Bava Kamma 119 - Stealing is a Serious Matter (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBLuGrBfFgJJwD7kOf8l4YkOePU1hvJgi-SyV-rixAdqXnWZ_5xAexWOCtacPWKfwpdxPCzV_tsUwBfMkGpZj6HR8zAr1a5YHiMI4viYMWTCtBcKnJLlT30d3PRFxddqA9y3iR3euPnu9e/s1600-h/Paul+Charles+Chocarne-Moreau+-+Chimney+Sweeps+Stealing+Bread,+1897.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5329046214302503682" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBLuGrBfFgJJwD7kOf8l4YkOePU1hvJgi-SyV-rixAdqXnWZ_5xAexWOCtacPWKfwpdxPCzV_tsUwBfMkGpZj6HR8zAr1a5YHiMI4viYMWTCtBcKnJLlT30d3PRFxddqA9y3iR3euPnu9e/s320/Paul+Charles+Chocarne-Moreau+-+Chimney+Sweeps+Stealing+Bread,+1897.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 250px;" /></a>One should not buy items from someone who tells him to conceal his purchase because they may be stolen.<br />
<br />
An <a href="http://community.livejournal.com/talmud_daily/1364.html">informer</a> may be killed if he informs habitually or is on his way to inform. However, his possession may not be destroyed because <a href="http://bible.cc/job/27-17.htm">he may have righteous descendants</a>.<br />
<br />
Anyone who robs a prutah from his fellow is as if <a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/1-19.htm">he too</a><a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/1-19.htm">k</a> <a href="http://bible.cc/jeremiah/5-17.htm">his soul</a> <a href="http://bible.cc/joel/3-19.htm">from</a> <a href="http://bible.cc/2_samuel/21-1.htm">him</a>, for at times, he will not have any money left to buy food and will starve to death.<br />
<br />
Insignificant leftovers of materials given to the craftsman for work belong to him.<br /><br /><div>Art: Chimney Sweeps Stealing Bread by Paul Charles Chocarne-Moreau</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/12.txt
<a id="src-00306"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/12.txt`

Bava Kamma 12 - Are Slaves Like Land?  (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjjQ_W-3nHJ6YYlWIysh_KsXltTulOXKwGtcS5pbPfcqflSYW9fwWctuZo6kRApYzUphbr9pqMWH39poLZNhuskAbPu28iA_RzlGWEVGSjE0qKVCE8vcl9J3cK78DWFd3vRZB53JB02cio4/s1600-h/Pieter+Gerritsz+van+Roestraten+-+Casket+of+jewels+on+a+table.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5289433599411937586" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjjQ_W-3nHJ6YYlWIysh_KsXltTulOXKwGtcS5pbPfcqflSYW9fwWctuZo6kRApYzUphbr9pqMWH39poLZNhuskAbPu28iA_RzlGWEVGSjE0qKVCE8vcl9J3cK78DWFd3vRZB53JB02cio4/s320/Pieter+Gerritsz+van+Roestraten+-+Casket+of+jewels+on+a+table.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 281px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Movable properties can be acquired by dint of land acquisition, and no additional act of acquisition (such as lifting) is then required, based on "...<a href="http://bible.cc/2_chronicles/21-3.htm">And their father gave them many gifts of gold and silver, and delicacies, together with the fortified cities in Judah</a>." Since the slaves are inherited like land, based on "...<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/25-46.htm">you shall bequeath them as permanent property</a>..." can one acquire movables together with the slaves? - No, because they move, unlike cities in Judah.<div><br />
<div>
</div>
<div>
One is not liable for damages to properties belonging to the Temple, based on "...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-35.htm">the ox of his fellow</a>..." - his fellow, but not Temple.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Casket of jewels on a table by Pieter Gerritsz van Roestraten</div>
</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/13.txt
<a id="src-00307"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/13.txt`

Bava Kamma 13 - Whose Ox Did the Damage?  (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiuxd3irKwAUIR47qQjKezibJ7eoEP6Y4kmsb3QAzPrQ2Qv2AgheulAob3TY4WN9LbTIlH4hgAjTRPGz7r5KQUMDIO2yaFgoUW536iQBaGi8VKlIuhrfzBwW7AEoLG0R0Bgpwo_0coCnGZQ/s1600-h/W.+J.+Chapman+-+Cattle+Against+A+Landscape+-+1863.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5289912420226961074" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiuxd3irKwAUIR47qQjKezibJ7eoEP6Y4kmsb3QAzPrQ2Qv2AgheulAob3TY4WN9LbTIlH4hgAjTRPGz7r5KQUMDIO2yaFgoUW536iQBaGi8VKlIuhrfzBwW7AEoLG0R0Bgpwo_0coCnGZQ/s320/W.+J.+Chapman+-+Cattle+Against+A+Landscape+-+1863.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 238px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>The laws of damages only apply to privately held properties. Thus, if the identity of the damaging ox is unclear, and the owners of the two suspect oxen each blame the other, one saying, "It was your ox that damaged," while the other one saying, "No, it was your ox that damaged" - the damaged party cannot collect from  either owner.<br />
<br />
One is liable for damage done anywhere except for premises reserved exclusively for the damager. If the damage occurs on his premises, the damager can ask, "What was your ox doing on my premises?"<div><br /></div><div>Art: Cattle Against A Landscape by W. J. Chapman</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/14.txt
<a id="src-00308"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/14.txt`

Bava Kamma 14 - Who Can Judge? (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgMvJCJ5mewNkhqvmr3OzBRfXM9Nbn3dzCei_6cQIfsw0hsP6dsVn7oP63VL2he1u9qPzHU4rUaXu0vjYkCxbuBPFazmeC3Kv8E_q6tIG89ih4XNYsqZgZG99XZbC53EX2X72e_6oSlgy_X/s1600-h/Domenico+Tintoretto+%28Robusti%29+-+Allegory+Of+Virtue+Above+The+Portraits+Of+Three+Lawyers+And+A+Notary.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5290226371032190850" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgMvJCJ5mewNkhqvmr3OzBRfXM9Nbn3dzCei_6cQIfsw0hsP6dsVn7oP63VL2he1u9qPzHU4rUaXu0vjYkCxbuBPFazmeC3Kv8E_q6tIG89ih4XNYsqZgZG99XZbC53EX2X72e_6oSlgy_X/s320/Domenico+Tintoretto+(Robusti)+-+Allegory+Of+Virtue+Above+The+Portraits+Of+Three+Lawyers+And+A+Notary.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 228px;" /></a>If the damage done by the tooth or foot of an animal happened in a jointly owned yard, then if the yard was set for joint use for the eaten produce but not for oxen, the damager is liable.<br />
<br />
Any three knowledgeable persons who have mastered related areas of law can form a court to judge ordinary damages cases. However, unusual cases involving penalties, such as half-damages awarded in the first three instances of goring by an ox, can only be judged by people possessing an uninterrupted chain of ordination since the time of Moses. Therefore, such cases can not be adjudicated today.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Allegory Of Virtue Above The Portraits Of Three Lawyers And A Notary by Domenico Tintoretto (Robusti)</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/15.txt
<a id="src-00309"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/15.txt`

Bava Kamma 15 - Do Normal Oxen Gore? (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhffGVAMNvALICJ96dfauYN6B5tDtbR2bkcJ5UY7-BfA_C3Th8bFRM6veAVdcVJ9we9NrnQwPfhZ-yAtZJDj5w0rKRbsZxO9cv3F1kzsT89dglfsXMa7ADeJWJAiY4RqttqH18FhlayzRE3/s1600-h/Francisco+De+Goya+y+Lucientes+-++Village+Bullfigh.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5290532840779389426" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhffGVAMNvALICJ96dfauYN6B5tDtbR2bkcJ5UY7-BfA_C3Th8bFRM6veAVdcVJ9we9NrnQwPfhZ-yAtZJDj5w0rKRbsZxO9cv3F1kzsT89dglfsXMa7ADeJWJAiY4RqttqH18FhlayzRE3/s400/Francisco+De+Goya+y+Lucientes+-++Village+Bullfigh.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 245px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 400px;" /></a><div>Is the payment of half damages for goring compensation or a penalty?</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-weight: bold;">Compensation argument</span>: It is common for oxen to gore, and they must, therefore, be guarded. By rights, therefore, the ox's owner should pay for all the damage, but the Merciful One took pity on him and reduced his liability by half because this ox had not yet become warned.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-weight: bold;">Penalty argument</span>: oxen do not ordinarily gore or do malicious damage. By rights, therefore, the ox's owner should not have to pay at all, but the Merciful One penalized him in order that he should guard his ox more carefully.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Village Bullfight by Francisco De Goya y Lucientes</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/16.txt
<a id="src-00310"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/16.txt`

Bava Kamma 16 - Usual and Unusual Damagers (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjSK2g_Yhe9JxOcI0egPuGSLVb30YwJYympNUdwTxuGHMzlIv2cYTKGVvVO45AMdrDGjeOjXpyyqv1SLDCfNDEjQMtPK0JYiFN7GrXrUVdO7s-vHAOTs5jCozT-myhr3sKNiyxfl0p7AG4h/s1600-h/Gabriel+Metsu+-+Woman+Eating+And+Feeding+Her+Cat.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5290887160063477762" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjSK2g_Yhe9JxOcI0egPuGSLVb30YwJYympNUdwTxuGHMzlIv2cYTKGVvVO45AMdrDGjeOjXpyyqv1SLDCfNDEjQMtPK0JYiFN7GrXrUVdO7s-vHAOTs5jCozT-myhr3sKNiyxfl0p7AG4h/s320/Gabriel+Metsu+-+Woman+Eating+And+Feeding+Her+Cat.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 260px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">The final decision is that <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-35.htm">half-damages</a> are a penalty. Thus, if a dog killed and ate sheep or a cat killed and ate a chicken, it is a case of unusual damage and not collected in court. However, this only applies to large animals, but small animals are in the "tooth" damage category and can be collected.<br />
<br />
Five damage categories are considered unusual and liable for only half-damage: domestic animals who gore, push, bite, squat, and kick. Among the five damage categories deemed normal, with their owners "warned" of the complete liability: an animal while walking ("foot"), an ox that already gored, and a man that does damage.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Woman Eating And Feeding Her Cat by Gabriel Metsu</span></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/17.txt
<a id="src-00311"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/17.txt`

Bava Kamma 17 - Innocent and Established Damagers (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjilb847swtPB66hu2eRjo4wzNLLqKrXaCLxA-8UPrvCzlmgkrke-S31Ac-lcZD374u2fNrOkkl1V0jisFkggRw46hdNeS7jCNLhdxqGjYqzQLyZASLMz6XLtN5kM7OeBgeRziYjhhOWVl0/s1600-h/Paulus+Potter+-+Four+Bulls.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5298316152972247874" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjilb847swtPB66hu2eRjo4wzNLLqKrXaCLxA-8UPrvCzlmgkrke-S31Ac-lcZD374u2fNrOkkl1V0jisFkggRw46hdNeS7jCNLhdxqGjYqzQLyZASLMz6XLtN5kM7OeBgeRziYjhhOWVl0/s320/Paulus+Potter+-+Four+Bulls.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 262px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a>What difference is there between the half payment in the case of an innocent and the full payment in the case of an established damager? The owner's liability in the case of innocent first-time gorings is <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-35.htm">limited to the value of the ox that did the damage</a>;&nbsp;in the case of established damages, the owner pays the full amount of the damage with his best property.<br />
<br />
Regarding what is the foot of an animal considered an established damager? For breaking things in the course of its walking but not when kicking.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Four Bulls by Paulus Potter</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/18.txt
<a id="src-00312"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/18.txt`

Bava Kamma 18 - Breaking a Broken Utensil (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyXoY06CGUXLYjtMIgU5gZLSQ9Fg4s-7NR1RC7XRZq8UTr4tYS396HbOSkuyeOA5WnA3mkR5jsseVU5Y-9lJZ4_VHwVeZJjatKFg3ztj8Zr6J6vkFHO3jce0nwjvUHtHh1jSEA1MDGCRtv/s1600-h/Willem+Joseph+Laquy+-+A+Scullery+Maid+Preparing+A+Chicken" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5291762289114488626" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyXoY06CGUXLYjtMIgU5gZLSQ9Fg4s-7NR1RC7XRZq8UTr4tYS396HbOSkuyeOA5WnA3mkR5jsseVU5Y-9lJZ4_VHwVeZJjatKFg3ztj8Zr6J6vkFHO3jce0nwjvUHtHh1jSEA1MDGCRtv/s320/Willem+Joseph+Laquy+-+A+Scullery+Maid+Preparing+A+Chicken" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 238px;" /></a>If one threw a utensil from the top of a roof, and someone came along and shattered this utensil in midair with a stick, is the one wielding the stick liable, or has he merely broken a broken utensil? Is the utensil considered broken from the start of the process?<br />
<br />
Can we rely on another ruling: If chickens were pecking at the rope of a bucket, and it snapped, and the bucket broke, the chicken owner is responsible for damages. Is it because the bucket is broken from the beginning of the fall, and thus, the chickens are directly responsible? No! Perhaps the damages refer to the rope.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Scullery Maid Preparing A Chicken by Willem Joseph Laquy</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/19.txt
<a id="src-00313"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/19.txt`

Bava Kamma 19 - Bull breaking vessels with its male organ (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggth-wX1MA0tYANqTad00OfXK6QeS2JZj3dcYoiEgRfNGPM11D-fSah1NUf3tBDJFD6mXLl5RGEz9YLwkDvge3NWS-S6E9oDlEvKfNIGhk-IQwDMlOSOOG6e3D-RfaZNKc9K_1E0Ecrwoc/s1600-h/Aelbert+Cuyp+-+Rooster+and+Hens.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5291982416652588402" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggth-wX1MA0tYANqTad00OfXK6QeS2JZj3dcYoiEgRfNGPM11D-fSah1NUf3tBDJFD6mXLl5RGEz9YLwkDvge3NWS-S6E9oDlEvKfNIGhk-IQwDMlOSOOG6e3D-RfaZNKc9K_1E0Ecrwoc/s320/Aelbert+Cuyp+-+Rooster+and+Hens.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 296px;" /></a><div>If an animal dropped dung onto a dough, ruining it, then it is not similar to pushing with the body, for which the owner pays full damages, but rather to pebbles shooting from under the animal's foot, for which the owner pays half damages.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If a rooster extended its head into the hollow of a glass vessel and shrieked into it, breaking it, then this, too, is similar to pebbles because the rooster did not do damage with his body but with vibrations. But isn't it abnormal for the rooster to do so? Perhaps there were seeds there.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>Consider an animal damaging a vessel by swishing its male organ. Is this similar to horn damage (done of malevolence) or to foot damage (done by just passing by?) Unresolved.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Rooster and Hens by Aelbert Cuyp</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/2.txt
<a id="src-00314"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/2.txt`

Bava Kamma 2 - Four Categories of Damages (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi75vuSHxqiN3bNBc7GnLTMuCFHwmtAdJB6qUS9m0selsMY9S2OYsh9wN4x3qYFXocP6k7zzo8MMg3VjeGqE5jNfl3RljFFdRSFRLToZDAs42Yst6D7uj2ph_kzNdGoxfycok_OOPf01dz_/s1600-h/L%C3%A9on-Augustin+L%27hermitte+-+Heads+of+Two+Oxen.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5285700462254554866" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi75vuSHxqiN3bNBc7GnLTMuCFHwmtAdJB6qUS9m0selsMY9S2OYsh9wN4x3qYFXocP6k7zzo8MMg3VjeGqE5jNfl3RljFFdRSFRLToZDAs42Yst6D7uj2ph_kzNdGoxfycok_OOPf01dz_/s320/L%C3%A9on-Augustin+L%27hermitte+-+Heads+of+Two+Oxen.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 242px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">There are four primary categories of damages, and all other cases can be classified as belonging to one of these: the ox, the pit, the man, and the fire.<br />
<br />
Liability for one can not be deduced from the other. For example, a man is responsible in full for even accidental damage, while the owner of an ox is liable for half the damage the first three times; a fire isn't alive, and a pit doesn't move around.<br />
<br />
However, since they can all cause damage, the owner is responsible for watching over them and paying damages from the choicest land.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Heads of Two Oxen by Leon Augustin L'Hermitte</span></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/20.txt
<a id="src-00315"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/20.txt`

Bava Kamma 20 - "Tooth" damages (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjqN96OKMYbR21IuB1gRs_TQD2lKJYmEVSyKpS4T3P61qfAEIqwnQu9q_jDnSxWpoixbVyhyx0QlgvK9jfzOX6KHGM-RHWVnaZUq8CaBoA_8OtyO3aGsCoMyWTwK1krDFrUlnwB33LzbBb7/s1600-h/Theophile+Alexandre+Steinlen+-+Ete,+Chat+sur+une+Balustrade,+1909" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5292507780513875602" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjqN96OKMYbR21IuB1gRs_TQD2lKJYmEVSyKpS4T3P61qfAEIqwnQu9q_jDnSxWpoixbVyhyx0QlgvK9jfzOX6KHGM-RHWVnaZUq8CaBoA_8OtyO3aGsCoMyWTwK1krDFrUlnwB33LzbBb7/s320/Theophile+Alexandre+Steinlen+-+Ete,+Chat+sur+une+Balustrade,+1909" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 266px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>What are normal "tooth" damages obligating the owner to full payment? Fruits and vegetables. The owner pays only half the damage if an animal eats a garment or utensil. When is this? On the damaged party's premises, but if the animal eats in the public domain, the owner pays only for what he benefited by skipping its next feeding.<br />
<br />
Eating in a pinch, such as cats eating dates and donkeys eating fish, is normal damage.<br />
<br />
If one lives in the yard of his fellow without the latter's knowledge, does he have to pay rent? The inquiry is only in regard to a yard that is not for rent and a person who usually rents.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Ete, Chat sur une Balustrade by Theophile Alexandre Steinlen</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/21.txt
<a id="src-00316"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/21.txt`

Bava Kamma 21 - This One Benefits, The Other One Does not Lose (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpzKIiZF6MkExIn4bj95Q-F74Fmiy_PgXL1xNLZNcQNDv-QCKQ7emTpOCz-TtjIFyOLqXVxsIyJBG7zQ2-cT8bpz8KLwn4HghU5Y45Rglipe84TUckZAaY95DQKUZWPZoCB4J2CKzU_V10/s1600-h/Carl+Vilhelm+Holsoe+-+An+Interior+with+a+Stove+and+a+View+into+a+Dining+Room.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5292823023437789538" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpzKIiZF6MkExIn4bj95Q-F74Fmiy_PgXL1xNLZNcQNDv-QCKQ7emTpOCz-TtjIFyOLqXVxsIyJBG7zQ2-cT8bpz8KLwn4HghU5Y45Rglipe84TUckZAaY95DQKUZWPZoCB4J2CKzU_V10/s320/Carl+Vilhelm+Holsoe+-+An+Interior+with+a+Stove+and+a+View+into+a+Dining+Room.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 273px;" /></a>The case of one living in the house of his fellow without the latter's knowledge is, in essence, "this one benefits and this one does not lose," and the final decision is that the squatter doesn't need to pay rent.<br />
<br />
Additional support for this ruling comes from "...<a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/24-12.htm">through desolation the gate is broken apart</a>," meaning that demons of desolation ruin the house, or alternatively from the reason that the residents see what needs repair and attend to it. What is the practical difference between these two reasons? Using the house for storing wood and straw.<div><br /></div><div>Art: An Interior with a Stove and a View into a Dining Room by Carl Vilhelm Holsoe</div>

---
