<a id="src-00317"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/22.txt`

Bava Kamma 22 - Dog or Kid Jump From a Roof (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyYFj4vA6Wc4UREuClkmL87HK01fBJsBTgUHrTUn1J2SsRCWLVJyDPS0LrIS6vgo4Vu7AZL4qGJxmkWgofuUUxzdj8fRtNhb1sGkYUjRmfPuokTi8nZgNkmVIjXoZLRQtfqUMVhor58bTR/s1600-h/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Peasant+Burning+Weeds.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5293042607490993138" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyYFj4vA6Wc4UREuClkmL87HK01fBJsBTgUHrTUn1J2SsRCWLVJyDPS0LrIS6vgo4Vu7AZL4qGJxmkWgofuUUxzdj8fRtNhb1sGkYUjRmfPuokTi8nZgNkmVIjXoZLRQtfqUMVhor58bTR/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Peasant+Burning+Weeds.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 243px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If a dog or a goat kid jumped from the top of a roof and broke the utensils it landed on below, the animal's owner pays full damages. If it fell? This opinion implies that the owner is not liable. Still, the final law is that the owner is responsible in a situation that begins with negligence and ends in an unavoidable mishap.<br />
<br />
If a dog took the biscuit from the coals and went to a stack of grain sheaves, where it ate the biscuit and set fire to the stack, for the biscuit, the dog's owner pays full damages, and for the stack, he pays half the damage.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Peasant Burning Weeds by Vincent Van Gogh</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/23.txt
<a id="src-00318"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/23.txt`

Bava Kamma 23 - Fire Damages (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhy0ZZPhg0_Bk2Iy0h86QAKXdf5L4TAsUXWTf8hcZbGplLnvSzb0DF0KDXXHcPvfBnKq6tQb1qKRtSscwiKFyIF9uXNt0mwNJj6AMc_bpCf710MP3VaLlKWmPgd2w1KDZUpwifw3BYEDviT/s1600-h/Jean+Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric+Bazille+-+The+Improvised+Field+Hospital.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5293580469853713074" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhy0ZZPhg0_Bk2Iy0h86QAKXdf5L4TAsUXWTf8hcZbGplLnvSzb0DF0KDXXHcPvfBnKq6tQb1qKRtSscwiKFyIF9uXNt0mwNJj6AMc_bpCf710MP3VaLlKWmPgd2w1KDZUpwifw3BYEDviT/s320/Jean+Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric+Bazille+-+The+Improvised+Field+Hospital.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 238px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If a person lit a fire in his field and the fire spread, that person is liable. Is that fire his "property,” and he is liable only for the damages, or is it “arrows" - his own force, and he is liable also for pain, healing, and unemployment? The answer is that it is like "arrows."<br />
<br />
A cow is only liable for eating someone else's fruit if it veered into someone's field. The cow's owner could try to claim that the cow's mouth is his premises, and "What is your fruit doing in my cow's mouth?" but the above case of a dog that ate a biscuit precludes this.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Improvised Field Hospital by Jean Frederic Bazille</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/24.txt
<a id="src-00319"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/24.txt`

Bava Kamma 24 - From Warned Back To Innocent (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgB2CbjGWBUeynjxaz0n7gW3XF5PcJpgzhZOt-x9X5BlXv1IsMUCaPcTo7fVx9voAfVva1RCEecQZ-IwglpZ7hmS88TPKrQORvlgbigpWCnev3sxKp_6vCObZtXxXnEGCoDy0J-Eovwp5Vb/s1600-h/Alfred+Dehodencq+-+Combat+De+Novillos.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5293880166267403410" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgB2CbjGWBUeynjxaz0n7gW3XF5PcJpgzhZOt-x9X5BlXv1IsMUCaPcTo7fVx9voAfVva1RCEecQZ-IwglpZ7hmS88TPKrQORvlgbigpWCnev3sxKp_6vCObZtXxXnEGCoDy0J-Eovwp5Vb/s320/Alfred+Dehodencq+-+Combat+De+Novillos.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 223px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><div>An innocent ox becomes "warned" for damages, and its owner becomes liable for complete payment after three gorings, which must happen on three different days, according to Rabbi Yehudah, or even on one day, according to Rabbi Meir.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-36.htm">The source</a>: "...from (1) yesterday (2) and before yesterday (3)..."</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
It reverts to "innocent" if it is confronted by circumstances that triggered goring the first three times yet now desists from this behavior on three separate days. Rabbi Meir adds that it reverts to "innocent" any time the children poke it between the horns and does not gore.</div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: Combat De Novillos by Alfred Dehodencq</div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" color="rgb(85 , 26 , 139)" style="text-decoration: underline;"><br /></span></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/25.txt
<a id="src-00320"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/25.txt`

Bava Kamma 25 - Ox on the Premises of Damaged Party (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj10JFzgbTL2_7syOCJxwfMvKWPmcnA01K8JgW5FzddwmHXo3cLNy-MrtDCCFnV5xpd5QV5x9vsm1XvOoXI_-bzgHthIBu_Bnwz9SWG4dGjf1_oKVseklJYoDoh3OovBC4ZN_0YU13oD4Za/s1600-h/John+Sell+Cotman+-+Ruined+House.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5294233761898852098" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj10JFzgbTL2_7syOCJxwfMvKWPmcnA01K8JgW5FzddwmHXo3cLNy-MrtDCCFnV5xpd5QV5x9vsm1XvOoXI_-bzgHthIBu_Bnwz9SWG4dGjf1_oKVseklJYoDoh3OovBC4ZN_0YU13oD4Za/s320/John+Sell+Cotman+-+Ruined+House.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 268px;" /></a><div><div>If an ox gored, pushed, bit, squatted, or kicked and thereby damaged something, then in the public domain, its owner pays half the damages. On the premises of the injured party, Rabbi Tarfon says: "Full damages," but the Sages say: "Half damages."</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Rabbi Tarfon said: "Consider a lenient case of tooth or foot in the public domain, where the owner is not liable to pay at all, yet on the premises of the damaged party, the owner would pay full damages. Is it not logical to require full payment in my stricter case?" And the Sages? Logic can make the payment equal but not increase it.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Ruined House by John Sell Cotman</div>
</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/26.txt
<a id="src-00321"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/26.txt`

Bava Kamma 26 - A Man Is Always Warned for Damages (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhNrjExQ8f3JUsedOoOPCA1VFce2jUuI-qTbZspetfBiB_01pZh9wrYsNm4c408ToXbt8P_xoS1SHesGF589GRBFdBnVb6MHuCx5m5XTiqTC0a2sdzB4APo3tgQaMUqw2LOXg5VRiyTVvzM/s1600-h/Jusepe+de+Ribera+-+Blind+Beggar+And+His+Boy+1632.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5294590415675766786" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhNrjExQ8f3JUsedOoOPCA1VFce2jUuI-qTbZspetfBiB_01pZh9wrYsNm4c408ToXbt8P_xoS1SHesGF589GRBFdBnVb6MHuCx5m5XTiqTC0a2sdzB4APo3tgQaMUqw2LOXg5VRiyTVvzM/s320/Jusepe+de+Ribera+-+Blind+Beggar+And+His+Boy+1632.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 258px;" /></a><div>A man is never innocent regarding damages in that he always pays in full for whatever he damages, whether he did the damage unintentionally or intentionally while awake or asleep. If he blinded the eye of his fellow or he broke utensils, he pays full damages.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
By grouping the “blinding” and “breaking utensils,” this ruling teaches that just as in the case of utensils, he pays for the actual damage <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-18.htm">but not the</a> &nbsp;“four things” - pain, healing, unemployment, and humiliation - so too if he blinded the eye of his fellow unintentionally, he pays for the actual damages but not the “four things.”</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Blind Beggar And His Boy by Jusepe de Ribera</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/27.txt
<a id="src-00322"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/27.txt`

Bava Kamma 27 - Liability of Two People Killing a Child (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEitS2CDbsGIK9srQ4I_GFNoKGt3tVa36tq5kpzRvkwd7JxiH3LcJY8tOm92uOXgw_XCukDEHY5mW0s8x0zO0Z_7KyPK4uzKH0Zc1wAmFCOH4PI-TrXL5PA1EVNDgOLn1iERMxCJi99T7lkr/s1600-h/Jan+Jansz.+den+Uyl+-+Still+life+with+an+overturned+jug,+c.1632-37.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5295096050440359826" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEitS2CDbsGIK9srQ4I_GFNoKGt3tVa36tq5kpzRvkwd7JxiH3LcJY8tOm92uOXgw_XCukDEHY5mW0s8x0zO0Z_7KyPK4uzKH0Zc1wAmFCOH4PI-TrXL5PA1EVNDgOLn1iERMxCJi99T7lkr/s320/Jan+Jansz.+den+Uyl+-+Still+life+with+an+overturned+jug,+c.1632-37.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 282px;" /></a>Suppose one threw a child off the roof, and another met the falling child with an upturned sword. In that case, Rabbi Yehudah ben Beteira says that the one wielding the sword is liable to execution because he hastened the child's death. Still, the Rabbis absolve him because the child is considered partly dead. They argue if "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/24-17.htm">all human life</a>"&nbsp;means any or all of it.<br />
<br />
If one places a jug in the public domain and another comes and stumbles and breaks it, the pedestrian is not liable. If the pedestrian was damaged by it, the owner of the jug is liable.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Still life with an overturned jug by Jan Jansz. den Uyl</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/28.txt
<a id="src-00323"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/28.txt`

Bava Kamma 28 - Can a Man Take Law into his own Hands? (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj90OtLsY3_BIicuBlm_K03lB7UIfrKK4GLzDlzmCIOxws6wV9OBG0Ei38mBlZ9nx7vtTY6YG9i-Q0vYqjMkyJeQaARzUNytsvY7_Sr2aBziXznuHYm1ChVBFhOqZuaUYanhlabHTd6xSo7/s1600-h/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Two+Peasants+Digging.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5295433486647156610" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj90OtLsY3_BIicuBlm_K03lB7UIfrKK4GLzDlzmCIOxws6wV9OBG0Ei38mBlZ9nx7vtTY6YG9i-Q0vYqjMkyJeQaARzUNytsvY7_Sr2aBziXznuHYm1ChVBFhOqZuaUYanhlabHTd6xSo7/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Two+Peasants+Digging.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 250px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Two partners were drawing water out of a cistern on alternative days, and one came to draw on a day that was not his. The other one stopped him with a stick.<br />
<br />
Rav Yehudah says that a person may not enforce the law for himself, but Rav Nachman says he may. They argue about a case where there will be no loss if he does not take action.<br />
<br />
Rav Yehudah explains: "Since there will be no loss, let him go before the judge." Rav Nachman says: "Since he is acting in accordance with the law, he does not have to trouble himself and go before the judge."<div><br /></div><div>Art: Two Peasants Digging by Vincent Van Gogh</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/29.txt
<a id="src-00324"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/29.txt`

Bava Kamma 29 - Responsibility for One's Objects (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhVUdQ38rEbIFUDTN0p199E5eyfn_DsIvZJG30flS2weoRKr-EqToBAsAWvNOliqQAKOsZYcAPmN2A6alQYtjmQVL1Dsgvb40rQ8FVdfd7XGejcxrDYYjsY9PLHhrtYiHjfrKlM2B-q9N7H/s1600-h/Jean+Baptiste+Simeon+Chardin+-+The+Cellar+Boy.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5295780254049028114" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhVUdQ38rEbIFUDTN0p199E5eyfn_DsIvZJG30flS2weoRKr-EqToBAsAWvNOliqQAKOsZYcAPmN2A6alQYtjmQVL1Dsgvb40rQ8FVdfd7XGejcxrDYYjsY9PLHhrtYiHjfrKlM2B-q9N7H/s320/Jean+Baptiste+Simeon+Chardin+-+The+Cellar+Boy.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 258px;" /></a>If one pitcher of water broke in the public domain, and another person slipped in the water, Rabbi Yehudah makes the owner of the pitcher liable only when he at least intended to put the pitcher down. Rabbi Meir makes him liable even when he stumbled or if the pitcher broke by itself; if a camel stumbled, he is liable if he stumbled first and the camel tripped over him.<br />
<br />
They also argue after the breakage: one maintains that if a person leaves his hazardous objects and declares them ownerless, he is liable, while the other one maintains that the person is not liable.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Cellar Boy by Jean Baptiste Simeon Chardin</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/3.txt
<a id="src-00325"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/3.txt`

Bava Kamma 3 - All Damages Are Not Equal (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhOFjJEa19hpmNhATdMF0lx6YkIr3wVV0HaeN66yq2W6pgHDH8bo1SSPSXC834CGUJQxzEo-iaos7-O1ISigaF1MYMjA2B8l69yG3iw9cPoTKZDo33SWUueLmXwKvj8Eg3LRaJ28u5llEX_/s1600-h/A-Short-Horned-Heifer,-Engraved-By-William-Ward,-Dartington,-1811.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5286175815744537538" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhOFjJEa19hpmNhATdMF0lx6YkIr3wVV0HaeN66yq2W6pgHDH8bo1SSPSXC834CGUJQxzEo-iaos7-O1ISigaF1MYMjA2B8l69yG3iw9cPoTKZDo33SWUueLmXwKvj8Eg3LRaJ28u5llEX_/s320/A-Short-Horned-Heifer,-Engraved-By-William-Ward,-Dartington,-1811.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 240px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Goring (using horns) is unique in that the ox's intent is to damage, and the ox is the owner's property who needs to watch it; its subcategories include squatting and kicking.<br />
<br />
Eating (tooth) is unique in that the animal's intent is for self-gratification; its subcategories include an animal scratching against the wall or soiling fruit by frolicking on it.<br />
<br />
Do subcategories have the same laws as the main damages? Mostly yes, except in a case where a cow was walking, and a pebble shot from under its foot and broke vessels, for which the owner pays only half the damages.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;A Short-Horned Heifer, Engraved By William Ward Dartington</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/30.txt
<a id="src-00326"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/30.txt`

Bava Kamma 30 - Pouring Water out in the Street (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEioTxPUS7EltbYYF9rU4gqeGCyflFngR5HG9yeNSLCIMNf7Xg4MpR5sF0Q4D-hu1A97BBEF1IJ4k2XlmCXziZSSGAlvdQB3kXSfSZFPJB3tvUyqjPPH-WuNTfrx4CQmlrUY0QZuugzDq5l0/s1600-h/Alfred+Sisley+-+The+Boat+in+the+Flood,+Port-Marly,+1876.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5296162597031982850" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEioTxPUS7EltbYYF9rU4gqeGCyflFngR5HG9yeNSLCIMNf7Xg4MpR5sF0Q4D-hu1A97BBEF1IJ4k2XlmCXziZSSGAlvdQB3kXSfSZFPJB3tvUyqjPPH-WuNTfrx4CQmlrUY0QZuugzDq5l0/s320/Alfred+Sisley+-+The+Boat+in+the+Flood,+Port-Marly,+1876.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 266px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Suppose one puts straw or stubble into the public domain to be converted into manure by people and animals stepping on it, and another person is damaged by it. In that case, the owner of the straw is liable for damages, and whoever is the first to take the straw acquires it – but we do not publicly announce this last law.<br />
<br />
Even in those cases where it is allowed to put hazardous objects out, such as pouring water out in the street in a rainy season, if a passerby is damaged, the one who poured out the water is liable.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Boat in the Flood by Alfred Sisley</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/31.txt
<a id="src-00327"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/31.txt`

Bava Kamma 31 - Potter Stumbled and Fell (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3mG6GyeOjUPg37IeimUkWX-OZX2Y_B-sKF-5mk33VftKpBsGRkkfZgPpBZMjK1ZDnLHB-OEzuBAVUL5RHEpSk9_wn7cRhchS8QXmYcbQMcfXRrkm4hF3urcYuOmFw2LFmxeVWUWI6-8U-/s1600-h/Sir+Lawrence+Alma-Tadema+-Pottery+Painting.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5296452970709077842" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3mG6GyeOjUPg37IeimUkWX-OZX2Y_B-sKF-5mk33VftKpBsGRkkfZgPpBZMjK1ZDnLHB-OEzuBAVUL5RHEpSk9_wn7cRhchS8QXmYcbQMcfXRrkm4hF3urcYuOmFw2LFmxeVWUWI6-8U-/s320/Sir+Lawrence+Alma-Tadema+-Pottery+Painting.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 225px;" /></a><div>If two potters were walking one behind the other in the public domain, and the first one stumbled and fell, and then the second one stumbled and fell over the first, the first one is liable for the damages to the second.&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Although the potter lying on the ground caused the damage passively, this is a case of damage inflicted by "man" since the obstacle was his body. He is consequently liable even for the damage to the second person's utensils. Although stumbling is not negligence, he should have warned the person behind him.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Pottery Painting by Sir Lawrence Alma-Tadema</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/32.txt
<a id="src-00328"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/32.txt`

Bava Kamma 32 - Running Before Shabbat (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjj2c6R6Y_hH5cTO8qPLanLoeLl-xNdvNzur0zh0oMBO0diSL0wt-SySWH8g5s0VLqySEQpi0xz_wKRaygW_Xgk9H6SNCTnAxVwco0-96SB_tOEkXCH1Zw434GNWljtctBtO3m2XBEsBkSC/s1600-h/George+Frederick+Watts+-+Two+Young+Women+Walking.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5296953302391899474" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjj2c6R6Y_hH5cTO8qPLanLoeLl-xNdvNzur0zh0oMBO0diSL0wt-SySWH8g5s0VLqySEQpi0xz_wKRaygW_Xgk9H6SNCTnAxVwco0-96SB_tOEkXCH1Zw434GNWljtctBtO3m2XBEsBkSC/s320/George+Frederick+Watts+-+Two+Young+Women+Walking.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 238px;" /></a>If two people were walking in the public thoroughfare, one was running, and one was walking, or both were running and did damage to one another, both are not liable to pay damages.<br />
<br />
Said Rabbi Yochanan, - This ruling only talks about the time right before Shabbat, when running for the sake of Shabbat is allowed, but otherwise the one who runs is liable.<br />
<br />
Suppose one chops wood in the public domain and thereby does damage in the private domain, or chops in the private domain and damages something in the public domain, or chops in private and damages something in the private domain. In all the cases, he is liable for full damages.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Two Young Women Walking by George Frederick Watts</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/33.txt
<a id="src-00329"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/33.txt`

Bava Kamma 33 - Damages in Fighting (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUHfwjy-hsrFQi0laZxjA1MkWnZQWdO9RdxP2RSnK8n2yuLThtaQWyrIDU2MyzKxsLJUTigLBKu0sCFulmZzfsoRnMGxJYdz4VXIvtTjAi9KlE_SJEP403SfBY4A27SspTyCG11DBB_xHb/s1600-h/James+Ward+-+Portraits+of+two+extraordinary+oxen,+the+property+of+the+Earl+of+Powis,+1814.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5297170200127156866" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUHfwjy-hsrFQi0laZxjA1MkWnZQWdO9RdxP2RSnK8n2yuLThtaQWyrIDU2MyzKxsLJUTigLBKu0sCFulmZzfsoRnMGxJYdz4VXIvtTjAi9KlE_SJEP403SfBY4A27SspTyCG11DBB_xHb/s320/James+Ward+-+Portraits+of+two+extraordinary+oxen,+the+property+of+the+Earl+of+Powis,+1814.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 210px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If two oxen not previously warned for goring fought and injured one another, then the owner of the less-damaged one pays the other owner half the difference in damages.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If the owners of both were warned that the oxen have gored three times, one pays for the excess full damages.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If one ox was innocent and another one warned, then if the damage done by the warned one is more significant, the owner pays for the excess full damages. If the damage done by the innocent one is more significant, the owner pays for the extra half of the damage.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Similarly, if two people injure one another, they pay for the excess full damages.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Portraits of two extraordinary oxen, the property of the Earl of Powis by James Ward</div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/34.txt
<a id="src-00330"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/34.txt`

Bava Kamma 34 - Half The Loss (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgUgkHMHL7l3zIyAkZCnkNUg3C2d-Sci5enPSzRQ0oc-8pVq2oz6VmSaprxK1QtXfOLAn0TJmaVYNJ6kNZ9ygBSzEeABwaHaXSe2k-ytSTivrgOLj75AJ1BMS0XGUcJXeEi4c8g8F0MBtxn/s1600-h/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Oxen+Resting.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5297703989613040322" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgUgkHMHL7l3zIyAkZCnkNUg3C2d-Sci5enPSzRQ0oc-8pVq2oz6VmSaprxK1QtXfOLAn0TJmaVYNJ6kNZ9ygBSzEeABwaHaXSe2k-ytSTivrgOLj75AJ1BMS0XGUcJXeEi4c8g8F0MBtxn/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Oxen+Resting.JPG" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 254px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>"<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-35.htm">And if a man's ox shall push the ox of his fellow, and it dies, they shall sell the live ox and divide its money, and the dead one, too, they shall divide.</a>"&nbsp;What are the precise circumstances?<br />
<br />
In the case of one ox worth two hundred <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zuz_%28coin%29">zuz</a> that gored another ox worth two hundred and the carcass is worth fifty, one owner takes half of the live ox and half of the dead one, and so does the other. Thus, each party suffers half the loss, and the damager can pay the carcass as a partial payment.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Oxen Resting by John Singer Sargent</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/35.txt
<a id="src-00331"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/35.txt`

Bava Kamma 35 - Oxen in Hot Pursuit (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhYaNgU9i7Ugp_mp_5qhNH5oae205iKA-W6uVG25WO_awmO0XbQvtSpLc2q9XlEESbT5Er7LxzeSlXxaXZeTiI7oChqy2LTkIVBgMCFczqyfuOeYSNmHhQeQ7nApAqY9VsuE5vFKVfRJDwV/s1600-h/Teutwart+Schmitson+-+The+team+of+oxen+breaks+loose.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5298024242008810162" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhYaNgU9i7Ugp_mp_5qhNH5oae205iKA-W6uVG25WO_awmO0XbQvtSpLc2q9XlEESbT5Er7LxzeSlXxaXZeTiI7oChqy2LTkIVBgMCFczqyfuOeYSNmHhQeQ7nApAqY9VsuE5vFKVfRJDwV/s320/Teutwart+Schmitson+-+The+team+of+oxen+breaks+loose.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 254px;" /></a>Imagine an ox was pursuing another ox, and the pursued ox was later found damaged. The damaged party says: "Your ox caused the damage," but the owner of the pursuing ox says, "Not so; it injured itself on a rock." The burden of proof rests on the one who seeks to exact money from his fellow.<br />
<br />
If two oxen were pursuing an ox and it was later found damaged, and the owner of one pursuing ox says, "Your ox did the damage," but the owner of the other states, "No, your ox did the damage" - both are exempt, because each can shift the blame to the other.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The team of oxen breaks loose by Teutwart Schmitson</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/36.txt
<a id="src-00332"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/36.txt`

Bava Kamma 36 - One Innocent Ox Gores Many (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiz2_dqm48r2jS8ildDgI3QwnE4WDkaOOmLpJDli7pp3ZCb1iTZNhSxx5xXnGp6rEippcK-WscoV91Ad8VEmaW9Z6f0UobynDUDLzbDJ-ZAk_DJE_CifdGj24t5KaAt_aF8Smvfdq4kAdyS/s1600-h/George+Catlin+-+Buffalo+Bulls+Fighting+in+Running+Season,+Upper+Missouri,+1837-39.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5298304150594700690" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiz2_dqm48r2jS8ildDgI3QwnE4WDkaOOmLpJDli7pp3ZCb1iTZNhSxx5xXnGp6rEippcK-WscoV91Ad8VEmaW9Z6f0UobynDUDLzbDJ-ZAk_DJE_CifdGj24t5KaAt_aF8Smvfdq4kAdyS/s320/George+Catlin+-+Buffalo+Bulls+Fighting+in+Running+Season,+Upper+Missouri,+1837-39.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 259px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If one ox gores many oxen while remaining innocent (Tam), its owner pays the owner of the last of the gored oxen his half-damage payment from the body of the ox that gored. If the ox is worth more than this payment, the excess goes to the one before, and so on - says Rabbi Meir. Why this order? In this case, each successive damaged party seized the ox as payment and became its guardian.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Rabbi Shimon says that the owners immediately become partners in the goring ox. Thus, each successive victim bears part of the responsibility for the further gorings, paying, for example, 100 zuz, 50, and 25, respectively.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Buffalo Bulls Fighting in Running Season, Upper Missouri by George Catlin</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/37.txt
<a id="src-00333"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/37.txt`

Bava Kamma 37 - At Times, Innocent, at Other Times, Malicious (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgOdajjJZ9C4y_5p57qqQ1ldE4EMacONYhoJIHRSu9EOU7Jvg2BqK_nDFaRaDrbdnxreICX9xr2RbVY5OMHesR4_ZEuF6D9lWP4O5KLm_JTHnCUdG8hxyIJpqiqPdTmCNb2rKNIsyHTzQGA/s1600-h/Van-Gogh+-+Autoportrait.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5298659732307666706" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgOdajjJZ9C4y_5p57qqQ1ldE4EMacONYhoJIHRSu9EOU7Jvg2BqK_nDFaRaDrbdnxreICX9xr2RbVY5OMHesR4_ZEuF6D9lWP4O5KLm_JTHnCUdG8hxyIJpqiqPdTmCNb2rKNIsyHTzQGA/s320/Van-Gogh+-+Autoportrait.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 281px;" /></a><div>Chanan the Wicked delivered a blow to the ear of a particular person. Rav Huna told Chanan, "Give the victim half a zuz." Chanan had a worn-out zuz but couldn't change it. He delivered a second blow to the other ear and gave the person the zuz.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If an ox is warned regarding its own species but not other species, or regarding young animals but not mature animals, the owner pays full damages where warned but half damages where he was not warned. Students asked Rabbi Yehudah about an ox warned for goring on Sabbath. He said, "For goring on Sabbath, he pays full damages, on weekdays, half-damages."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Autoportrait by Van-Gogh</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/38.txt
<a id="src-00334"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/38.txt`

Bava Kamma 38 - The Ox of One's Fellow (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiT0wsAMzHt_m1zHdi6zdSAZQmEq5CZ0jbzZtQkP6iMjk7rBH0aKoU038oXBZ-dX3f9uKIZPsqu1jcqGOezy3r3mDYSJ50aHkNJjgxTsV4iP8f3tmUbHDjOpYbEMMuw3cLPwS2OJtMR2bjW/s1600-h/Paulus+Potter+-+A+Husbandman+with+his+Herd+1648.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5299026583530085890" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiT0wsAMzHt_m1zHdi6zdSAZQmEq5CZ0jbzZtQkP6iMjk7rBH0aKoU038oXBZ-dX3f9uKIZPsqu1jcqGOezy3r3mDYSJ50aHkNJjgxTsV4iP8f3tmUbHDjOpYbEMMuw3cLPwS2OJtMR2bjW/s320/Paulus+Potter+-+A+Husbandman+with+his+Herd+1648.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 214px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If the ox of a Jew gored an ox of the Temple treasury, or if an ox of the Temple treasury gored the ox of a Jew, the owner is exempt: "<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-35.htm">...ox of his fellow...</a>"&nbsp;- and not an ox of the Temple treasury.<br />
<br />
If the ox of a Jew gored the ox of a Canaanite, the Jew was exempt. Still, if the ox of a Canaanite gored the ox of a Jew, the Canaanite paid full damages – a penalty on Canaanites who had no court system and were generally not careful about other people's possessions (Meiri), thus not applicable today.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Husbandman with his Herd by Paulus Potter</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/39.txt
<a id="src-00335"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/39.txt`

Bava Kamma 39 - Deaf-Mute, Deranged, and Minor Who Damage (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh2vDi8_WOgR9280_TEkAjVjTNEuizpfTTHGasQAceMoKkaGJ3CtNWl1jJaX0xY5y4DwsQNL8y26ZM4Afm02l1qft5dWzPXb0ENmQ6DKvNw6hyMjh_AD_QBE-ZUaQ6A-KoA2dMWSxtRuF-d/s1600-h/Ricardo+Canals+y+Llambi+-+Corrida+De+Toros.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5299394689914108674" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh2vDi8_WOgR9280_TEkAjVjTNEuizpfTTHGasQAceMoKkaGJ3CtNWl1jJaX0xY5y4DwsQNL8y26ZM4Afm02l1qft5dWzPXb0ENmQ6DKvNw6hyMjh_AD_QBE-ZUaQ6A-KoA2dMWSxtRuF-d/s320/Ricardo+Canals+y+Llambi+-+Corrida+De+Toros.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 238px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If the ox of a competent person gored the ox of a deaf-mute from birth, deranged, or a minor, the owner is liable, but in the reverse situation, the owner is exempt.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If the ox of an incompetent person gored someone, the court appoints an agent to watch over the ox and then accepts testimony in the agent's presence. Rabbi Meir says that the goring ox reverts to innocence if the minor becomes an adult, but Rabbi Yehudah says it remains warned.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Ordinarily, an ox that kills a man is put to death, but it is not liable if an ox of the arena kills.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Corrida De Toros by Ricardo Canals y Llambi</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/4.txt
<a id="src-00336"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/4.txt`

Bava Kamma 4 - How to Translate Mav'eh? (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhc0svspuAMdA6VOt8QG1I_Ws8f1Ajl5Q2HnslfVGFPw0OxoNQsDP0JUVAizZYDdSp_c1ukHK-twvdQQftrxje4eMzxFgrpOR6ab5wUOgKZpY-PEAdd-s8ShfVDqOmvZIvyPYtrqt_s9VK4/s1600-h/Gerrit+Dou+Extraction+of+the+tooth.jpeg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5286531517190585282" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhc0svspuAMdA6VOt8QG1I_Ws8f1Ajl5Q2HnslfVGFPw0OxoNQsDP0JUVAizZYDdSp_c1ukHK-twvdQQftrxje4eMzxFgrpOR6ab5wUOgKZpY-PEAdd-s8ShfVDqOmvZIvyPYtrqt_s9VK4/s320/Gerrit+Dou+Extraction+of+the+tooth.jpeg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 266px;" /></a>Out of the four damagers: ox, pit, man, and fire, the term for "man" or "ma'veh" can have  various translations. Rav translates ma'veh as a seeker or man; Shmuel translates it as the "tooth" of an animal consuming produce. Then how does this "tooth" differ from an ox? The intent of eating (tooth) is to have pleasure, while the intent of goring (ox) is to harm.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Oshaya listed thirteen primary damages: unpaid custodian, borrower, paid custodian, renter, bully, pain, healing, unemployment, and humiliation, plus the four primary damagers above. Why does the Mishna not include these? - It listed man and meant all types of damage inflicted by man.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Extraction of the Tooth by Gerrit Dou</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/40.txt
<a id="src-00337"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/40.txt`

Bava Kamma 40 - Borrowing a Goring Ox By Mistake (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjRruCpIpbEgbFNS5wy9MSoegIfMrO5x_OVW-9MX9sfe5m37KfXnYkFIUlTWxh-7A4kBLB_vV2t2DAi76-ya33VZ4OjbceAlNxsUr7izOv6exIuIuW4ExIuymQ13UJW2wIBb9x7Xm5luXpD/s1600-h/William+Huggins+-+Lion.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5299771356588600882" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjRruCpIpbEgbFNS5wy9MSoegIfMrO5x_OVW-9MX9sfe5m37KfXnYkFIUlTWxh-7A4kBLB_vV2t2DAi76-ya33VZ4OjbceAlNxsUr7izOv6exIuIuW4ExIuymQ13UJW2wIBb9x7Xm5luXpD/s320/William+Huggins+-+Lion.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 220px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If one borrowed an ox on the assumption that it is innocent and is found to have been warned for goring, then if it is under the borrower's care, the owner pays half-damages, while under the borrower's car, he pays full damages.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
But why?&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Borrower: "I borrowed an ox, not a lion!"&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Owner: "I told you it was aggressive, so you had to guard it. And even if it were innocent, you would pay half the damages."</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Borrower: "For the innocent, the payment comes from its body."</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Owner: "Even so, you would then repay me for the ox."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Lion by William Huggins</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/41.txt
<a id="src-00338"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/41.txt`

Bava Kamma 41 - An Ox Kills a Man (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi07sRCEGcGC8_KzVLSaK-fhPGiP5i0NqJiEwAa5edUcEDK6B6U9u5I1x9XtP0PIhzbJjhcPimM87i2_CAy02ukRczsNT9xrsGvWCjQao_VYwymJmxhaylDXoydCBRyeexni9WsCMX53Wb_/s1600-h/Elihu+Vedder+-+The+Dead+Alchemist+1868.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5300286434155752754" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi07sRCEGcGC8_KzVLSaK-fhPGiP5i0NqJiEwAa5edUcEDK6B6U9u5I1x9XtP0PIhzbJjhcPimM87i2_CAy02ukRczsNT9xrsGvWCjQao_VYwymJmxhaylDXoydCBRyeexni9WsCMX53Wb_/s320/Elihu+Vedder+-+The+Dead+Alchemist+1868.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 227px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If an <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-29.htm">ox gored a person and he died</a>, then if the ox was warned for goring, its owner pays <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-30.htm">redemption payment</a>, and if it was innocent, he is exempt from redemption, but in both cases, the ox is liable to death.<br />
<br />
The same law holds where the <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-31.htm">victim was a minor</a>.<br />
<br />
If the ox gored a <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-32.htm">Canaanite slave or a maidservant</a>, the ox is stoned, and the owner gives thirty sela  (about $5,000) no matter whether the slave is worth a hundred times more or a hundred times less than this amount.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Dead Alchemist by Elihu Vedder</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/42.txt
<a id="src-00339"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/42.txt`

Bava Kamma 42 - Can't Benefit From This Ox (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjfLDo7e5JJF_lvBsq6uVZOGfo5xO2Tzern4KuZL2v2DmE-qei4WWu64RhfSonPFfYFDhhijH6AxPJR0MX4C-jlCzl-S8-23Q5bXGin9LKfwwUjMIr0AK0wUPPGG9rwG4s7XXi-9qHQRPms/s1600-h/Frans+Snyders+-+Cook+with+Food+1630s.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5300656823367021650" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjfLDo7e5JJF_lvBsq6uVZOGfo5xO2Tzern4KuZL2v2DmE-qei4WWu64RhfSonPFfYFDhhijH6AxPJR0MX4C-jlCzl-S8-23Q5bXGin9LKfwwUjMIr0AK0wUPPGG9rwG4s7XXi-9qHQRPms/s320/Frans+Snyders+-+Cook+with+Food+1630s.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 233px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-28.htm">"If an ox shall gore a man or a woman and he shall die, the ox shall surely be stoned; its flesh may not be eaten, and the owner of the ox shall be innocent."</a><br />
<br />
Since "... the ox shall surely be stoned..." means that it died without proper slaughtering and is forbidden for consumption, "...its flesh may not be eaten..." teaches that even if the owner slaughtered it, its meat is still prohibited.<br />
<br />
And "...the owner of the ox shall be innocent (clean)..." teaches that he can't sell it, as people say, "so-and-so has gone out clean of his possessions."<div><br /></div><div>Art: Cook with Food by Frans Snyders</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/43.txt
<a id="src-00340"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/43.txt`

Bava Kamma 43 - Damages Collected After Death (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjPK4Lv_YEeMt2zUWgIJGwx0PUIgLbBgUSx_F5GzYleXYMAD0LzUAGDzQ-EtRApddFN3wefzCSvRYNU5CFYQCY1uj9mOoQbqjh48s7BWSU6HkkYmi8qVtAZdv6I5meJQ79W1BsuQzqIxpZy/s1600-h/Edgar+Degas+-+Edmond+And+Therese+Morbilli.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5300885197379316610" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjPK4Lv_YEeMt2zUWgIJGwx0PUIgLbBgUSx_F5GzYleXYMAD0LzUAGDzQ-EtRApddFN3wefzCSvRYNU5CFYQCY1uj9mOoQbqjh48s7BWSU6HkkYmi8qVtAZdv6I5meJQ79W1BsuQzqIxpZy/s320/Edgar+Degas+-+Edmond+And+Therese+Morbilli.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 242px;" /></a><div>What does the phrase "<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-29.htm">...and it killed a man or a woman...</a>" teach us? To make the owner of a goring ox liable to redemption payment for the killing of a woman as for a man? No, it is already written: "...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-28.htm">if an ox shall gore a man or a woman</a>..." &nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Instead, to equate a woman with a man in damages: if a man dies before collecting, his damage payments go to his heirs, so too does a woman - her damage payments go to her heirs and not to her husband – because the husband inherits only the actual assets that the wife possessed at the time of her death.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Edmond And Therese Morbilli by Edgar Degas</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/44.txt
<a id="src-00341"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/44.txt`

Bava Kamma 44 - An Ox That Did Not Mean To Kill (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhk0PazLGZw0cWCd0GBTlq7Y3XKykmqywUARQFZsPzo7ZZt2PM_IJh0wJuWvSNzDfwcII1bZJt-gE1GhOqK8DUR0LWjRLNffj_LuEu3xB0B75lY9aPlRIjZprRM5Gui01Gt_0Dam8L1uC5W/s1600-h/Thomas+Jones+-++A+Wall+In+Naples.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5301269843867453938" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhk0PazLGZw0cWCd0GBTlq7Y3XKykmqywUARQFZsPzo7ZZt2PM_IJh0wJuWvSNzDfwcII1bZJt-gE1GhOqK8DUR0LWjRLNffj_LuEu3xB0B75lY9aPlRIjZprRM5Gui01Gt_0Dam8L1uC5W/s320/Thomas+Jones+-++A+Wall+In+Naples.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 207px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">"...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-31.htm">whether it gores a boy or it gores a girl</a>..." &nbsp;Wouldn't I know it by logic: a man is liable for killing a man, whether adult or minor, and an ox is liable for killing a man – must be, whether adult or minor? No, man's law is more strict, with liability for pain, cure, etc. Therefore, the verse is needed.<br />
<br />
If an ox was rubbing itself against the wall and the wall collapsed on a man and killed him, or if the ox intended to kill an animal but instead killed man, or to kill a Canaanite but instead killed a Jew, the ox is exempt.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Wall in Naples by Thomas Jones</span></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/45.txt
<a id="src-00342"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/45.txt`

Bava Kamma 45 - Custodian Is Responsible for Damages as the Owner (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiE2kvhVoSUDNSS8sgvaNlmwan7Ghsg7uToLWWXzLkhuNdGyS9AzXxlbxNd3OJN7LllzQD0TYZglXSDdq_rCORP-8pCi2y1EW_mPLu2nfQdG67o88Us9E14XkWhE4-G9-hFxI1M5DMWj5TF/s1600-h/Sir+John+Everett+Millais+-+A+Yeoman+of+the+Guard.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5301619388291874290" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiE2kvhVoSUDNSS8sgvaNlmwan7Ghsg7uToLWWXzLkhuNdGyS9AzXxlbxNd3OJN7LllzQD0TYZglXSDdq_rCORP-8pCi2y1EW_mPLu2nfQdG67o88Us9E14XkWhE4-G9-hFxI1M5DMWj5TF/s320/Sir+John+Everett+Millais+-+A+Yeoman+of+the+Guard.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 253px;" /></a><div>If the owner of an animal entrusted it to the care of an unpaid custodian, a borrower, a paid custodian, or a renter, and then the animal damaged something, the custodian is responsible for the damage as if he would have been the owner.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-weight: bold;"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-style: italic;">Laws of Custodians</span></span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>An unpaid custodian is responsible only for damage resulting from his negligence.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>A paid custodian is responsible if the item is stolen or lost but not for unavoidable mishaps, such as an animal that broke a limb, was captured by armed brigands, or died of natural causes.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>A borrower is liable for theft, loss, and unavoidable mishap but not for damage or loss incurred through regular use.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: A Yeoman of the Guard by Sir John Everett Millais</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/46.txt
<a id="src-00343"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/46.txt`

Bava Kamma 46 - Money In Doubt (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEioldzeIDNdeNxdSKlknt2ymrDElJbFUti-adU06A53xTXei79qMrn1xquzjrbGOtGgiW-X2gfzsKw2UxHNAgH3z9r5xPqKF_d5p86LcYm3D8LupLAjDOl67aTqi5MdXHJ6Sain1_SEm_-t/s1600-h/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+New+Born+Calf+Lying+On+Straw.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5301996511757459922" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEioldzeIDNdeNxdSKlknt2ymrDElJbFUti-adU06A53xTXei79qMrn1xquzjrbGOtGgiW-X2gfzsKw2UxHNAgH3z9r5xPqKF_d5p86LcYm3D8LupLAjDOl67aTqi5MdXHJ6Sain1_SEm_-t/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+New+Born+Calf+Lying+On+Straw.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 222px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If an ox gored a pregnant cow and killed it, and the cow's fetus was found at its side, but it is not known whether the cow gave birth before the ox gored it and the fetus' death is unrelated to goring, or it gave birth after the ox gored it and the goring caused it to miscarry - the ox's owner pays half damages for the cow and one-quarter damages for the offspring.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Sumchos: money whose ownership is in doubt is divided by litigants. </div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Sages: <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/24-14.htm">The one seeking to exact payment from his fellow bears the burden of proo</a><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/24-14.htm">f! </a></div><div><br /></div><div>Art: New Born Calf Lying On Straw by Vincent Van Gogh</div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/47.txt
<a id="src-00344"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/47.txt`

Bava Kamma 47 - Someone's Things in My Courtyard! (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjIq6if84S5P4Uy0Oza31viKwrcT0rXjzka2C2fb9AGTTuQzbqSkV8c0hiXV5t05UBjiyIsv-nQsimgoadRG91uN1QFg8W74R8mcbYSjK4jZrc0Qu2VBdMwkutkLHf-REG_dcR6rdDyYM7k/s1600-h/Willard+Leroy+Metcalf+-+Pottery+Shop+at+Tunis.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5302363302301414514" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjIq6if84S5P4Uy0Oza31viKwrcT0rXjzka2C2fb9AGTTuQzbqSkV8c0hiXV5t05UBjiyIsv-nQsimgoadRG91uN1QFg8W74R8mcbYSjK4jZrc0Qu2VBdMwkutkLHf-REG_dcR6rdDyYM7k/s320/Willard+Leroy+Metcalf+-+Pottery+Shop+at+Tunis.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 246px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If a potter brought his pots into a homeowner's courtyard without permission, and the homeowner's animal broke the pots, the homeowner is exempt from liability. If the homeowner's animal was damaged through the pots, the owner of the pots is liable to pay for the damage.  But if he brought his pots with the homeowner's permission and they were broken, the owner of the courtyard is liable.<br />
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
The same laws are valid if one brought his produce into a courtyard and an animal ate or harmed it.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Rebbi says: "The homeowner is not liable unless he explicitly accepts the obligation to guard it."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Pottery Shop at Tunis by Willard Leroy Metcalf</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/48.txt
<a id="src-00345"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/48.txt`

Bava Kamma 48 - An Ox Falls into a Cistern and Kills Someone (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg-B4Am2i-bQTRBMwWX3RBlcZ_agwgY1qRCGioxGcUJxjpMPUuB2kZoPHss0NfKxTZ3oGAC8-mmvAmUqrBlO1GqMUJ-rTxlSGtmqJ9lhP55YjuZgLHu7wOvoB4GABlU_nHmmYj2FFWgu0yG/s1600-h/William+Sidney+Mount+-+At+The+Well.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5302898985159323698" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg-B4Am2i-bQTRBMwWX3RBlcZ_agwgY1qRCGioxGcUJxjpMPUuB2kZoPHss0NfKxTZ3oGAC8-mmvAmUqrBlO1GqMUJ-rTxlSGtmqJ9lhP55YjuZgLHu7wOvoB4GABlU_nHmmYj2FFWgu0yG/s320/William+Sidney+Mount+-+At+The+Well.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 236px;" /></a>If one brought his ox into a homeowner's courtyard without permission and the homeowner's ox gored it, or the homeowner's dog bit it, the homeowner is exempt from liability. If the trespasser's ox gored the homeowner's ox, the trespasser is liable.<br />
<br />
If the trespasser's ox fell into the homeowner's cistern and fouled its waters, the trespasser is liable. If the homeowner's father or son was in the cistern and was killed by the falling ox, the trespasser must pay redemption reparation. But if he brought his ox into the courtyard with the owner's permission and it was damaged there, the courtyard's owner is liable.<br />
<br />
Art: At The Well by William Sidney Mount

---

### content/bava_kamma/49.txt
<a id="src-00346"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/49.txt`

Bava Kamma 49 - Damages to a Pregnant Woman (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhrQLaLaboO0xHG6pfj3v3R_ON4aOcjMNTZbCy6Fgy5Asj5hi3__pzfY2BPx4wh-3e2nOGz1z54X2ACU5o_s6DkmYb3l1TS50Iq2LseFfr7dFzYQD5mNhMiD08i3ZjmstF9rY0mDVjft7Dn/s1600-h/Thomas+Rowlandson+-+The+Pregnant+Woman,+1815.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5303258790200891442" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhrQLaLaboO0xHG6pfj3v3R_ON4aOcjMNTZbCy6Fgy5Asj5hi3__pzfY2BPx4wh-3e2nOGz1z54X2ACU5o_s6DkmYb3l1TS50Iq2LseFfr7dFzYQD5mNhMiD08i3ZjmstF9rY0mDVjft7Dn/s320/Thomas+Rowlandson+-+The+Pregnant+Woman,+1815.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 238px;" /></a>If an ox intended to gore its fellow ox, and it struck a pregnant woman instead, and her offspring were miscarried, the ox's owner is exempt from paying for the value of the offspring.<br />
<br />
But if a <span style="font-style: italic;">person</span> intended to strike his fellow and instead struck a pregnant woman and her offspring were miscarried, <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-22.htm">he must pay her husband the full value of the offspring</a>. For this,&nbsp;they assess how much she was worth before giving birth and how much after miscarriage, using prices of the slave market. Of course, if the woman suffered an additional injury, that damage is assessed separately.<br />
<br />
Art: The Pregnant Woman by&nbsp;Thomas Rowlandson

---

### content/bava_kamma/5.txt
<a id="src-00347"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/5.txt`

Bava Kamma 5 - Can Ox and Man Teach About Fire? (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiZaG4kr3oB9824mNsMGp-uqk-0KuZ1iWYShk4R3p0CUYOO_BlKLBusHvtZjRiyNgeY7dhuPUuc_6NBAptQI9bhyphenhyphenRWzT0nmEg0W0DWxbMwwqvF6KFLzl-8oDWGkcSwX6bdQ2Lqn0V00yq74/s1600-h/Friedrich+Wasmann+-+Girl+Sleeping+By+The+Fire,-1843.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5286816131200953330" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiZaG4kr3oB9824mNsMGp-uqk-0KuZ1iWYShk4R3p0CUYOO_BlKLBusHvtZjRiyNgeY7dhuPUuc_6NBAptQI9bhyphenhyphenRWzT0nmEg0W0DWxbMwwqvF6KFLzl-8oDWGkcSwX6bdQ2Lqn0V00yq74/s320/Friedrich+Wasmann+-+Girl+Sleeping+By+The+Fire,-1843.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 250px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Ox and man each have stringencies over the other, and the liability for one can't be derived from another.<br />
<br />
If combined, can the two teach liability for fire? Ox has the intent to damage, whereas fire does not. However, a man is liable even for damage that he inflicts while sleeping. Thus, the intent to damage is not essential.<br />
<br />
Man is liable for four damage payments but fire for just one. However, the ox disproves that since it is also liable for just one payment.<br />
<br />
Man and ox are alive, and fire is not; thus, liability for fire had to be mentioned in the Torah.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Girl Sleeping By The Fire by Friedrich Wasmann</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/50.txt
<a id="src-00348"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/50.txt`

Bava Kamma 50 - Donkey Falls Into a Pit (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDPSr8Usmz5NmYNnTHyFfQUqCW2yNmb6JvL0EOBcOtaosUh8mQ2BcINsZLxF1xBxWFXId3nDFTb2vGspjWVTwe3axRlekDFatGqMIohO3Xvxuf0iV-H8MUyEEctYAaIMTDx5M4KAc5-34a/s1600-h/Edgar+Bundy+-+Peasant+Children+with+Donkeys.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5303602828771799154" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDPSr8Usmz5NmYNnTHyFfQUqCW2yNmb6JvL0EOBcOtaosUh8mQ2BcINsZLxF1xBxWFXId3nDFTb2vGspjWVTwe3axRlekDFatGqMIohO3Xvxuf0iV-H8MUyEEctYAaIMTDx5M4KAc5-34a/s320/Edgar+Bundy+-+Peasant+Children+with+Donkeys.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 246px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-33.htm">If one digs a pit in the public domain and an ox or a donkey falls into it</a>, he is liable to pay the damages.<br />
<br />
Whatever shape one digs, he is liable to pay for the damage his excavation causes. If so, why is specifically a pit mentioned in the Torah? Just as a standard pit has sufficient depth to cause death, being ten hand-breadths deep, one is liable for any obstacle that has sufficient depth to cause death.<br />
<br />
One is not liable for the death of a donkey in a pit less than 10 hand-breadths but is liable for the injury.<br />
<br /><div>Art: Peasant Children with Donkeys by Edgar Bundy</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/51.txt
<a id="src-00349"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/51.txt`

Bava Kamma 51 - A Pit of Two Partners (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjePKt3UDfi5q2xHMtPJ15WbJ8FRwv8CDvIwqvD4wKqSQ3xYPBOOGnamLXHlkepXlPssr1ZM06LTptNMyXM32VHev92BDDLJwC6lheXm1j7-gJWMKqBEJsofLfLuu3uMvMwjkvABjb6RGIp/s1600-h/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Ditchdiggers.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5303976429137085490" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjePKt3UDfi5q2xHMtPJ15WbJ8FRwv8CDvIwqvD4wKqSQ3xYPBOOGnamLXHlkepXlPssr1ZM06LTptNMyXM32VHev92BDDLJwC6lheXm1j7-gJWMKqBEJsofLfLuu3uMvMwjkvABjb6RGIp/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Ditchdiggers.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 198px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If there is a pit of two partners, and the first one passed by and did not cover it, and then the second one passed by it and did not cover it, the second one is liable to pay for the damage it causes.<br />
<div>
<br />
But the first one was also negligent! In this case, he handed over the pit's cover to the second one.<br />
<br />
But how can a pit of two partners exist? The one who completed it is liable! In this case, one dug a pit nine hand-breadths deep and then they both simultaneously uprooted a clump of earth from its bottom.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Ditchdiggers by Vincent Van Gogh</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<br />

---

### content/bava_kamma/52.txt
<a id="src-00350"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/52.txt`

Bava Kamma 52 - A Pit that is Open (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi_8paGi_M3L7lEwp4198vQdluXjGGtq1e_P27xOyj8Ek1aXz5mxjM5JrRZ6B_8qUyXrAUTPAlgBBLK_E9gj97F8Bz6tF8qGpeNGfQDOrSUx0E86rUSTSDW0bgMYEon97xKZsWMByNDsH9w/s1600-h/Pascal-Adolphe-Jean+Dagnan-Bouveret+-+Hamlet+and+the+Gravediggers+1883.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5304246418382863858" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi_8paGi_M3L7lEwp4198vQdluXjGGtq1e_P27xOyj8Ek1aXz5mxjM5JrRZ6B_8qUyXrAUTPAlgBBLK_E9gj97F8Bz6tF8qGpeNGfQDOrSUx0E86rUSTSDW0bgMYEon97xKZsWMByNDsH9w/s320/Pascal-Adolphe-Jean+Dagnan-Bouveret+-+Hamlet+and+the+Gravediggers+1883.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 265px;" /></a><div>A pit of two partners – if the first partner covered it after he used it, and the second one came to use it and found it uncovered (worms ate the lid) and didn't cover it, the second one is exclusively liable for any damage that it does.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If one covered a pit properly and nevertheless an ox or a donkey fell into it and died, he is exempt.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If an ox with its utensils fell into a pit and the utensils broke, the pit owner is liable to pay for the damage to the animal but is exempt from paying for damage to the utensils. </div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: Hamlet and the Gravediggers by Pascal-Adolphe-Jean Dagnan-Bouveret</div>
<div>
</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/53.txt
<a id="src-00351"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/53.txt`

Bava Kamma 53 - A Man and An Ox Together Push another Ox into a Pit  (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwY0h9GKEE0yAfF7halFzyooSx3q1yym1OIGhyphenhyphenJXHHrp8rovqHAFdMABbop5ORF0b_ZAActVdBnjIIXhjAiNseiolyzn0BuZwfXZDNULxxjUVqYGVYfFR6DxGUTVys4FA9Q-zfPIWWgVPZ/s1600-h/John+Quidor+-+The+Gold+Diggers+1832.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5304698045346359138" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwY0h9GKEE0yAfF7halFzyooSx3q1yym1OIGhyphenhyphenJXHHrp8rovqHAFdMABbop5ORF0b_ZAActVdBnjIIXhjAiNseiolyzn0BuZwfXZDNULxxjUVqYGVYfFR6DxGUTVys4FA9Q-zfPIWWgVPZ/s320/John+Quidor+-+The+Gold+Diggers+1832.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 242px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If a worker digs a pit, he, and not his employer, is liable for the damages - because "there is no messenger for transgression," and it is forbidden to  create damaging obstacles  in the public domain.<br />
<br />
If someone pushes an ox into a pit or startles the animal and it falls, the owner of the pit is liable for whatever can't be collected from the first man.<br />
<br />
If an ox and a person together push either a person or an animal or utensils into a pit, all (the person, the ox, and the pit) are liable for damages. Still, only a human is liable for the "<a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_kamma/bava_kamma26.html" target="_blank">four payments</a>."<br />
<br /><div>Art: The Gold Diggers by John Quidor</div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/54.txt

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/54.txt`

Bava Kamma 54 - All Animals are Equal in Front of the Law (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTaW0XO7JIW0DTcGMXUISLGOV_JXjNWeMQYneLY0GKgu1_PKYxUvk3dQ4s0ETsB5FaKHNccZ3zjcePGr49DPbTMQEG7N0MJMcDFvMORuUMrjdc71ZYrY1JXAkOqRz4QEqXGrh5gOrrYNK_/s1600-h/James+Ward+-+Donkeys,+horse+and+pigs+by+a+barn+in+a+farmyard.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5304964333186695682" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTaW0XO7JIW0DTcGMXUISLGOV_JXjNWeMQYneLY0GKgu1_PKYxUvk3dQ4s0ETsB5FaKHNccZ3zjcePGr49DPbTMQEG7N0MJMcDFvMORuUMrjdc71ZYrY1JXAkOqRz4QEqXGrh5gOrrYNK_/s320/James+Ward+-+Donkeys,+horse+and+pigs+by+a+barn+in+a+farmyard.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 250px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span style="font-size: medium;">The same law that applies to an ox also applies to any domestic animal regarding the following:<br />
<ol><li><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-33.htm">Payment of damages for its falling into a pit</a>,&nbsp;<br />
</li>
<li><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/19-12.htm">forceful separation from Mount Sinai at the Giving of the Torah</a>,&nbsp;<br />
</li>
<li><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-3.htm">the twofold payment a thief must make for stealing an animal</a>,&nbsp;<br />
</li>
<li><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/22-1.htm">returning a lost object</a>,<br />
</li>
<li><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/23-5.htm">unloading an animal</a>,<br />
</li>
<li><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/25-4.htm">prohibition of muzzling an animal when it is threshing</a>,<br />
</li>
<li>prohibition of <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/19-19.htm">mating </a>or <a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/22-10.htm">plowing with diverse species</a> together,<br />
</li>
<li><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/5-14.htm">prohibition of having one's animal work on Sabbath</a>.</li>
</ol>Moreover, any wild beast or bird is legally the same.<br />
Why is an ox or donkey explicitly mentioned? Because Scripture speaks of the usual case.<br />
</span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Donkeys, horse and pigs by a barn in a farmyard by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">James Ward</span></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/55.txt
<a id="src-00353"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/55.txt`

Bava Kamma 55 - Guard Your Animal (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXW_HEa9gee_9Z_uutFsO9qBh-BCQ_1KKmoxnoRwpjbEJdZ1Ze4ZQir0F_rPWmJo0Sh4NkFPQVdzWHOx81yjo9S1tx3RZw4RehWa4MqiwADW2uRaKgtC5R6bChDXEJi6zrDI8n_WOm-pZG/s1600-h/Charles+%C3%89mile+Jacque+:+Grazing+Sheep+with+a+Sheperdhess+Beyond.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5305496149419680658" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgXW_HEa9gee_9Z_uutFsO9qBh-BCQ_1KKmoxnoRwpjbEJdZ1Ze4ZQir0F_rPWmJo0Sh4NkFPQVdzWHOx81yjo9S1tx3RZw4RehWa4MqiwADW2uRaKgtC5R6bChDXEJi6zrDI8n_WOm-pZG/s320/Charles+%C3%89mile+Jacque+:+Grazing+Sheep+with+a+Sheperdhess+Beyond.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 254px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>One who brought a sheep into a fold and properly locked the gate after it, but it escaped and damaged the property of another, is not liable to pay for the damage; one who didn't properly lock the gate is liable.<br />
<br />
If the fold was breached at night, or robbers breached it, he is not liable; if the robbers took the sheep out, they are liable.<br />
<br />
If he left the sheep in the sun or gave it over to a deaf-mute, deranged, or minor, and it escaped and damaged, he is liable; if he gave it to a shepherd, the shepherd assumes the responsibility.<br />
<br />
Art: Grazing Sheep with a Sheperdhess Beyond by Charles Emile Jacque

---

### content/bava_kamma/56.txt
<a id="src-00354"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/56.txt`

Bava Kamma 56 - Not Liable in Court but Liable in Heaven (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2GBC8TqosOraE62MOPXit86OjPScOOyyfWUMfD4sXMqo1KyRkLkfi-EJaUlAOcWUHb3lZZMU7mivl6LCM2lxFU0mIPBXJcsHEO00zNLcprtXBHoiPHlxg0hxJYjJ45l1kWeI6Sz9C9xi0/s1600-h/Walter-Dendy+Sadler+-+A+Breach+of+Promise,+published+1895.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5305820063089675810" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2GBC8TqosOraE62MOPXit86OjPScOOyyfWUMfD4sXMqo1KyRkLkfi-EJaUlAOcWUHb3lZZMU7mivl6LCM2lxFU0mIPBXJcsHEO00zNLcprtXBHoiPHlxg0hxJYjJ45l1kWeI6Sz9C9xi0/s320/Walter-Dendy+Sadler+-+A+Breach+of+Promise,+published+1895.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 227px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>There are four cases of monetary loss for which the perpetrator is not liable to pay under the law of man. Still, he is liable under the law of Heaven (because one is not liable for causing damage indirectly):<br />
<ul>
<li>One who breaches a wall before his fellow's animal (the animal exited its enclosure and fled);</li>
<li>One who bends his fellow's standing grain toward a fire (the fire then reaches the grain with the aid of an unusually strong wind);</li>
<li>One who hires false witnesses to testify (on behalf of his fellow);</li>
<li>One who knows testimony beneficial to his fellow but does not testify on his behalf.</li>
</ul>
Art: A Breach of Promise by Walter-Dendy Sadler

---

### content/bava_kamma/57.txt
<a id="src-00355"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/57.txt`

Bava Kamma 57 - Caring for the Lost Object, Too Much Responsibility? (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjHcPWVAc_PG5PloGuKTizaLrIgR27VML-suj_nDuw4UKer7x0LK6Y7JNQLi75uEgd2V0ARqqwtMXYF00SD5lZnfhh9uXxq4I-khQD00RixDUkmhTC6DqtChswS-F-4JGi5ALBb1DX4NeIk/s1600-h/Marcus+Stone+-+Lost+In+Thought,+1864.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5306088759147754610" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjHcPWVAc_PG5PloGuKTizaLrIgR27VML-suj_nDuw4UKer7x0LK6Y7JNQLi75uEgd2V0ARqqwtMXYF00SD5lZnfhh9uXxq4I-khQD00RixDUkmhTC6DqtChswS-F-4JGi5ALBb1DX4NeIk/s320/Marcus+Stone+-+Lost+In+Thought,+1864.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 254px;" /></a><div><div>Is the finder of a lost object treated as a paid custodian, liable even if the object is stolen or lost, or as an unpaid custodian, liable only for negligence?</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Ruling: if the finder returned it where the owner will see it, he is not obligated to deal with it further, but if it was stolen or lost, he is responsible. Doesn't it follow that it was stolen or lost from the finder's home, and he is thus a paid custodian? No! It was stolen from the place where he returned it, because he returned it in the afternoon, too late for the owner to see it.</div>
</div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: Lost In Thought by Marcus Stone</div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_kamma/58.txt
<a id="src-00356"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_kamma/58.txt`

Bava Kamma 58 - An Animal That Fell into a Garden (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh6pkpz0HX39cKf_AICAPLXsHnZV43bloUisxe9T_78h5KeNrsoMzxtac0_C4jV1pjwceaDhk0iJVQztfoRRnoH_ZUvqhhYd7IChQ6B4oNyFXX3dWIjnB08LUqWQkTRwcYaC1Sy1LigtLDx/s1600-h/Nicolaes+Berchem+-+Animal+Study.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5306486213493435938" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh6pkpz0HX39cKf_AICAPLXsHnZV43bloUisxe9T_78h5KeNrsoMzxtac0_C4jV1pjwceaDhk0iJVQztfoRRnoH_ZUvqhhYd7IChQ6B4oNyFXX3dWIjnB08LUqWQkTRwcYaC1Sy1LigtLDx/s320/Nicolaes+Berchem+-+Animal+Study.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 219px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If an animal fell into a garden and was saved from injury by the produce, the owner pays for the benefit of saving it from injury. The owner can't claim that his friend was doing a mitzvah saving his animal.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If the animal continues eating, the owner pays for not having to feed it next time. Once the animal knows its way to the garden, the owner is liable if he doesn't watch it more closely.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If the owner was negligent and has to pay full damages in the field, they are estimated as a &nbsp;loss in value of a field sixty times larger, with similar damage.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Art: Animal Study by Nicolaes Berchem</div>

---

Bava Kamma 59 - Wearing Black Shoes in the Marketplace (Torts)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5H1mtzNjjzRXHHt9DJPJRWaUMGAAbVwE-iKOyZGsaaokuyNcoPdf7Lo8nThL1RLwVKstsT_RTdsdHVw9GOi4OyTC7Cs7kAC-Qh_3otLe6QziVSw6Zx61iKwiyBuYuc5OqArtekJ-WKDF-/s1600-h/Van+Gogh+-+A+Pair+Of+Shoes.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5306829772211902066" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5H1mtzNjjzRXHHt9DJPJRWaUMGAAbVwE-iKOyZGsaaokuyNcoPdf7Lo8nThL1RLwVKstsT_RTdsdHVw9GOi4OyTC7Cs7kAC-Qh_3otLe6QziVSw6Zx61iKwiyBuYuc5OqArtekJ-WKDF-/s320/Van+Gogh+-+A+Pair+Of+Shoes.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 263px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><div>Eliezer the Younger was wearing black shoes, as is the custom of mourners, and was standing in the marketplace of Nahardea. Officers of the House of the Exilarch asked, “What is different with these shoes?” He answered, “Because I am mourning over the destruction of Jerusalem.”</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
They asked, “Are you so important?” and imprisoned him for haughtiness. He said, “I am a great scholar.”</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
They asked, “How do we know?” He said, “Ask me a question, or I will ask &nbsp;you.”</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
He confused them with questions about damage payments for cutting budding dates, and they released him.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: A Pair Of Shoes by Van Gogh</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
