### content/bava_metzia/101.txt
<a id="src-00404"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/101.txt`

Bava Metzia 101 - Eviction Notice (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMM6qQQzvsBiX2RrWqIdND3qascqiWigzA9mTuRCdvoUp43PUD264B61588LH-KiaRDVLxP1PHJq0-n1LdXGj9YrZuKvZJ6Y_o-QW6abdB1iNvv8wMzeypITYls-7HU-oQuk6uoDZXBE5O/s1600-h/Henri+Eugene+Augustin+Le+Sidaner+-+A+House+in+Winter.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5366175917628018146" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMM6qQQzvsBiX2RrWqIdND3qascqiWigzA9mTuRCdvoUp43PUD264B61588LH-KiaRDVLxP1PHJq0-n1LdXGj9YrZuKvZJ6Y_o-QW6abdB1iNvv8wMzeypITYls-7HU-oQuk6uoDZXBE5O/s320/Henri+Eugene+Augustin+Le+Sidaner+-+A+House+in+Winter.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 217px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Suppose one rents a house to his fellow. In that case, he cannot evict the tenant in the winter, i.e., from Succoth until Passover - unless he gives the tenant notice in the summer, at least thirty days before the beginning of Succoth because during winter, rental houses in Israel were hard to find.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">In large cities, where there is a perennial housing shortage, a landlord must give twelve months' notice before evicting a tenant. </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">With regard to stores, both in towns and large cities, a landlord must give twelve months' notice to allow the storeowners to start collecting on the credit they usually extend to their customers. </span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: A House in Winter by Henri Eugene Augustin Le Sidaner</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

### content/bava_metzia/102.txt
<a id="src-00405"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/102.txt`

Bava Metzia 102 - Rights and Obligations of a Landlord and his Tenant (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgAKuykyX07c_e9FIfRPlK3FZ2hLRpXa0tnZNxBKQHD6QHMVwAO4NnFCZ8de5F-AK81TZQKqB8Q8rJCFN4LAMpodhqbSGogcutFQxZn43k1hqS7CHAdqiMFYOp2gUSSUseYtNuRsHxKNS2Y/s1600-h/Kibbutz+Regavim%E2%80%99s+abandoned+Synagogue,+Copyright+-+Hayim+Shtayer.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5366560332766175362" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgAKuykyX07c_e9FIfRPlK3FZ2hLRpXa0tnZNxBKQHD6QHMVwAO4NnFCZ8de5F-AK81TZQKqB8Q8rJCFN4LAMpodhqbSGogcutFQxZn43k1hqS7CHAdqiMFYOp2gUSSUseYtNuRsHxKNS2Y/s320/Kibbutz+Regavim%E2%80%99s+abandoned+Synagogue,+Copyright+-+Hayim+Shtayer.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 254px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one rents a house to his fellow, it is the duty of the tenant to prepare a mezuzah for it, and when the tenant leaves, he should not take the mezuzah away, even to affix it in another house. He can, however, demand compensation from the next resident.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one rents a house to his fellow for a year, and the year was then proclaimed a leap year, that is, an extra month was added, the tenant need not pay additional rent because of it. If, however, he rented the house to the tenant by the month, and the year was then proclaimed a leap year, the tenant must pay rent for the extra month. The last ruling is obvious and is only taught for the sake of completeness.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Kibbutz Regavim's Abandoned Synagogue by Hayim Shtayer</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/103.txt
<a id="src-00406"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/103.txt`

Bava Metzia 103 - Field Leases (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2W7hgd3N37mlvEwLDWEhXxqaDqEGfcSLLRqSTwEE6pv6YRaF2KaxEfc2qArwL3ffZtH-GoJCWZ6w0JdWopT1AZw6lnp1wswxAXd-qy2QtKK3prLc7poTj04GaaY41tsqueinuuApeYJCL/s1600-h/Wlodzimierz+Tetmajer+-+In+the+Wheat+Field.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5366963642083867634" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2W7hgd3N37mlvEwLDWEhXxqaDqEGfcSLLRqSTwEE6pv6YRaF2KaxEfc2qArwL3ffZtH-GoJCWZ6w0JdWopT1AZw6lnp1wswxAXd-qy2QtKK3prLc7poTj04GaaY41tsqueinuuApeYJCL/s320/Wlodzimierz+Tetmajer+-+In+the+Wheat+Field.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 216px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">There are two arrangements under which fields are leased: sharecropping and tenant farming. A sharecropper pays the owner of the land a fixed percentage of the crops, for example, a half, third, or quarter, and keeps the rest. The tenant farmer pays a fixed amount, usually using the field’s produce, but if it’s not enough, he buys from the market.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one leases a field from his fellow and they did not agree on the way of cultivating the field, such as cutting or uprooting the crop or whether to plow afterward, they should follow the local custom.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Just as they divide the wine, so they divide the branches and the canes - in the same proportion, and this applies only to sharecropping.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: In the Wheat Field b Wlodzimierz Tetmajer</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/104.txt
<a id="src-00407"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/104.txt`

Bava Metzia 104 - Calamities in the Field and Laymen's Contracts (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgevBkPX-b36HwRdk2OD7rgLn0EabOOgsu7Mt7IZ2PNFNk6_IUWRREOvKE7kq6hVGCSJkRg65T1sBrg4Lv3J4c0GpD7MFfS50lBHI8o_5rBkZx48ioGMgIOGkGtcYFNjgD3lKGmjwEKRRbp/s1600-h/Paul+Gauguin+-+Aven+Valley+Upstream+Of+Pont+Aven.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5367284905040511842" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgevBkPX-b36HwRdk2OD7rgLn0EabOOgsu7Mt7IZ2PNFNk6_IUWRREOvKE7kq6hVGCSJkRg65T1sBrg4Lv3J4c0GpD7MFfS50lBHI8o_5rBkZx48ioGMgIOGkGtcYFNjgD3lKGmjwEKRRbp/s320/Paul+Gauguin+-+Aven+Valley+Upstream+Of+Pont+Aven.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 248px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Suppose one leased a field from his fellow, which had a stream from which it could be conveniently watered or a tree that produced fruit without requiring much work. In that case, the field commands a higher rent. If the spring dried up or the tree was felled, he may not deduct anything from his rent in compensation for his loss. If he mentioned that his reason for renting the fields was the river or the tree – then he may deduct.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If a sharecropper leased a field and left it fallow, they assess how much it was fit to yield, and he must give that amount because a layman's contract usually says, "If I leave it fallow and do not work it properly, I will pay according to the best."</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Aven Valley Upstream Of Pont Aven by Paul Gauguin</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/105.txt
<a id="src-00408"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/105.txt`

Bava Metzia 105 – Disagreements Between a Tenant and a Field Owner (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhvP_YYFBBKkKKv4TxG7scp3lH8OZ-Ww6XlSdTsb_6ssSrkXartJDfAvfd80CIIz7oGfVsGmgQg8dr3ESxfqLTlWZ59iqg-siLbdO9iSQJujOHyXHjqHcFCM8ye7faFjr-vJAeGw7-VNgsa/s1600-h/Camille+Pissarro+-+Haystack,+Pontoise.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5367830223004514098" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhvP_YYFBBKkKKv4TxG7scp3lH8OZ-Ww6XlSdTsb_6ssSrkXartJDfAvfd80CIIz7oGfVsGmgQg8dr3ESxfqLTlWZ59iqg-siLbdO9iSQJujOHyXHjqHcFCM8ye7faFjr-vJAeGw7-VNgsa/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Haystack,+Pontoise.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 262px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Suppose a tenant farmer leased a field from his fellow but did not want to weed it and said to the landowner, "What concern is it of yours since I am committed to giving you your full rental?". In that case, we do not listen to him, for the landowner can reply, "If your lease expires and you don't renew it, the field will grow weeds for me."</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If a sharecropper leases a field from his fellow and it does not produce a substantial crop, he wants to abandon working the field. If there is enough growing in it to produce a heap, he is obligated to care for it. Rabbi Yehudah says, "What kind of limit is a heap? Rather, if there is enough for sowing the field again."</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Haystack, Pontoise by Camille Pissarro</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/106.txt
<a id="src-00409"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/106.txt`

Bava Metzia 106 – General vs. Localized Calamities (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgE0HTesBcRpXM52awOcTnjgIOBJ0N1FwqC7QGHSF4GwNGmlf5QRkwamTOo2oy0mBk46_8gE5tOfrAlzg-Icx5HtK5k0HBcn5t1Are3wCTki93IC8Z6ErIJqpx_NL_2pkwHVMX4O-Dr7kWS/s1600-h/Shibata+Zeshin+-+Grasshopper+and+wheat.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5368177454669685154" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgE0HTesBcRpXM52awOcTnjgIOBJ0N1FwqC7QGHSF4GwNGmlf5QRkwamTOo2oy0mBk46_8gE5tOfrAlzg-Icx5HtK5k0HBcn5t1Are3wCTki93IC8Z6ErIJqpx_NL_2pkwHVMX4O-Dr7kWS/s320/Shibata+Zeshin+-+Grasshopper+and+wheat.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 260px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If a tenant farmer leased a field from his fellow and locusts ate up the crop, or it was blasted by wind, which blew the kernels out of the ears of grain, if it is a general calamity, he may deduct from his rental. Since the whole area was stricken, his field was considered unfit for crops, and the tenant committed himself to paying full rental only on the assumption that the field would remain suitable for crops for the duration of the lease.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If the loss was localized, the owner can claim it was the farmer's ill fortune, and the farmer may not deduct it from his rental.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Grasshopper and Wheat by Shibata Zeshin</span></div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/107.txt
<a id="src-00410"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/107.txt`

Bava Metzia 107 - Natural Events vs. Luck (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhFKzKSJc8R7Q8KG_ZralQwyN_OMOZi8bdjw586pzFijZysU3wTU2W3nPzet7gVvfSHlssykyWRGS2STZrwD-SZMJRaijH1rptC0h3x_fWm4hfUOiFSDRsjKqH_y1dH-3Ba9HE49FXM8lix/s1600-h/William+Simpson+-+Hospital+and+Cemetery+1856.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5368425523762941250" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhFKzKSJc8R7Q8KG_ZralQwyN_OMOZi8bdjw586pzFijZysU3wTU2W3nPzet7gVvfSHlssykyWRGS2STZrwD-SZMJRaijH1rptC0h3x_fWm4hfUOiFSDRsjKqH_y1dH-3Ba9HE49FXM8lix/s320/William+Simpson+-+Hospital+and+Cemetery+1856.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 210px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If a tenant farmer leased a field from his fellow, and the crop was blasted by the wind, which reduced its quality, he may pay his rental out of this crop. If the wheat of that crop was superior, the tenant cannot buy grain of average quality but must give the landowner his payment out of that produce.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rav once went to a cemetery and used an incantation to discover how every person there died, and he stated that ninety-nine out of a hundred died from an evil eye and only one from natural causes.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rav Chanina said that </span><a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/22-5.htm" target="_blank"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">everything is in the hands of Heaven except for cold drafts</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">. </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">In the future, </span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/7-15.htm" target="_blank"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">God will remove all illnesses</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">, even the ones mentioned.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Hospital and Cemetery by William Simpson</span></div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/108.txt
<a id="src-00411"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/108.txt`

Bava Metzia 108 – The Right of the Adjoining Property Holder (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiX5DDfni7mzOLcfsKmPZueSHfIm1z94lE1AcB_olX8lJQdECiOhK_KCezbDSHThOyCRliznfnYJbHaI5a4MffYKuVWnmBYoKRbbAqAGINDrFR8PhinUzotpuvFbqttPyiUkIIrh_mri2rg/s1600-h/Pieter+The+Younger+Brueghel+-+A+Village+Landscape+With+Farmers.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5368903456847584802" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiX5DDfni7mzOLcfsKmPZueSHfIm1z94lE1AcB_olX8lJQdECiOhK_KCezbDSHThOyCRliznfnYJbHaI5a4MffYKuVWnmBYoKRbbAqAGINDrFR8PhinUzotpuvFbqttPyiUkIIrh_mri2rg/s320/Pieter+The+Younger+Brueghel+-+A+Village+Landscape+With+Farmers.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 223px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">An immediate neighbor of a property has the right to first purchase it. An outsider who wants to buy a field can easily find another one, but a neighbor gains significantly from being able to buy an adjoining field. This rule is based on "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/6-18.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">You shall do what is right and good in the eyes of God</span></a>,"<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;which commands one to go beyond the letter of the law.</span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one wants to buy a field and inquires of the neighbor of that field if he can do it, and the neighbor allows it,  a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/06/bava-metzia-45-coins-used-for-symbolic.html">formal act of acquisition</a> is still required, or else the neighbor can later claim that had he come to buy the land, he would be asked a higher price, but that he never meant to relinquish his right.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Village Landscape With Farmers by Pieter The Younger Brueghel</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/109.txt
<a id="src-00412"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/109.txt`

Bava Metzia 109 – Short-term vs. Long-term Leases (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi5Hz2v5fVyqonyRPdwUNboY0XZJJ6ejbiiKp3Pw7mPbdmtCF4vg524PEB5fejSBrZxfNOV-4MmZXLVIg6EbwJyk05X8QuxdVTh5pqr9AeEdqWfouKuxhWxxLGILotJKcr7WW1WUSH4XlUn/s1600-h/John+Love+-+The+Sycamores.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5369189455534190610" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi5Hz2v5fVyqonyRPdwUNboY0XZJJ6ejbiiKp3Pw7mPbdmtCF4vg524PEB5fejSBrZxfNOV-4MmZXLVIg6EbwJyk05X8QuxdVTh5pqr9AeEdqWfouKuxhWxxLGILotJKcr7WW1WUSH4XlUn/s320/John+Love+-+The+Sycamores.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 271px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">If one leases a field from his fellow for just a few years (less than seven), he may not sow it with flax, and he has no rights to the beams of any sycamores (planetrees) growing there.</span><br />
<div>
<span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
</span></div>
<div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">Although flax is a very profitable crop, it depletes the soil excessively, and it takes up to seven years to recover fully. Planting flax would lead him to return the land in worse condition than he had received it.</span></div>
<div>
<span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
</span></div>
<div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">This ruling applies only to a tenant farmer, where the landowner receives a fixed payment no matter what the land produces. In the case of a sharecropper, we assume that the landowner agrees to a more intensive use of the land based on the principle "let the land become poor but not the owner."</span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Sycamores by John Love</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/11.txt
<a id="src-00413"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/11.txt`

Bava Metzia 11 - Acquisition with the Help of a Field (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhKad1p5HWt_tbHWOYYIeAdPBVRri7QqgPHq7wjNkgPRjFVzUxCcnMdZHc46qRIot5UkhvENs1G31NAgugw1DjLmrdg-F7pRGb0rLarQNF_YP079ao3BZ5feMKGwVFowVVLuj_lm1na-65P/s1600-h/Frida+Kahlo+-+Little+Deer.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5332771365784583234" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhKad1p5HWt_tbHWOYYIeAdPBVRri7QqgPHq7wjNkgPRjFVzUxCcnMdZHc46qRIot5UkhvENs1G31NAgugw1DjLmrdg-F7pRGb0rLarQNF_YP079ao3BZ5feMKGwVFowVVLuj_lm1na-65P/s320/Frida+Kahlo+-+Little+Deer.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 238px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If one saw people running after a find, after a lame deer, or after young pigeons that cannot yet fly, and said, "My field has acquired it for me," - it has indeed acquired it for him. If the deer was running normally, or if the pigeons were flying, and he said, "My field has acquired it for me," - he has said nothing.</div><div><br /></div><div>This method of acquisition is called "courtyard." The owner doesn't have to declare his intention – it is only stated to emphasize the second case in the ruling. He does have to stand next to his field, making it comparable to a courtyard.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Little Deer by Frida Kahlo</div>

---

Bava Metzia 110 – Timely Payment of a Hired Worker (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDCAUVgj5Qr6EoU9v0pJMYKoyQC5oagB4fCDBplAmSL7VpXtBv459YFFVfLnGCMWWLwTbTFaAVBb36bAY8Pp0ERcwmPN3_jdV-bpYWBE5QGbn5QjdbtcuX8gkSKEvuPGjPoW4sgmSr-igh/s1600-h/Kazimir+Severinovich+Malevich+-+Female+Worker.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5369623656507452930" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDCAUVgj5Qr6EoU9v0pJMYKoyQC5oagB4fCDBplAmSL7VpXtBv459YFFVfLnGCMWWLwTbTFaAVBb36bAY8Pp0ERcwmPN3_jdV-bpYWBE5QGbn5QjdbtcuX8gkSKEvuPGjPoW4sgmSr-igh/s320/Kazimir+Severinovich+Malevich+-+Female+Worker.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 258px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">An employer is prohibited from delaying payment due to his employee: "<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/19-13.htm">The wage of a hired worker shall not  stay overnight with you until morning.</a>" and "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/24-15.htm">On his day shall you pay his hire and the sun shall not set upon him</a>...."<br /><br />One who is hired for the day and completes his work in the evening collects his payment all night; that is, the entire night constitutes the payment time of the worker.  One hired for the night collects all day; that is, the collection time for one who terminates his employment at daybreak is that day.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Female Worker by Kazimir Severinovich Malevich</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/111.txt
<a id="src-00415"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/111.txt`

Bava Metzia 111 – Prohibition Again Delaying Payment to an Employee (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEifhhY6Hz0qU5LKrqbDMM-v3DZ7gfrLKk4V26mDF8QOyoUAvN3PQDCe14_qdYUR6SCW_uORbm_qYfHzDlHeUmakxcKYwMaAl7MkRSi_oRMGlxBeMfVN_mYmiFf4vvlbFh73lHTUeK-2rliv/s1600-h/Francis+Davis+Millet+-+Flemish+Kitchen.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5369953672290842498" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEifhhY6Hz0qU5LKrqbDMM-v3DZ7gfrLKk4V26mDF8QOyoUAvN3PQDCe14_qdYUR6SCW_uORbm_qYfHzDlHeUmakxcKYwMaAl7MkRSi_oRMGlxBeMfVN_mYmiFf4vvlbFh73lHTUeK-2rliv/s320/Francis+Davis+Millet+-+Flemish+Kitchen.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 238px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">Whether it be the hire of a man, the hire of an animal, or the hire of a utensil – that is, the wages due a man for his labor, or the payment due him for renting his animals or utensils, one is subject to <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/08/bava-metzia-110-timely-payment-of-hired.html">both prohibitions against delaying a payment</a>.<br /><br />When is this so? When the worker demanded his wage from the employer. But if the worker did not demand his wages from the employer, the employer does not transgress the law. If the employer directed him to a storekeeper or a moneychanger (by arranging an account with them), but the worker was not paid, the employer does not transgress the law.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Flemish Kitchen by Francis Davis Millet</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/112.txt
<a id="src-00416"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/112.txt`

Bava Metzia 112 – Delaying Payments for Contractual Work (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhmIojWmGdkj84nC_IQGBMbc4NnZT0jMX9aGkCuRP48xG33hnUdCWFgNRNNxdnI1rcy3PZpZQAi8KOEysuBKn-jv0tQfEUwvHA_5GFu9aMNOtGH05zAX9NIOyXBCNsu5iuC55-p6u8lSiFr/s1600-h/Diego+Rodriguez+de+Silva+y+Velazquez+-+Peasants+at+the+Table+-+El+Almuerzo+1620.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5370426184850926018" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhmIojWmGdkj84nC_IQGBMbc4NnZT0jMX9aGkCuRP48xG33hnUdCWFgNRNNxdnI1rcy3PZpZQAi8KOEysuBKn-jv0tQfEUwvHA_5GFu9aMNOtGH05zAX9NIOyXBCNsu5iuC55-p6u8lSiFr/s320/Diego+Rodriguez+de+Silva+y+Velazquez+-+Peasants+at+the+Table+-+El+Almuerzo+1620.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 278px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">If an employer delays payment for contractual work, where a craftsman agreed to complete a specific task for a fixed sum, does he transgress the prohibition not to hold wages overnight?<br /><br />This depends on how one views the improvement to the utensil that the craftsman makes. If the craftsman acquires the improvements, he, in effect, sells the owner that portion when he returns the finished product, and the money that the owner owes is not considered wages but a loan.<br /><br />The prevailing view, however, is that the craftsman does not acquire the improvements and that the payments owed to him are thus wages. Hence, the prohibition against delaying payments applies to contractual work.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Peasants at the Table, El Almuerzo by Diego Rodrigues De Silva y Velasquez</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/113.txt
<a id="src-00417"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/113.txt`

Bava Metzia 113  - Lender's Right to Take Borrower's Security (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEghVb-AmSYkiwCOzywGjlYHeafyfSnMUnjKE5nN6Y0_tMRGiB18welwF0vVgAmOnQNY2US9Y56nTkviOEQ0PSf0nhaSIWeDRkNYI6BtCLbBr7R2QwwiHAtX2liPjPFGPfelmf5ngQkD-hsm/s1600-h/Thomas+Worthington+Whittredge+-+The+Club+House+Sitting+Room+at+Balsam+Lake,+Catskills.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5370790800241377570" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEghVb-AmSYkiwCOzywGjlYHeafyfSnMUnjKE5nN6Y0_tMRGiB18welwF0vVgAmOnQNY2US9Y56nTkviOEQ0PSf0nhaSIWeDRkNYI6BtCLbBr7R2QwwiHAtX2liPjPFGPfelmf5ngQkD-hsm/s320/Thomas+Worthington+Whittredge+-+The+Club+House+Sitting+Room+at+Balsam+Lake,+Catskills.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 212px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If the loan fell due, but the borrower did not pay on time, and the lender wants to take the property of the borrower as security until the loan is paid, the borrower has to observe a few rules:</span><br />
<div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br />* The lender is <a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/24-10.htm">prohibited from going into the borrower's house</a>;</span><br />
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">* Even if the borrower takes the article into the street, the lender is prohibited from taking it personally. He may obtain an article for security only by going to court;</span><br />
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">* The <a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/24-13.htm">lender has to return an article of security to a borrower who needs it</a>. For</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"> example, he may have to return the pillow at night and the plow by day.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Clubhouse Sitting Room at Balsam Lake, Catskills by Thomas Worthington Whittredge&nbsp;</span></div>
</div>
<div>
</div>

---

Bava Metzia 114 – Prophet Elijah and Rabba Bar Avuha (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiDCagMeQ3uGU8R6YE5q0cdSDrcppCMSWpzBAAVSDPsysGFP7B6_J3oRzwWqGjlmuJyH1WuYEfWW6PU3WmVOD7ekE-lXwgo2NeXogSzBaZNlBOkzNJNsG5DAa0uUS1JM7xxUkotdRMm4bvT/s1600-h/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+The+Falling+Leaves.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5371076421955867874" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiDCagMeQ3uGU8R6YE5q0cdSDrcppCMSWpzBAAVSDPsysGFP7B6_J3oRzwWqGjlmuJyH1WuYEfWW6PU3WmVOD7ekE-lXwgo2NeXogSzBaZNlBOkzNJNsG5DAa0uUS1JM7xxUkotdRMm4bvT/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+The+Falling+Leaves.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 255px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">Rabba Bar Avuha found Elijah, the prophet, standing in a cemetery of idolaters and asked him, "Why is the master, who is a Kohen, standing in a cemetery?"<br /><br />Elijah answered, "Did you not learn the Order  of Purities?"  For Rabbi Shimon Bar Yochai said, based on "<a href="http://bible.cc/ezekiel/34-31.htm">Now you my sheep, the sheep of my pasture, are you called man</a>..." - about whom it is said, "...<a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/19-14.htm">when a man dies in a tent</a>..." and therefore only Jewish graves are impure for a Kohen.<br /><br />He said to Elijah, "I am not able to properly study the four most essential orders; am I to study the sixth (Purities)? – for I am destitute."<br /><br />Elijah brought him to the Garden of Eden and told him to collect some leaves. Rabbah understood that he was spending his reward in the World To Come and threw the leaves away. Still, his cloak absorbed the smell, and he sold it for 12,000 golden dinars – and distributed them to his sons-in-law.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: The Falling Leaves by Vincent Van Gogh</span></div>

---

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/115.txt`

Bava Metzia 115 – What May Not be Taken as a Security (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh4WcV6820By1ajc9xq35w78IwEIuKKPPVgpZhXqvFFhO0KUZFuA-zK6gNp3-tWMJnmNCrJCfKBx4w8fx9TTFRoGxQackCfvNPt2eGgdJf0owSLtZDMa0NTrP0jS0UBCxARx_LzclvqsANo/s1600-h/Jean-Victor+Bertin+-+A+Mill,+1800-06.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5371422961378214274" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh4WcV6820By1ajc9xq35w78IwEIuKKPPVgpZhXqvFFhO0KUZFuA-zK6gNp3-tWMJnmNCrJCfKBx4w8fx9TTFRoGxQackCfvNPt2eGgdJf0owSLtZDMa0NTrP0jS0UBCxARx_LzclvqsANo/s320/Jean-Victor+Bertin+-+A+Mill,+1800-06.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 250px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One who takes a portable mill </span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">as a security</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"> is liable for taking two utensils, for it is stated, "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/24-6.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">He shall not take a lower millstone or an upper millstone as a security</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">..." Therefore, even if the lender was warned only once not to take the borrower's mill, he is liable to two sets of lashes.</span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Furthermore, one is liable for taking any item that the debtor requires for his food preparation because "...</span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/24-6.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">he is taking a life as a security</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">." </span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Mill by Jean-Victor Bertin</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/116.txt
<a id="src-00420"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/116.txt`

Bava Metzia 116 – The Ground and the Upper Floor of a House (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj7I7uNmNKtpnECxGU2GhbeXvhMUvIocKQxW5IKV_HzN-qC12Mj0em-HfGROkVBozywr7J52gLtCxChVMKIM0XGES-_snczLQmNeSCx8HJf7nBVb9sjiFv7fqwPHhv07b_E85jAqgBbW0do/s1600-h/Ivan+Nikolaevich+Kramskoy+-+Italian+Ruins,+1876.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5371708843763024130" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj7I7uNmNKtpnECxGU2GhbeXvhMUvIocKQxW5IKV_HzN-qC12Mj0em-HfGROkVBozywr7J52gLtCxChVMKIM0XGES-_snczLQmNeSCx8HJf7nBVb9sjiFv7fqwPHhv07b_E85jAqgBbW0do/s320/Ivan+Nikolaevich+Kramskoy+-+Italian+Ruins,+1876.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 247px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">If two people lived in a two-story house, such as two brothers who inherited their father's house, one taking the ground floor and the other the upper story and the building collapsed, how do we allocate the debris? They divide the wood, the stones, and the earth (used as cement) in proportion to the heights of their respective properties.<br /><br />To allocate the whole and the broken stones, we determine how each wall collapsed. If it collapsed directly downward, presumably, the lower stones broke, and the rest of the wall fell upon them, so the whole stones were allotted to the owner of the upper story. If the wall was knocked over to the side, presumably, the upper stones broke, and the owner of the ground floor gets the whole ones.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Italian Ruins by Ivan Nikolaevich Kramskoy</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/117.txt
<a id="src-00421"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/117.txt`

Bava Metzia 117 – The Upper Apartment's Floor Fell In (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBx5pFxvFlNIUqnp7cGffB2qD48LBjm1STjnXU7Xm4Cg-7c18kP6H6Ho-alLJh2J1D2i0kR_OfooVRZEPOX9x9yKOt2NqeZNfL8H7v_zxC-58e0wxTGMuwymr3EsYXykDEgqyE9zl0Kinm/s1600-h/Gustave+Caillebotte+-+A+Balcony.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5372142182070442882" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBx5pFxvFlNIUqnp7cGffB2qD48LBjm1STjnXU7Xm4Cg-7c18kP6H6Ho-alLJh2J1D2i0kR_OfooVRZEPOX9x9yKOt2NqeZNfL8H7v_zxC-58e0wxTGMuwymr3EsYXykDEgqyE9zl0Kinm/s320/Gustave+Caillebotte+-+A+Balcony.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 282px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 100%;"><span style="font-size: 130%;">Consider the case of a two-story house, the owner living on the ground floor, and a tenant in the upper story. If part of the floor of the upper apartment fell in – and the owner does not want to repair it – the occupant of the upper apartment may go down and live in the landlord's apartment below until the landlord fixes the upper apartment for him.<br /><br />What are the circumstances? If the landlord rented "this upper apartment," he would have no further obligation. If he rented "an upper apartment," he could provide another upper apartment. Our ruling is applicable when the landlord says, "I am renting you this upper apartment, which is on top of this lower apartment." With these words, he pledged the lower apartment to support the tenancy of the upper story.</span><br /></span><div><span style="font-size: 100%;"><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 100%;"><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: A Balcony by Gustave Caillebotte</span></span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/118.txt

Bava Metzia 118 – Two Gardens (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhmWcFJvc-gIT5zA32aVBB3KwvWRZ4PkTCC_CnrPX6AnoXbSAZO5A6wAOONq0iJ7sABPCZ_cOnKDTCkNr19_XadO7DUQ0oFJeLO1LmvIdxxQiunCW1OTqshH0TW62W_oqtrgMXGwVVzabUg/s1600-h/Giuseppe+Arcimboldo+-+Vegetables+In+A+Bowl+Or+The+Gardener.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5372444286722963202" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhmWcFJvc-gIT5zA32aVBB3KwvWRZ4PkTCC_CnrPX6AnoXbSAZO5A6wAOONq0iJ7sABPCZ_cOnKDTCkNr19_XadO7DUQ0oFJeLO1LmvIdxxQiunCW1OTqshH0TW62W_oqtrgMXGwVVzabUg/s320/Giuseppe+Arcimboldo+-+Vegetables+In+A+Bowl+Or+The+Gardener.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 219px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If there are two gardens, one above the other, and vegetables are growing out of the vertical surface between them, to whom do the vegetables belong? Rabbi Meir says, "They belong to the owner of the higher garden." Rabbi Yehudah says, "They belong to the owner of the lower garden."</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Meir said, "If the owner of the upper garden wants to take his earth away, there would be no vegetables left!" Rabbi Yehudah said, "If the owner of the lower garden wants to fill his garden with earth, there would be no vegetables there."</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Shimon said, "Any vegetables that the owner of the higher garden can reach with his hand and take – belong to him. The other vegetables belong to the owner of the lower garden."</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Vegetables in a Bowl or The Gardener by Giuseppe Arcimboldo</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/119.txt
<a id="src-00423"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/119.txt`

Bava Metzia 119 – The Law is Like Rabbi Shimon (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpPreWnJ6fM5iUyB3vlqqiuAu3m-KNLcwVMk6x9xcRQTpo2qIi2C2qJ63nnVU7ZjwZiKlf635wETo8-S2H-RaW-DnxMzDSUI-UtTbRA6sAbNpOj1HrkrF2BpnbZ_can50Esj_fUjYFkfHq/s1600-h/Mason,+Major+George+Henry+-+A+Boy+with+Vegetables.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5373021130595379330" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpPreWnJ6fM5iUyB3vlqqiuAu3m-KNLcwVMk6x9xcRQTpo2qIi2C2qJ63nnVU7ZjwZiKlf635wETo8-S2H-RaW-DnxMzDSUI-UtTbRA6sAbNpOj1HrkrF2BpnbZ_can50Esj_fUjYFkfHq/s320/Mason,+Major+George+Henry+-+A+Boy+with+Vegetables.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 303px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">In the  </span><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/08/bava-metzia-118-two-gardens.html" target="_blank"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">case of vegetables growing out of the vertical wall</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"> between two gardens, why does Rabbi Shimon says that the reach of the upper garden's owner's hand determines to whom the vegetables belong?</span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">In principle, Rabbi Shimon agrees with Rabbi Meir's view that the vegetables belong to the owner of the upper garden because they are growing out of his earth. Rabbi Shimon, however, maintains that the upper owner abandons any vegetables that he cannot reach. Since he would have to go through his neighbor's garden to pick the vegetables and it would be embarrassing to ask his neighbor's permission, it is assumed that he relinquishes them to his neighbor.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">They reported Rabbi Shimon's ruling to the Persian King Shapur, and he said in praise of it, "We extend our graciousness to Rabbi Shimon."</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: A Boy with Vegetables by Major George Henry Mason</span></div>

---

Bava Metzia 12 - To Whom the Finds Belong (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3YVGnJvutd0-q6eYLp-tiECDnBiJE0QXgI_zETE3-7RzGqqgEmqggAIpQ1xDNXHet9nwgBzMc536TbM6f_Pby7-20v67efXvfiRZXDsLS9HFyvQfuC_xH5S3fa_8Q6eRCI6FHHAbrlgz2/s1600-h/Sir+Lawrence+Alma-Tadema+-+A+Silent+Greeting.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5333119704202939106" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3YVGnJvutd0-q6eYLp-tiECDnBiJE0QXgI_zETE3-7RzGqqgEmqggAIpQ1xDNXHet9nwgBzMc536TbM6f_Pby7-20v67efXvfiRZXDsLS9HFyvQfuC_xH5S3fa_8Q6eRCI6FHHAbrlgz2/s320/Sir+Lawrence+Alma-Tadema+-+A+Silent+Greeting.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 236px;" /></a><div><div>If an owner of a purse declared it ownerless and then threw it through someone's house so that it entered one door and exited through another, does the homeowner acquire the purse with the "courtyard" acquisition? - This still needs to be answered.</div><div><br /></div><div>The find of one's dependent son or daughter, of one's Canaanite slave, male or female, and of one's wife belong to him, some from the Torah, and some by Rabbinical enactment. The find of one's independent son or daughter, of one's Hebrew servant or maidservant, and of one's wife whom he divorced, although he has not yet paid her Ketubah, belong to them.</div></div><div><br /></div><div>Art: A Silent Greeting by Sir Lawrence Alma-Tadema</div>

Bava Metzia 13 - Loans and Real Estate (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2lWZal9M6liJeM7F8HRU9nKiLInLiAnt-wgARQSsonm3QeJW1ex0_LE3sEZVo_jTE5kj2gsDSa969RZyUXSMCYii0KSfSXkaHixOwuhiPQR9oCp-U8SnSwWlXBVcAj0TQnb9eHQSXGCfH/s1600-h/Gabriel+Metsu+-+The+Letter-Writer+Surprised++1662.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5333533398202027810" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2lWZal9M6liJeM7F8HRU9nKiLInLiAnt-wgARQSsonm3QeJW1ex0_LE3sEZVo_jTE5kj2gsDSa969RZyUXSMCYii0KSfSXkaHixOwuhiPQR9oCp-U8SnSwWlXBVcAj0TQnb9eHQSXGCfH/s320/Gabriel+Metsu+-+The+Letter-Writer+Surprised++1662.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 271px;" /></a><div>If one found notes of indebtedness, he should not return them neither to the creditor nor to the borrower.</div><div><br /></div><div>If the creditor has the note, he can use the note as evidence that the debt has not yet been paid. If the debtor has the note, he can produce it to prove the debt has been repaid. Thus, if the debtor does not admit to the loan, the note can't be returned.</div><div><br /></div><div>Furthermore, a loan creates a lien on the properties the debtor sells after the loan has been made. Even if the debtor admits to the loan, it can't be returned because the creditor and the debtor may have colluded to defraud the buyers of these properties.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: The Letter-Writer Surprised by Gabriel Metsu</div>

---

Bava Metzia 14 - Power of Attorney (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7JvpyQTtKUx7k2Z8Wq-yVuGg4mTZH8ixIifuz8fWJka0OZ7vHqF2PeLCfiBerfAn8zZiRlUmDM9Y_WlXUAPm2-J2v7sFzrXanmpgFGcfToPBvgnawBJlaMQ13CXt7zetL-vV7fO5vhVp4/s1600-h/Hubert+Salentin+-+Good+News.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5334068324160982674" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7JvpyQTtKUx7k2Z8Wq-yVuGg4mTZH8ixIifuz8fWJka0OZ7vHqF2PeLCfiBerfAn8zZiRlUmDM9Y_WlXUAPm2-J2v7sFzrXanmpgFGcfToPBvgnawBJlaMQ13CXt7zetL-vV7fO5vhVp4/s320/Hubert+Salentin+-+Good+News.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 250px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Suppose Reuven sold a field to Shimon with a guarantee (Reuven agreed to refund Shimon's money if the field is collected by Reuven's creditors). Reuven's creditor comes and attempts to collect the field from Shimon in payment of Reuven's obligation. In that case, the law is that Reuven may go and argue the case with the creditor to prevent him from collecting the field. And the creditor may not tell Reuven, "You have no standing in the matter."<br /><br />But otherwise, anyone who has no standing cannot argue the case in court, and attorney representation is disallowed, and so decides Shulchan Aruch. Other opinions, however, allow power of attorney.<br /><br /><div>Art: Good News by Hubert Salentin</div>

---

Bava Metzia 15 - Repossession of a Stolen Field (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj6ybucMr2aLH54T_QVmylCg0OudNEsnzJ8gMEe6gy78mnif-gkpcy9F0Qmx6dJpAf0DJcmOFEulapPLesEbacgKF9RoXKY02jBMJCnnorspmkRgrjl0bPOTEcyuy6GY-5KR8OFJqNjhm03/s1600-h/Van+Gogh+-+Wheatfield+with+Crows.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5334427709183195890" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj6ybucMr2aLH54T_QVmylCg0OudNEsnzJ8gMEe6gy78mnif-gkpcy9F0Qmx6dJpAf0DJcmOFEulapPLesEbacgKF9RoXKY02jBMJCnnorspmkRgrjl0bPOTEcyuy6GY-5KR8OFJqNjhm03/s320/Van+Gogh+-+Wheatfield+with+Crows.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 152px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If one sells a field to his fellow and it is discovered that the field was not his to sell – that the seller had stolen the field – and the rightful owner repossesses the field, the defrauded seller has the right to obtain compensation for his money by suing the seller.<br /><br />However, he has no right to the value of the improvement to the land, such as a crop or a house. Since the field was never his, the purchase money is considered a loan. The payment for improvement looks like interest, which is forbidden – so says Shmuel. The accepted ruling is that the purchaser has the right to improvements.<br /><br />Art: Wheatfield with Crows by Van Gogh

---

Bava Metzia 16 - When the Found Loan Document IS Returned (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDKVqUZsSr63Xq1m6tobIPUWrkekgA6j9NcUX04kn67OfeCh_Sm_nQUUDKIl7WiWmsHJ8AerNQH-j9EdTf6hkZfh2LJpphLBh5jQThUKI7oRA2qL2HAnUE3ljd-MF4sXnblgdS1uhkAGmB/s1600-h/Edwart+Collier+-+Letter+rack+with+documents+and+miniature+of+Charles+I.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5334637814123157858" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDKVqUZsSr63Xq1m6tobIPUWrkekgA6j9NcUX04kn67OfeCh_Sm_nQUUDKIl7WiWmsHJ8AerNQH-j9EdTf6hkZfh2LJpphLBh5jQThUKI7oRA2qL2HAnUE3ljd-MF4sXnblgdS1uhkAGmB/s320/Edwart+Collier+-+Letter+rack+with+documents+and+miniature+of+Charles+I.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 231px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one finds a certified loan document in court, he should return it to the creditor. Usually, it is the creditor who certifies the note. If the borrower had repaid the money, he should have ripped the document right there, and if he didn't, he brought undue loss to himself.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br />
</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">According to the letter of the law, the land, once repossessed, need not be returned to the debtor when he wants to repay his loan. And it is only because of "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/6-18.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">You shall do that which is fair and good in the eyes of God</span></a>"&nbsp;<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">that the Sages said the land must be returned.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br />
</span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;Letter rack with documents and miniature of Charles I -Edward Collier</span></div>

Bava Metzia 17 - One is not Believed About his Debt (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj027pi-esl3drh0V8g6SqG-IDAYVQk_8_aydQ9X0AriPfmtCdlBSM1CbhpQ5MW0dg7IEg-TrgKKnfdQwibd9v-CtYm693bUNDyhmA8_m732-DndwlUcQwXeHoJj1IfucQWlJ-A_V2sFxz6/s1600-h/Jean+Hippolyte+Flandrin+-+Double+Portrait+of+the+d%27Assy+Brothers.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5335016510115618914" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj027pi-esl3drh0V8g6SqG-IDAYVQk_8_aydQ9X0AriPfmtCdlBSM1CbhpQ5MW0dg7IEg-TrgKKnfdQwibd9v-CtYm693bUNDyhmA8_m732-DndwlUcQwXeHoJj1IfucQWlJ-A_V2sFxz6/s320/Jean+Hippolyte+Flandrin+-+Double+Portrait+of+the+d%27Assy+Brothers.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 223px;" /></a><div>If a creditor tells his debtor, "You owe me a maneh (100 zuz, $5000), and the debtor says, "I owe you nothing because I never borrowed," and witnesses testify against the debtor that he did borrow, and subsequently the debtor said, "I paid this debt" - he is presumed a liar about that money, and&nbsp;without providing witnesses&nbsp;he is not believed that he repaid.</div><div><br /></div><div>A monetary obligation imposed by the court, such as Ketubah, has the strength of a document, and without witnesses, one is not believed to claim that he repaid it.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Double Portrait of the d'Assy Brothers by Jean Hippolyte Flandrin</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/18.txt
<a id="src-00430"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/18.txt`

Bava Metzia 18 - One Found Bills of Divorce, Sickbed Will, Etc. (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgzs41lMyYxBzAilYVMKVjyx2OOHtEM0yxQhj3OjjOHTVcv9RL_ZgBelYwWFyPF25q3K50XrhPa2llH9EIjxpFXgvOOPPAu5M3U249WczUIiK8qUNxuuyJ1r6MvZadLpvYQFroX-wT_bxGG/s1600-h/Carl+Wilhelm+Holsoe+-+Asleep.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5335373050051447234" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgzs41lMyYxBzAilYVMKVjyx2OOHtEM0yxQhj3OjjOHTVcv9RL_ZgBelYwWFyPF25q3K50XrhPa2llH9EIjxpFXgvOOPPAu5M3U249WczUIiK8qUNxuuyJ1r6MvZadLpvYQFroX-wT_bxGG/s320/Carl+Wilhelm+Holsoe+-+Asleep.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 283px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If one found bills of divorce, bills of emancipation of slaves, sickbed wills, gift documents, or receipts – he should not return them to the recipients named on them. It is possible that they were written with the intent to give them, but the author reconsidered and decided not to give them, and it was he who lost them. The above documents effect the transaction; thus, if the writer lost them, they don't take effect.</div><div><br /></div><div>Wills are generally not effective in Torah law; unless a formal gift has been made before death, the property passes automatically to the rightful heirs defined by the Torah. Sickbed will is an exception.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Asleep by Carl Wilhelm Holsoe</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/19.txt
<a id="src-00431"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/19.txt`

Bava Metzia 19 - How to Write a Will under the Torah Law (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgHQwkfKMdra3KS-tuasAkr86geeJ4GG1-vCvEXw27IPOPQ3-1YlTmbAo6k7Cgg9PzJBdRNjBN6fcsRYY0rN5MA9rnhqyEgyoNhUactyNtzIxFMqMYJeuVwUbbjcbEw6dPFJWubiQG5feLq/s1600-h/Sir+William+Orpen+-+A+Bloomsbury+Family.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5335788821813682498" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgHQwkfKMdra3KS-tuasAkr86geeJ4GG1-vCvEXw27IPOPQ3-1YlTmbAo6k7Cgg9PzJBdRNjBN6fcsRYY0rN5MA9rnhqyEgyoNhUactyNtzIxFMqMYJeuVwUbbjcbEw6dPFJWubiQG5feLq/s320/Sir+William+Orpen+-+A+Bloomsbury+Family.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 311px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Under Torah law, wills are invalid because all property passes to a person's natural heirs upon his or her death. One possible correct way is&nbsp;to stipulate that the gift takes effect "from today and after death."<div><br /></div><div>Under this clause, the gift is granted to its beneficiary in two stages: the property itself is given immediately, and the benefactor relinquishes his right to transfer it to anyone else. However, the right to the property's yield (i.e., including such things as produce and rental income) is not granted to the beneficiary until the benefactor's death. Thus, the benefactor continues to use his property for the remainder of his life.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: A Bloomsbury Family by Sir William Orpen</div>

---

<a id="src-00432"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/2.txt`

Bava Metzia 2 - Two People Found a Garment (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGkVdH5TubXpit8QN_yuRWTO1QckPB7cQrBKD9gqXjs5Wc2XqfX5XsVd3Rdm-b0Kdx6ql7j8FuyQi46g5YXsYeUslzSDprNkryLyIa3Chfcx_oY6vV0c5dY5fnmsc9nkZJMiHWPEz3l_OV/s1600-h/Basil+Woodhouse+-+Pulling+the+Favourite,+cartoon+from+Tatler+magazine,+1st+December+1909.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5329432337814312530" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGkVdH5TubXpit8QN_yuRWTO1QckPB7cQrBKD9gqXjs5Wc2XqfX5XsVd3Rdm-b0Kdx6ql7j8FuyQi46g5YXsYeUslzSDprNkryLyIa3Chfcx_oY6vV0c5dY5fnmsc9nkZJMiHWPEz3l_OV/s320/Basil+Woodhouse+-+Pulling+the+Favourite,+cartoon+from+Tatler+magazine,+1st+December+1909.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 214px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>Two litigants come before the court, holding onto a cloak. One says, "I found it first," and the other says, "I found it first." One says, "It is mine," and the other says, "It is mine." One must swear that he owns no less than half of it, and the other one must swear that he owns no less than half of it, and they then divide it - if possible, or sell it and divide the money.</div><div><br /></div><div>
</div><div>Why claim "It is mine?" It's another case where they both gave money to the storekeeper and now argue about whose the article is.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Pulling the Favourite - cartoon from Tatler magazine, by Basil Woodhouse</div>

Bava Metzia 20 - The Found Documents That Are Returned (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEglRDzZKVk1auflebN4csRqTGucBdDupipfRInUXyz5960aJch_FwS6GKUSDrFJEUaihIeYXudFf5p04P_92AHY_5phMq-Bo8E19Rso753ZT8WNwW9frM2yMbWpz4_BfWMZlS8A6PESpSJV/s1600-h/James+de+Vine+Aylward+-+A+Difficult+Letter.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5336116385252084130" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEglRDzZKVk1auflebN4csRqTGucBdDupipfRInUXyz5960aJch_FwS6GKUSDrFJEUaihIeYXudFf5p04P_92AHY_5phMq-Bo8E19Rso753ZT8WNwW9frM2yMbWpz4_BfWMZlS8A6PESpSJV/s320/James+de+Vine+Aylward+-+A+Difficult+Letter.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 250px;" /></a><div>Suppose one found letters of assignment (an official letter stating that property was assessed and confiscated to satisfy a debt), notes of sustenance (certifying that a husband has agreed to provide for his stepdaughter's support), certificates of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halitza">Halitza</a> or any act of the court. In that case, he should return these to the party named in them to receive the document.</div><div><br /></div><div>There is no concern here that the documents were written in advance because the courts do not draw documents in advance.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>If one found a loan document belonging to others among his papers, it should be set aside until Elijah the Prophet comes and resolves its ownership.<span class="Apple-tab-span" style="white-space: pre;"> </span></div><div><br /></div><div>Art: A Difficult Letter by James de Vine Aylward</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/21.txt
<a id="src-00434"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/21.txt`

Bava Metzia 21 - Lost Objects that the Finder May Keep (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwhZAAijJOl7_v9zQmqzIIv95x5ho5ojiIw3U1AGgRkVNUQJ7u3kYHpA5MI2oabFNNviwbmud0Fa5hFkHjWp5oCH79Ns-Lv5n8WjzVMqpeeX3APj-UZ72y0vv81TXODTpqOLjgMm0cfyco/s1600-h/Jean-Francois-Raffaelli+-+Lhomme+Aux+Deux+Pains.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5336656251642143458" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwhZAAijJOl7_v9zQmqzIIv95x5ho5ojiIw3U1AGgRkVNUQJ7u3kYHpA5MI2oabFNNviwbmud0Fa5hFkHjWp5oCH79Ns-Lv5n8WjzVMqpeeX3APj-UZ72y0vv81TXODTpqOLjgMm0cfyco/s320/Jean-Francois-Raffaelli+-+Lhomme+Aux+Deux+Pains.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 214px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">When an object without an identifying mark is lost, the owner despairs recovering it because he knows that even if it is found, he will be unable to prove it is his.  Therefore, the following objects belong to the finder: scattered produce, scattered coins, small sheaves in the public domain, round cakes of pressed figs, and baker's loaves.<br />
<br />
When someone loses such an object, but before he discovers his loss - Rava says that the thing is already abandoned, but Abaye disagrees. The law in this case follows Abaye: until the owner has consciously despaired of recovering the lost object, the finder is not permitted to keep it.<br />
<br />
This is the "Y" in the six cases abbreviated <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/05/bava-metzia-21-lost-objects-that-finder.html">Y</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">A</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/04/eruvin-15-abaye-wins.html">L</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/11/kiddushin-51-should-betrothal-allow.html">K</a> G <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">M</a>, where the law follows Abaye against Rava.<br />
</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;Jean-Francois-Raffaelli - Lhomme Aux Deux Pains</span></div>

---

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/22.txt`

Bava Metzia 22 - Despair without being Aware (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTC_bC3O1ElTDIszu5-hLfvYA3eFCiIN0zMmUZu4O5xeJFCRxsrfgNQRUL7TAWNy4r6zS9qjw-IqOb6XeD2J4yDQ0dsX7JAGqZnyjOQ6LJ00wm9krSl5UcnReuHxpZeWRlFx6vQV6_AkER/s1600-h/Marcus+Stone+-+Stealing+the+Key.jpeg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5336818296453427954" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTC_bC3O1ElTDIszu5-hLfvYA3eFCiIN0zMmUZu4O5xeJFCRxsrfgNQRUL7TAWNy4r6zS9qjw-IqOb6XeD2J4yDQ0dsX7JAGqZnyjOQ6LJ00wm9krSl5UcnReuHxpZeWRlFx6vQV6_AkER/s320/Marcus+Stone+-+Stealing+the+Key.jpeg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 222px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Consider the ruling: "If a  thief, who takes in secret, stole from one and gave to the other, the recipient may keep the goods." Similarly, if a robber who robs openly takes from one and delivers to the other, the recipient may keep it again.<br />
<br />
The robber case is understandable - the owner despairs getting his things back, and the recipient thus acquires them. But in the case of a thief, the owner is unaware of his loss! It must be that the despair that will come later is already effective, just like<a href="http://community.livejournal.com/talmud_daily/7057.html"> Rava and not Abaye</a>? No! The "thief" is an armed robber who is like a thief in that he hides – so here, too, the owner despairs.</span><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Stealing the Key by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Marcus Stone</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">
<br />
</span></div>

Bava Metzia 23 - Basic Rules of Lost Objects (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh49Sm_Gf8LTBGgiL4qNLt0D3DcXubG9WeU-dRJX8U-9PXf8ggGJhsXCAHEEkusoE2-Gf_17WQbS8bN5nLnQ8nTVPUusZggQ10Is06AOsGCXbCqFv1bvPnVz03unkkxKZqVmXVlehtshZPQ/s1600-h/Paul+Gauguin+-+Faaturuma-Aka-Melancholy.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5337258859240898578" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh49Sm_Gf8LTBGgiL4qNLt0D3DcXubG9WeU-dRJX8U-9PXf8ggGJhsXCAHEEkusoE2-Gf_17WQbS8bN5nLnQ8nTVPUusZggQ10Is06AOsGCXbCqFv1bvPnVz03unkkxKZqVmXVlehtshZPQ/s320/Paul+Gauguin+-+Faaturuma-Aka-Melancholy.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 222px;" /></a><div>Once the owner has said, "Woe to me for the monetary loss I have sustained," or expressed his belief in the hopelessness of recovering the lost object in any manner, he has given up hope of ever recovering it, and whoever finds it now may keep it.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>If one finds objects with an identifying mark or sign (siman), the finder must announce his find. This sign can be weight, bundle count, or location where it was lost.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>If objects without a sign look like they have been left by the owner, the finder announces them, lest the people who don't observe this law will take them.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Faaturuma-Aka-Melancholy by Paul Gauguin</div>

---

<a id="src-00437"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/24.txt`

Bava Metzia 24 - Going Beyond the Letter of the Law (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_mGmXxtE9rIDPP_gAV3NAH6EL-m2dnjeKf37h-G2791j4ebRwRy9liVkP4XJyIPEcP3QCuAmY1Aqd0lab4uCflmbb6RSGrAfSr9-kJd4fSZBZWKjoySR_dVhvUNLyusUITVZDUhZwmMFS/s1600-h/John+Opie+-+A+gentleman+and+a+miner+with+a+specimen+of+copper+ore.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5337627948886778610" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_mGmXxtE9rIDPP_gAV3NAH6EL-m2dnjeKf37h-G2791j4ebRwRy9liVkP4XJyIPEcP3QCuAmY1Aqd0lab4uCflmbb6RSGrAfSr9-kJd4fSZBZWKjoySR_dVhvUNLyusUITVZDUhZwmMFS/s320/John+Opie+-+A+gentleman+and+a+miner+with+a+specimen+of+copper+ore.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 254px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>Rav Yehudah followed behind the master, Shmuel, in the cereal store market. He asked Shmuel, "If one found a purse here, what is the law?" Shmuel said, "It belongs to the finder." Many people pass by here, and one is likely to take it. Thus, the owner despairs.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>Rav Yehudah continued, "If a Jew comes and gives an identifying mark for it, what is the law?" Shmuel said, "He is obligated to return it." How can both rulings be true? The second statement reflects a moral obligation to go beyond the letter of the law.</div><div><br /></div><div>John Opie - A gentleman and a miner with a specimen of copper ore</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/25.txt
<a id="src-00438"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/25.txt`

Bava Metzia 25 - Found Items One has to Announce (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjGmKJejFCQhyphenhyphen7-PCEQsur-RKPB7RKLjmIBp3VoQ5dhfH5mNd9f6jnvDskCox6IOpBIkhC4pyQtq-64tqzIBtlR3oWAoR33_YbcOzPYKhZYSZbB-cxwtoqghUuCEnWpyXNnLEbzHhFI3y4/s1600-h/Jean-L%C3%A9on+G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me+-+Harem+Women+Feeding+Pigeons+in+a+Courtyard.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5337971177401048258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjGmKJejFCQhyphenhyphen7-PCEQsur-RKPB7RKLjmIBp3VoQ5dhfH5mNd9f6jnvDskCox6IOpBIkhC4pyQtq-64tqzIBtlR3oWAoR33_YbcOzPYKhZYSZbB-cxwtoqghUuCEnWpyXNnLEbzHhFI3y4/s320/Jean-L%C3%A9on+G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me+-+Harem+Women+Feeding+Pigeons+in+a+Courtyard.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 236px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>If one finds items with an identifying mark, he can presume that the owner has not despaired of recovering them; hence, he has to announce the find and return it to the owner. Examples include produce in a container or a container as is, homemade loaves of bread, jugs of wine, and jugs of oil – these used to have individual seals.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>If one found young pigeons tied with a rope behind a wall – which provides partial protection - he should not touch them. Perhaps a person put them there, and if the finder takes them and announces them, the owner may not have signs to claim them.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Harem Women Feeding Pigeons in a Courtyard by Jean-Leon Gerome</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/26.txt
<a id="src-00439"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/26.txt`

Bava Metzia 26 - Objects Lost in a Rental House (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiKbTGb1Nkv9kIK-mTEXeq4vobaisDADEBfieelyR0uXEHPfnEFEiQa1kqCHp6LXUJI_rFq35D7Wf4aWdZro-iSe0IY6h6UzPk4NDR1B3ElHbWClCLygeWZTsUHMOrYtkjYsMAT0o7dvQ7l/s1600-h/Robert+Scott+Tait+-+A+Chelsea+Interior,+1857.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5338350356308730530" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiKbTGb1Nkv9kIK-mTEXeq4vobaisDADEBfieelyR0uXEHPfnEFEiQa1kqCHp6LXUJI_rFq35D7Wf4aWdZro-iSe0IY6h6UzPk4NDR1B3ElHbWClCLygeWZTsUHMOrYtkjYsMAT0o7dvQ7l/s320/Robert+Scott+Tait+-+A+Chelsea+Interior,+1857.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 217px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><div>If one is in the habit of renting his house to others and finds lost objects there, they belong to him. &nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>Typically, they should be returned to the last renter, but here we are dealing with a case of three people renting together. If one of them lost coins and can't find them, he despairs of getting them back. He thinks of the other two: "They probably took the coins and intend to keep them. But if I confront one, he can tell me it was the other, and I can't make him take an oath." Thus, the finder can keep them.</div><div><br /></div></div><div>Art: A Chelsea Interior by Robert Scott Tait</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/27.txt
<a id="src-00440"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/27.txt`

Bava Metzia 27 - Are Identifying Marks Torah Law? (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh_aQ2O63izkQNEMnO55Sd917kzHNkp4ur0E4OByKS1wmlnCEwlzPIeOBpSpe3DOHqanMEVWXn6r1QoMI-6VYn-YYvpGkQ7wjFOFi7CA9zG63nJAwewlWsEjEUhkdJuGJRsW1TindWoTl6J/s1600-h/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+The+Poet%27s+Garden.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5338724273542697650" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh_aQ2O63izkQNEMnO55Sd917kzHNkp4ur0E4OByKS1wmlnCEwlzPIeOBpSpe3DOHqanMEVWXn6r1QoMI-6VYn-YYvpGkQ7wjFOFi7CA9zG63nJAwewlWsEjEUhkdJuGJRsW1TindWoTl6J/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+The+Poet's+Garden.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 262px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>The commandment to return lost objects states, "...<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/22-3.htm">and so shall you do with his garment...and with any lost article</a>..."</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
The garment is already included in "any lost article," so what does it teach? - Just as a garment is unique in that it has identifying marks and claimants (owners), so too, anything that has identifying marks must be announced. However, one is not obligated to return a lost object that the owner has despaired of recovering.&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Do we see from this ruling that identifying marks are from the Torah? No. The ruling might be primarily interested in the second part, the owner's despair, and mention the marks only incidentally.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: The Poet's Garden by Vincent Van Gogh</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/28.txt
<a id="src-00441"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/28.txt`

Bava Metzia 28 - How Lost Objects are Announced (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhtiuocWN5WQW11kv5AMj6yGItmsPOcAMYvDT3NdRYNAVwThTMxqt6lySf3ptjj5Btr1qgmo89dVmtmppg54dAVwcg7cl6-z1_1YD40eaH_PgRDM2ByEFagWQviHRKda3kqQEMWIdyosORS/s1600-h/Walter+Langley+-+Thoughts+Far+Away.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5339249824205779858" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhtiuocWN5WQW11kv5AMj6yGItmsPOcAMYvDT3NdRYNAVwThTMxqt6lySf3ptjj5Btr1qgmo89dVmtmppg54dAVwcg7cl6-z1_1YD40eaH_PgRDM2ByEFagWQviHRKda3kqQEMWIdyosORS/s320/Walter+Langley+-+Thoughts+Far+Away.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 303px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>Where in the Torah do we find the idea of returning lost objects by identifying marks? From: "...<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/22-2.htm">and it (the lost object) will remain with you <span style="font-weight: bold;">until</span> your brother seeks it out</a>...". Since you can't return it <span style="font-weight: bold;">before</span> he asks (seeks) for it, the word "seek" must mean something else – that you must seek out whether he is a liar by using identifying marks.<br />
<br />
Thus, a lost <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Get_%28divorce_document%29">Get</a> can be returned if the owner names a sign, such as a hole next to a specific letter.<br />
<br />
During the Temple times, the finder would announce his find three times, on Passover, Shavuot, and Sukkot, but now it is announced in the neighborhood.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Thoughts Far Away by Walter Langley</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/29.txt
<a id="src-00442"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/29.txt`

Bava Metzia 29 - How to Take Care of Found Objects (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiQ9W6KI5jhnuPV21hPYW14KXgjkSsZMOAKg97PsuJhiEHvcLAbfX1-jqbwgFgPBm1qw-HuMzkJuJeM-ueko5KSFzSJRQ5EUeoK6cNE75SKhXaHLuK6M7IaKAQmr-D9MhotQZbCNvD5VGYj/s1600-h/John+Frederick+Peto+-+Take+Your+Choice+1885.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5339605136427057298" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiQ9W6KI5jhnuPV21hPYW14KXgjkSsZMOAKg97PsuJhiEHvcLAbfX1-jqbwgFgPBm1qw-HuMzkJuJeM-ueko5KSFzSJRQ5EUeoK6cNE75SKhXaHLuK6M7IaKAQmr-D9MhotQZbCNvD5VGYj/s320/John+Frederick+Peto+-+Take+Your+Choice+1885.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 210px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>One who finds a lost object is not required to bear the expense of maintaining it until the owner reclaims it. For example, a rooster or calf needs to be fed but can not do anything to earn their keep. They should be sold, and the money should be held for the owner. If an animal works and eats, such as an ox or donkey, it should be put to work for twelve months and sold. One may use that money, so if it is lost, he is responsible.<br />
<br />
If one found books (scrolls), he should read from them once in thirty days to air them out and prevent their decay.<br />
<br />Art: Take Your Choice by John Frederick Peto<br />
<br />

---

### content/bava_metzia/3.txt
<a id="src-00443"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/3.txt`

Bava Metzia 3 - Borrower Admits Loan In Part (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiNv26KKLAqQFyWd40tGSQwVi-727rT9nrX0sNqLDh2RBnVLiyh_3utIemorQ0niX8tWa6UEQ2Qhw00rBfal5MPxqCEwZ3lqPoFWFxiqWjdqauRRZLzDUrrCMdetJFq_2kLNV-H7i1LzbXv/s1600-h/Robert+W.+Wright+-+A+Private+Letter,+1879.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5329908526945121314" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiNv26KKLAqQFyWd40tGSQwVi-727rT9nrX0sNqLDh2RBnVLiyh_3utIemorQ0niX8tWa6UEQ2Qhw00rBfal5MPxqCEwZ3lqPoFWFxiqWjdqauRRZLzDUrrCMdetJFq_2kLNV-H7i1LzbXv/s320/Robert+W.+Wright+-+A+Private+Letter,+1879.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 244px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 100%;">If one says, "You owe me $100," and the borrower admits to owing $50, the borrower has to <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-9.htm">repeat his statement under oath</a>&nbsp;and pay $50.&nbsp;</span><div><span style="font-size: 100%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 100%;">There is a presumption that people are not brazen to deny a loan outright since the creditor did them a favor. Likely, the borrower would like to repay but doesn't have the complete amount, so he admits to a part, thinking of repaying the rest later. So, the Torah imposed an oath to force him to tell the truth.

Likewise, if witnesses testified that the borrower owes part of the loan, he has to take an oath for the rest.</span><div><br /></div><div><span style="font-size: 100%;">Art: A Private Letter by Robert W. Wright</span></div></div>

---

Bava Metzia 30 - When One is not Required to Return a Lost Object (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjxzPxWk3nlVS57L1DM_VGcLVMpgwoJad7HblMmElDFfh733oBm7XnwB3yAgADfuOMtYNNWCFUwzMiatUpFmue6R8VMMegOkkbjuvu5pzM5sFDlWEY78VMPA2cXAu9U0RqWXPt0O6bPnyeN/s1600-h/Lauritz+Andersen+Ring+-+Old+man+walking+in+a+rye+field.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5339943955217403538" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjxzPxWk3nlVS57L1DM_VGcLVMpgwoJad7HblMmElDFfh733oBm7XnwB3yAgADfuOMtYNNWCFUwzMiatUpFmue6R8VMMegOkkbjuvu5pzM5sFDlWEY78VMPA2cXAu9U0RqWXPt0O6bPnyeN/s320/Lauritz+Andersen+Ring+-+Old+man+walking+in+a+rye+field.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 255px;" /></a>In the verse "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/22-1.htm">You shall not see the ox of your brother or his sheep wandering and hide from them, rather, you shall return them to your brother</a>," the words "...and hide from them..." can be understood to mean that sometimes you do hide from them. For example, an elderly person is not required to pick up an  object beneath his dignity.<br /><br />Concerning the areas in which Moses should instruct the Jews, the words "...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/18-20.htm">that they shall do</a>..." refer to maintaining a standard of conduct that goes beyond the letter of the law. Said Rabbi Yochanan: "Jerusalem was destroyed only because Jews didn't go beyond the letter of the law."<br /><br /><div>Art: Old man walking in a rye field by Lauritz Andersen Ring</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/31.txt
