**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/31.txt`

Bava Metzia 31 - What is Considered a Lost Object (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiMlkGTBuINzgvzQh7vR7suFwBKppRG2aZzh7sK_aoF8xy0s-Vhe4Sz2UA-pCccciVKFHoZ5plBkEPPxmP5nXJOeSsIP-xjWcaF5SBFZAEbQe74m9RL_VqpeBJ3P76DFDWJr7ks0aWJAO6r/s1600-h/Henry+Weekes+-+Sand+Asses.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5340210731133559698" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiMlkGTBuINzgvzQh7vR7suFwBKppRG2aZzh7sK_aoF8xy0s-Vhe4Sz2UA-pCccciVKFHoZ5plBkEPPxmP5nXJOeSsIP-xjWcaF5SBFZAEbQe74m9RL_VqpeBJ3P76DFDWJr7ks0aWJAO6r/s320/Henry+Weekes+-+Sand+Asses.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 234px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>How is a finder to determine whether the objects he has found are truly lost? If he found a donkey or  a cow grazing by the road, this is not considered a lost object. This is a lost object if he found a donkey with its gear overturned or a cow running through the vineyards.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If one returned an animal and it ran away, and this happened four or five times, he is still obligated to return it yet again because it is stated, "...<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/22-1.htm">return, you shall return them</a>..." For missed work, he gets  compensation only as a laborer. But if he stipulates his wage in court, he can get it.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Sand Asses by Henry Weekes</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/32.txt
<a id="src-00446"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/32.txt`

Bava Metzia 32 - Unloading and Loading (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-ZzoRi9OGwhtG4bDcOqhkpW312oH-owPzOb06kLDwHls4y9292CfHYqz5V1o0VpZ1yt8VRh6JHh7-Fri_I_SWKEXXWH0GrK2Zjjam2uIo6InYXhqns1XNVTjd677eX3f5N4l59Cu1pwHO/s1600-h/Mortimer+Ludington+Menpes+-+Bearing+a+Burden.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5340597424614748386" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-ZzoRi9OGwhtG4bDcOqhkpW312oH-owPzOb06kLDwHls4y9292CfHYqz5V1o0VpZ1yt8VRh6JHh7-Fri_I_SWKEXXWH0GrK2Zjjam2uIo6InYXhqns1XNVTjd677eX3f5N4l59Cu1pwHO/s320/Mortimer+Ludington+Menpes+-+Bearing+a+Burden.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 250px;" /></a><div>If one saw another person's animal lying under its burden, and he unloaded it, allowing it to get up, and then reloaded the load upon it, and then shortly after that, the animal lay down again, he is still obligated to unload or reload as necessary, for it is stated: "...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/23-5.htm">help, you shall help</a>..."</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If the owner impudently walked away and sat down, saying to the bystander, - "Since the commandment to unload my animal is incumbent upon you, if you wish to unload, then unload, but I shall not help you," - the bystander is exempt, for it is stated "...<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/23-5.htm">you shall help with him</a>..."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Bearing a Burden by Mortimer Ludington Menpes</div>
<div>
</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/33.txt
<a id="src-00447"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/33.txt`

Bava Metzia 33 - Suffering of Sentient Beings (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhI2vChdfFB6Vz5cX-pTScNa_bZnhdGKSG5bejDp_fpsXt515paJKPFgDnWH1nBxFdBbvpqbPMOSP-3_K9qNLc6bD0ngl2hD8XzqvCdiNhW2_0hidO3dwbcmydQf8WbJq3g68peaLiHdL9M/s1600-h/Rebrandt+Balaam.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5340983415072990322" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhI2vChdfFB6Vz5cX-pTScNa_bZnhdGKSG5bejDp_fpsXt515paJKPFgDnWH1nBxFdBbvpqbPMOSP-3_K9qNLc6bD0ngl2hD8XzqvCdiNhW2_0hidO3dwbcmydQf8WbJq3g68peaLiHdL9M/s320/Rebrandt+Balaam.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 233px;" /></a><div>One should protect living beings from suffering, as evidenced by <a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/22-32.htm">the angel rebuking Balaam for striking his she-ass</a>.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
But consider this ruling: if one has a choice whether to unload his friend's animal, which is suffering under a load or to load his enemy's – he should load his enemy's in order to subdue his own evil inclination. What about the animal suffering? - Subduing one's evil inclination is more important.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Retrieving his lost article takes precedence over the lost article of his father or his teacher. A lost article of his teacher takes precedence over that of his father unless his father is also a Sage. </div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>Art: Balaam by Rembrandt</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/34.txt
<a id="src-00448"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/34.txt`

Bava Metzia 34 - The Four custodians (Finds)
<span style="font-size: medium;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEitzdlCBHXb2rneW1xLV8r3P0dBQc4Qgu4cZLDvad7zZX-AUic8cH2__AP1V7cnrH5fp6GWu4mJ70_Gj2k_cawd7XWEIiQRXZhDnQ2228jW63rEIAYs-9mpnUNMFLkSmbzB5fstx8VQ25Z3/s1600-h/Andre-Henri-Dargelas+-+Protecting+The+School+Children.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5341856466712620194" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEitzdlCBHXb2rneW1xLV8r3P0dBQc4Qgu4cZLDvad7zZX-AUic8cH2__AP1V7cnrH5fp6GWu4mJ70_Gj2k_cawd7XWEIiQRXZhDnQ2228jW63rEIAYs-9mpnUNMFLkSmbzB5fstx8VQ25Z3/s320/Andre-Henri-Dargelas+-+Protecting+The+School+Children.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 252px;" /></a>The four types of custodians are an unpaid custodian,  a paid custodian, a renter, and a borrower.</span><br />
<ul>
<li><span style="font-size: medium;">The unpaid<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-7.htm">&nbsp;custodian</a> must safeguard the object but not use it and is liable for any loss caused by his negligence;</span></li>
<li><span style="font-size: medium;">The paid custodian also may not use the object, but because he is being paid, he is liable even for theft or loss not due to his negligence;</span></li>
<li><span style="font-size: medium;">The renter pays for the right to use another's property, and his liability is identical to that of the paid custodian;</span></li>
<li><span style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-14.htm">Borrower</a> bears the highest degree of responsibility – he is liable even for mishaps beyond his control, with the exception of work-related damages.</span></li></ul><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Protecting The School Children by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Andre-Henri-Dargelas</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/35.txt
<a id="src-00449"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/35.txt`

Bava Metzia 35 - A Deposit that was Stolen (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgCoHoxdALEF7dST03wGcclDgmwJ8cnsIEktaT_4DzGTOdsrlo0bbPzh1Gy0BnOJE3yTjNrU_quPdmTewWKYYZivvK8DnDiSyl6p-SFbxQXedPKXFVwpumijLeNXRXWEwQYEh3Nwm6pJcd8/s1600-h/Egbert+van+der+Poel+-+Cottage+with+a+Still-Life+of+Kitchen+Utensils.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5341860822094726130" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgCoHoxdALEF7dST03wGcclDgmwJ8cnsIEktaT_4DzGTOdsrlo0bbPzh1Gy0BnOJE3yTjNrU_quPdmTewWKYYZivvK8DnDiSyl6p-SFbxQXedPKXFVwpumijLeNXRXWEwQYEh3Nwm6pJcd8/s320/Egbert+van+der+Poel+-+Cottage+with+a+Still-Life+of+Kitchen+Utensils.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 254px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If one deposits an animal or utensils with another for safekeeping and they were stolen or lost, the custodian can take an oath that he was not negligent and free himself from payment. If he did  not desire to swear and paid, and then the thief is found, the thief pays the double amount to the custodian.<br />
<br />
If one rented a cow and then lent it to another, and it subsequently died a natural death, then the renter is not liable for that, but the borrower is liable to pay the renter. Rabbi Yossi says that the renter needs to return the value of the cow to the owner.<br />
<br /><div>Art: Cottage with a Still-Life of Kitchen Utensils by Egbert van der Poel</div>

---
